Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Effect of 'Thumma' in Conditional Divorce: A Usul Dispute
Analysis of 'thumma' in conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle regarding the word 'thumma' in suspended divorce statements and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
'Thumma' does not break speech connection; the Sahibayn's view prevails over Abu Hanifa's linguistic pause interpretation.

In this passage, we dive into a classic usul al-fiqh dispute over the meaning of the word 'thumma' (then) in conditional divorce statements. The debate turns on whether 'thumma' implies a pause in speech (Abu Hanifa) or merely a sequential order without breaking the connection (Sahibayn). Understanding this dispute is key to mastering how linguistic analysis interacts with legal maxims and common usage in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
Note the two cases presented: condition delayed (saying 'you are divorced' then silent) and condition presented ('if you enter the house, then divorced, then divorced').
These scenarios test the effect of 'thumma' on the attachment of divorces to the condition.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
Abu Hanifa holds that the first divorce is suspended, the second occurs immediately (due to the pause from 'thumma'), and the third is invalid for lack of marital place.
3
Contrast with the Sahibayn's ruling
The Sahibayn hold that all three divorces are suspended on the condition and occur in sequence when the condition is fulfilled.
They view 'thumma' as indicating a continuous sentence with ordered sequence.
4
Analyze the linguistic reasoning
Examine the argument over 'thumma': does it imply a pause in speech (Abu Hanifa) or just a temporal sequence (Sahibayn)?
Later scholars critique Abu Hanifa's interpretation as contrary to common usage.
5
Evaluate the hadith evidence
The hadith 'let him expiate his oath then do what is better' is cited to show 'thumma' indicates sequence without pause, supporting the Sahibayn.
This dalil is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala, but its usage in common speech is considered.
6
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage concludes that the Sahibayn's view is more correct, as stated by al-Muslim and al-Sunbuli.
The mufta bihi position today follows the Sahibayn.

بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث بحث "ثم " قال: "أنت طالق" وسكت على هذا القدر، فوقع هذا الطلاق ولم يبق محلاً لما بعده؛ لأنها غير موطوءة فيلغو، وهذا إذا أخر الشرط. فلا عدة لها ولو قدم الشرط بأن قال: "إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق ثم طالق ثم طالق" تعلق الأول به ووقع الثاني ولغا الثالث؛ لأن الأول متصل بالشرط فلا بد أن يكون معلقا به، ثم لما سكت وقال: "طالق" وقع هذا الثاني في الحال، ثم لما قال: "طالق" لغا هذا الثالث؛ لعدم المحل، وفائدة تعلق الأول: أنه إن ملكها ثانيًا بالنكاح ووجد الشرط يقع الطلاق حينئذ بالتعليق السابق، ولا يقال: إذا كان التراخي في التكلم بقي قوله: "طالق" بلا مبتدأ، فكيف يقع؛ لأنا نقول : يضمر المبتدأ بدلالة العطف؛ لأنه ضروري، فكأنه قال: ثم أنت طالق، بخلاف الشرط، فإنه زائد لا يحتاج إلى تقديره. وقالا : الطلاق الثاني فوقع هذا الطلاق أي في الحال لعدم تعلقه بالشرط لوجود السكوت الفاصل. (القمر) فيلغو: أي ما بعد الأول وهو الثاني والثالث (القمر) وقع هذا الثاني إلخ لوجود المحل، فإن الطلاق الأول لم يقع في الحال. (القمر) لعدم المحل لأنها بانت بالطلاق الثاني بلا عدة. (القمر) وفائدة تعلق إلخ جواب سؤال تقريره: أنه ينبغي أن يلغو الأول أيضًا؛ لأن غير الموطوءة بانت بواحدة بلا عدة فلا فائدة في بقاء الأول معلقا بالشرط لعدم المحل حينئذ؟ (القمر) بخلاف الشرط إلخ: دفع دخل تقريره : أنه لم لا يقدر الشرط حتى يتعلق الثاني والثالث به كتعلق الأول به؟.(القمر) تقديره فيقع في الحال ولا يعلق بالشرط المحشي وقالا إلخ : قلت : قال صاحب "المسلم": وقولهما أشبه، وقال مولانا عبد العلي صاحب مطلع الأسرار الإلهية في شرح المنار : بأن التراخي في التكلم إن كان فإما أن يكون مفاد كلمة "ثم " وهو بديهي البطلان، فإنه لا دلالة له إلا على التراخي إما أنه في التكلم فلا يفهم، وإما أن يكون لازما له لزوما خارجيًا وهو أيضًا باطل؛ لأن الوصل موجود بالضرورة، وإما أن يكون لازماً ذهنيًا عرفيًا أو عقليًا فذلك أيضًا باطل؛ فإنا نسمع كلمة "ثم" ونفهم مدلوله ولا يخطر بالبال التراخي في التكلم أصلا، وإما أن يكون لازماً شرعيًا بأن جعل الشارع هذا الوصل كلا وصل ورتب عليه أحكام التراخي فلابد من إبانته بدليل صاف عن غوائل الشبهات هذا انتهى كلامه، فثبت بهذا ضعف كلام الإمام وما بين العلماء من توجيهات كلامه بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث بحث "ثم" يتعلقن جميعًا وينزلن على الترتيب؛ لأن الوصل في التكلم متحقق عندهما ولا فصل في العبارة، فيتعلق الكل بالشرط سواء قدم الشرط أو أخر، ولكن في وقت الوقوع ينزلن على الترتيب، فإن كانت مدخولاً بها يقع الثلاث، وإن لم تكن مدخولاً بها يقع الأول وبانت به ولا يقع الثاني والثالث، وأما عند أبي حنيفة رحله فإن كانت غير مدخول بها فقد علمت حالها، وإن كانت مدخولاً بها، فإن قدم الجزاء يقع الأول والثاني في الحال وتعلق الثالث بالشرط، فكأنه سكت على الأولين، ثم قال: "أنتِ طالق إن دخلت الدار"، وإن قدم الشرط تعلق الأول بالشرط ووقع الثاني والثالث في الحال؛ لما قلنا هكذا قيل. وفي قوله عليه السلام : "فليكفر عن يمينه ثم ليأت بالذي هو خير" بيان لمجاز كلمة "ثم" بعد بيان حقيقتها، فهو أيضًا لا يخلو من ضعف ووهن مثلاً قالوا: إن الإمام إنما أهدر الاتصال التكلمي قولاً بكمال التراخي، وهذا غير وافٍ فإن هذا النحو من الكمال أي جعل الموجود الثابت هدرًا لا يساعده العرف في كلمة "ثم"، ووجه صدر الشريعة بأن الإمام إنما قال ذلك؛ لئلا يتراخى حكم الإنشاء عنه، والأصل عدم التراخي، وهذا أيضًا غير واف؛ لأن كلمة "ثم " مانعة عن الوصل في الحكم كما يكون الشرط مانعا وحاكم بعضهم بأنه على تقدير جواز تخصيص العلة يتم هذا بإبداء المانع وإما على تقدير جواز تخصيص العلة فلا بد من هذا القول أي التراخي في التكلم لأنه لو تراخى الحكم فقط عن التكلم به لزم تخصيص العلة وهو التكلم. قال صاحب "مطلع الأسرار الإلهية" في بعض كتبه أنه إن سلم بطلان تخصيص العلة، فلا يتم أيضًا، فإنا لا نسلم أن الإنشاء علة لوجود الحكم بالفعل، بل على حسب اقتضاءه، فأنت طالق؛ إذ معناه طالق في الحال صار سببًا لوقوع الطلاق في الحال، وإذا زيد عند الدخول صار علة للوقوع عنده فيجوز أن يكون إذا زيد كلمة "ثم" يكون سببًا للوقوع متراخيا عن الأول، وقيل في توجيه كلام الإمام أقوال أخر لا نطيل الكلام بذكرها. (السنبلي) يتعلقن أي الطلقات الثلاث بالشرط، وقال في "المسلم": إن قول الصاحبين أشبه بالصواب. (القمر) وبانت به أي بانت المرأة بالأول بلا عدة؛ لأنها غير مدخولة. (القمر) يقع الأول والثاني في الحال لأن المرأة المدخول بها محل لهما.(القمر) لما قلنا من أنه وقع السكوت على الأول، ثم وقع التكلم بالآخرين وهي محل للطلاقين الآخرين.(القمر) يمينه: المراد به المحلوف عليه كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَجْعَلُوا اللَّهَ عُرْضَةً لِأَيْمَانِكُمْ ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٢٤)
Explanation of the divisions of the third division. Discussion of 'thumma'. He said: 'You are divorced' and was silent to this extent, so this divorce occurred and no place remained for what follows; because she is not one who has been touched, so it is invalid, and this is when he delayed the condition. So she has no waiting period. If he presented the condition by saying: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, then divorced, then divorced', the first is attached to it, the second occurs, and the third is invalid; because the first is connected to the condition so it must be suspended on it, then when he was silent and said 'divorced', this second occurred immediately, then when he said 'divorced', this third is invalid due to the lack of place. The benefit of the attachment of the first is that if he marries her a second time and the condition occurs, the divorce occurs then by the previous suspension. And it is not said: if the delay in speech remained, his saying 'divorced' would be without a subject, so how does it occur? For we say: the subject is implied by the indication of the conjunction because it is necessary, so it is as if he said: 'then you are divorced', unlike the condition, for it is extra and does not need to be estimated. And they (the two companions) said: the second divorce occurs immediately because it is not attached to the condition due to the existence of the separating silence. (al-Qamar) 'is invalid' means what comes after the first, i.e., the second and third. (al-Qamar) 'this second occurs' etc. due to the existence of a place, for the first divorce did not occur immediately. (al-Qamar) 'due to the lack of place' because she became separated by the second divorce without waiting period. (al-Qamar) 'The benefit of the attachment' etc. is an answer to a question whose premise is: it should be that the first is also invalid, because the non-touched woman becomes separated by one divorce without waiting period, so there is no benefit in the first remaining suspended on the condition due to lack of place then? (al-Qamar) 'unlike the condition' etc. is a rebuttal of an objection whose premise is: why is the condition not estimated so that the second and third are attached to it like the first? (al-Qamar) 'its estimation' occurs immediately and is not attached to the condition. And they said etc.: I said: the author of 'al-Muslim' said: their statement is more appropriate. And our master Abd al-Ali, author of 'Matla' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya' in Sharh al-Manar: that if delay in speech is [the meaning], then either it is the purport of the word 'thumma' and that is obviously false, for it only indicates delay, either in speech which is not understood, or it is an external necessary concomitant and that is also false because the connection exists necessarily, or it is a customary or rational mental concomitant and that is also false; for we hear the word 'thumma' and understand its meaning and no delay in speech comes to mind at all, or it is a legal necessary concomitant by the Lawgiver making this connection as no connection and attaching the rulings of delay to it, then it must be clarified by a proof free from the snares of doubts. This ends his speech. So by this the weakness of Imam Abu Hanifa's statement and the scholars' interpretations of it is established. Explanation of the divisions of the third division. Discussion of 'thumma'. All three are suspended and descend in order; because the connection in speech is realized according to them and there is no separation in the utterance, so all are attached to the condition, whether he presents the condition or delays, but at the time of occurrence they descend in order. If she is one who has been touched, the three occur; if she is not one who has been touched, the first occurs and she becomes separated by it, and the second and third do not occur. And according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), if she is not one who has been touched, you already know her case. If she is one who has been touched, then if he presents the consequence, the first and second occur immediately and the third is suspended on the condition, as if he was silent on the first two and then said: 'You are divorced if you enter the house'. If he presents the condition, the first is attached to the condition and the second and third occur immediately, for what we said, thus it is said. And in his statement (peace be upon him): 'let him expiate for his oath then do what is better' is an explanation of the metaphorical use of the word 'thumma' after explaining its literal meaning. This is also not free from weakness and feebleness. For example, they said: Imam Abu Hanifa only disregarded the speech connection claiming complete delay, and this is insufficient, for this kind of completeness, i.e., making the existing and established thing disregarded, is not supported by common usage regarding the word 'thumma'. Sadr al-Sharia interpreted that Imam only said that so that the ruling of the construction is not delayed from it, and the principle is no delay, and this is also insufficient, because the word 'thumma' prevents connection in ruling just as the condition is a preventer. And some ruled that on the assumption that the particularization of the cause is permissible, this is complete by showing the preventer, but on the assumption that the particularization of the cause is permissible, this statement (i.e., delay in speech) is necessary, because if the ruling alone is delayed from the speech, it would entail particularization of the cause which is the speech. The author of 'Matla' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya' said in some of his books that if the invalidity of particularization of the cause is conceded, it is also not complete, for we do not concede that the construction is a cause for the existence of the ruling in actuality, but rather according to its requirement. So 'You are divorced' means divorced immediately, it became a cause for the occurrence of divorce immediately, and when 'upon entry' is added, it becomes a cause for occurrence at that time, so it is permissible that when the word 'thumma' is added, it becomes a cause for occurrence delayed from the first. And other statements were made in interpreting Imam's words, which we do not lengthen the speech by mentioning them. (al-Sunbuli) 'they are suspended' means the three divorces are suspended on the condition. And it is said in 'al-Muslim': the statement of the two companions is more correct. (al-Qamar) 'and she becomes separated by it' means the woman becomes separated by the first without waiting period because she is not touched. (al-Qamar) 'the first and second occur immediately' because the woman who has been touched is a place for both. (al-Qamar) 'for what we said' that there was a silence on the first, then speech occurred with the others, and she is a place for the other two divorces. (al-Qamar) 'his oath' means the thing sworn by, as in His statement: 'And do not make Allah an obstacle to your oaths' (al-Baqarah 2:224).
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the legal effect of the word 'thumma' (then) when used between statements of divorce in a conditional formula. The author begins by presenting the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa (rahimahullah) in two scenarios: (1) when the condition is delayed (e.g., saying 'You are divorced' and then being silent, then later stating the condition), and (2) when the condition is presented first (e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, then divorced, then divorced'). In both cases, Abu Hanifa holds that the first divorce is suspended on the condition, the second occurs immediately (because the pause after 'thumma' indicates a break in speech), and the third is invalid because the woman has already become separated by the second divorce. The passage then presents the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), which is that all three statements are suspended on the condition and occur in sequence when the condition is fulfilled. The rationale is that 'thumma' does not indicate a pause in speech but rather a sequential connection, so all parts remain linked. The text then critiques Imam Abu Hanifa's position, citing later scholars such as al-Sunbuli, Sahib al-Muslim, and Mawlana Abd al-Ali, who argue that common usage of 'thumma' does not imply a break in speech but rather a natural order. The hadith 'let him expiate his oath then (thumma) do what is better' is cited as evidence for the metaphorical use of 'thumma' to indicate sequence without a speech pause. The passage ends with further criticisms and the conclusion that the Sahibayn's view is more correct (as stated in al-Muslim and by al-Sunbuli).

Key Terms
ثم (thumma): A particle indicating sequence and delay; in this context, it is discussed whether it implies a pause in speech (Abu Hanifa) or merely an ordered sequence (Sahibayn).
سكوت (sukut): Silence or pause in speech; Abu Hanifa interprets 'thumma' as causing a pause, breaking the connection between the condition and later divorce statements.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension of a legal ruling (e.g., divorce) on the occurrence of a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, if a man says to his non-touched wife 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, then divorced, then divorced', how many divorces occur immediately?
A) None; all are suspended on the condition.
B) The first occurs immediately; the second and third are suspended.
C) The second occurs immediately; the first and third are suspended.
D) All three occur immediately.

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn's interpretation of 'thumma' as a sequential connector without speech pause is the stronger position in Hanafi usul and is the operative rule for fatwa.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
The Effect of 'Thumma' in Conditional Divorce: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on 'thumma' in conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the effect of 'thumma' in conditional divorce, and evaluate the usul arguments regarding causality and linguistic breaks.

Core Idea
The word 'thumma' creates a break in speech but not necessarily in legal effect — the Sahibayn's view that all divorces suspend sequentially prevails.

This passage from Noor al-Anwaar presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about the conjunction 'thumma' (then) in a conditional divorce statement. While the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that all three divorces are suspended on the condition and occur sequentially upon fulfillment, Abu Hanifa distinguishes based on the order of the statement and the wife's status. The discussion then probes deeper into whether 'thumma' prevents immediate legal causation, touching on usul principles about causality in speech. This lesson will guide you through both the fiqh ruling and the underlying usul reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Understand the conditional divorce statement: 'You are divorced, then you are divorced, then you are divorced, if you enter the house.' Note the distinction between consummated and non-consummated wife.
The condition 'if you enter' makes the divorces suspended.
2
State the Sahibayn's position
They hold all three divorces are suspended and occur in order upon condition fulfillment. If non-consummated, only one occurs. Their rationale: 'thumma' indicates a complete break in speech.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
For a consummated wife, the order of statement affects which divorces occur immediately. If divorces precede condition, first two occur immediately, third is suspended. If condition precedes, first is suspended, last two occur immediately. His rationale: 'thumma' can be rhetorical; immediate effect principle prevails.
This view is specific to a consummated wife.
4
Analyze the usul critique
The passage critiques Abu Hanifa's view through arguments about the hadith on expiation and whether speech is a cause (illa) for the ruling. Understand the debate on talfiq al-illa and taksis al-illa.
The critique centers on whether 'thumma' prevents legal connection.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The marginal note from al-Sanbali confirms that the Sahibayn's view is more correct (ashabah bi al-sawab). The practical outcome: all divorces are suspended, none occur immediately.
This is the relied-upon view for fatwa.

Source Text

يتعلقن جميعًا وينزلن على الترتيب؛ لأن الوصل في التكلم متحقق عندهما ولا فصل في العبارة، فيتعلق الكل بالشرط سواء قدم الشرط أو أخر، ولكن في وقت الوقوع ينزلن على الترتيب، فإن كانت مدخولاً بها يقع الثلاث، وإن لم تكن مدخولاً بها يقع الأول وبانت به ولا يقع الثاني والثالث، وأما عند أبي حنيفة رحله فإن كانت غير مدخول بها فقد علمت حالها، وإن كانت مدخولاً بها، فإن قدم الجزاء يقع الأول والثاني في الحال وتعلق الثالث بالشرط، فكأنه سكت على الأولين، ثم قال: 'أنتِ طالق إن دخلت الدار'، وإن قدم الشرط تعلق الأول بالشرط ووقع الثاني والثالث في الحال؛ لما قلنا هكذا قيل. وفي قوله عليه: 'فليكفر عن يمينه ثم ليأت بالذي هو خير' بيان لمجاز كلمة 'ثم' بعد بيان حقيقتها، فهو أيضًا لا يخلو من ضعف ووهن مثلاً قالوا: إن الإمام إنما أهدر الاتصال التكلمي قولاً بكمال التراخي، وهذا غير وافٍ فإن هذا النحو من الكمال أي جعل الموجود الثابت هدرًا لا يساعده العرف في كلمة 'ثم'، ووجه صدر الشريعة بأن الإمام إنما قال ذلك؛ لئلا يتراخى حكم الإنشاء عنه، والأصل عدم التراخي، وهذا أيضًا غير واف؛ لأن كلمة 'ثم' مانعة عن الوصل في الحكم كما يكون الشرط مانعا وحاكم بعضهم بأنه على تقدير جواز تخصيص العلة يتم هذا بإبداء المانع وإما على تقدير جواز تخصيص العلة فلا بد من هذا القول أي التراخي في التكلم لأنه لو تراخى الحكم فقط عن التكلم به لزم تخصيص العلة وهو التكلم. قال صاحب 'مطلع الأسرار الإلهية' في بعض كتبه أنه إن سلم بطلان تخصيص العلة، فلا يتم أيضًا، فإنا لا نسلم أن الإنشاء علة لوجود الحكم بالفعل، بل على حسب اقتضاءه، فأنت طالق؛ إذ معناه طالق في الحال صار سببًا لوقوع الطلاق في الحال، وإذا زيد عند الدخول صار علة للوقوع عنده فيجوز أن يكون إذا زيد كلمة 'ثم' يكون سببًا للوقوع متراخيا عن الأول، وقيل في توجيه كلام الإمام أقوال أخر لا نطيل الكلام بذكرها. (السنبلي) يتعلقن أي الطلقات الثلاث بالشرط، وقال في 'المسلم': إن قول الصاحبين أشبه بالصواب. (القمر) وبيانت به أي بانت المرأة بالأول بلا عدة؛ لأنها غير مدخولة. (القمر) يقع الأول والثاني في الحال لأن المرأة المدخول بها محل لهما. (القمر) لما قلنا من أنه وقع السكوت على الأول، ثم وقع التكلم بالآخرين وهي محل للطلاقين الآخرين. (القمر) يمينه: المراد به المحلوف عليه كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَجْعَلُوا اللَّهَ عُرْضَةً لِأَيْمَانِكُمْ ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٢٤)
They all become suspended and occur in order; because connection in speech is realized according to them (the two companions) and there is no separation in the phrase, so all are suspended by the condition whether the condition is stated before or after, but at the time of occurrence they occur in order. If she has been consummated, all three occur; if she has not been consummated, the first occurs and she becomes separated by it, and the second and third do not occur. According to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, if she is non-consummated, you already know her case; if she is consummated, and he presents the result (the divorces) first, the first and second occur immediately and the third is suspended by the condition, as if he remained silent on the first two and then said: 'You are divorced if you enter the house.' If he presents the condition first, the first is suspended by the condition and the second and third occur immediately; because of what we said it is said. And in his statement, peace be upon him: 'Let him expiate for his oath then let him do that which is better' is an explanation of the metaphorical use of the word 'thumma' after explaining its literal meaning. This too is not free from weakness and frailty. For example, they said: The Imam (Abu Hanifa) only disregarded the sequential connection in speech as a claim of complete separation, and this is insufficient because this type of completeness, i.e., nullifying the existing established, is not supported by custom in the word 'thumma'. Sadr al-Shariah explained that the Imam said this so that the ruling of the utterance should not be delayed from it, and the principle is no delay. This too is insufficient because the word 'thumma' prevents connection in the ruling just as the condition prevents. And some ruled that on the assumption that specification of the cause is permissible, this is complete by presenting the preventer; but on the assumption that specification of the cause is not permissible, then this saying is necessary, i.e., delay in speech, because if only the ruling is delayed from the speech, it would require specification of the cause which is the speech. The author of 'Matla' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya' said in some of his books: If the invalidity of specifying the cause is accepted, it is still not complete, for we do not accept that the utterance is a cause for the existence of the ruling in actual fact, but rather according to its requirement. So 'You are divorced' meaning 'divorced now' becomes a cause for the occurrence of divorce immediately, and when it is increased at the time of entry, it becomes a cause for occurrence at that time. So it is possible that when the word 'thumma' is added, it becomes a cause for occurrence delayed from the first. It was said in explaining the Imam's statement there are other sayings, we will not prolong the speech by mentioning them. (al-Sanbali) They are suspended: meaning the three divorces are suspended by the condition. And it was said in 'al-Muslim': The statement of the two companions is more correct. (al-Qamar) And she becomes separated by it: meaning the woman becomes separated by the first without waiting period because she is non-consummated. (al-Qamar) The first and second occur immediately because the consummated woman is a place for them. (al-Qamar) Because of what we said: that he remained silent on the first, then spoke with the others, and she is a place for the other two divorces. (al-Qamar) His oath: what is meant is the object sworn upon, as in the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And do not make Allah an obstacle in your oaths' (al-Baqarah: 224).
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is an intra-madhhab dispute (khilaf) within the Hanafi school regarding the effect of the word 'thumma' (then) in a conditional divorce statement. The issue: if a man says to his wife 'You are divorced, then you are divorced, then you are divorced, if you enter the house', how do the divorces occur? The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that all three divorces are suspended on the condition and occur in order when the condition is fulfilled. If the wife has not been consummated, only the first divorce takes effect immediately upon condition fulfillment and the rest do not occur, because a non-consummated wife cannot receive multiple divorces in one session. If she is consummated, all three occur sequentially. Abu Hanifa, however, distinguishes based on the order of the statement and the wife's status. If the wife is non-consummated, the ruling is the same. But if she is consummated and the man states the divorces first (the jaza') then says the condition, the first two divorces occur immediately and the third is suspended on the condition. If he states the condition first, then the first divorce is suspended on the condition and the second and third occur immediately. The reasoning is that the word 'thumma' indicates a break in speech but not necessarily a break in the legal effect; Abu Hanifa considers that the two immediate divorces can occur because the wife is capable of receiving them, and the word 'thumma' in this context is like a rhetorical pause. The passage then critiques this view, mentioning that Sadr al-Shariah and others attempted to justify Abu Hanifa's position but found it weak. The marginal note from al-Sanbali confirms that the view of the two companions is more correct according to 'al-Muslim'. The passage also touches on the metaphorical use of 'thumma' in the hadith about oath expiation, indicating that the discussion of 'thumma' has broader implications in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
ثم (thumma): A conjunction meaning 'then' indicating temporal order and separation in speech.
مدخول بها (madkhul biha): A wife who has had actual intercourse with her husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the effect of saying 'You are divorced, then you are divorced, then you are divorced, if you enter the house' to a consummated wife?
A) All three divorces occur immediately upon uttering them.
B) All three divorces are suspended and occur in order upon entry.
C) The first two occur immediately and the third upon entry.
D) The first occurs immediately, the second and third upon entry.

Key Takeaway
The word 'thumma' in conditional divorces indicates a sequential break, preventing simultaneous occurrence, and the Sahibayn's view is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Legal Effect of 'أو' in Dower and Expiation: A Usul Dispute
Usul dispute on particle 'أو' with fiqh application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle regarding the particle 'أو' to distinguish between valid and invalid choice in dower and expiation, and to derive the ruling according to both Hanafi positions.

Core Idea
The legal effect of 'أو' depends on whether the choice provides a genuine benefit; otherwise, the lesser option is obligatory.

The particle 'أو' (or) appears in marriage dower contracts and in Quranic expiation texts. Its interpretation is not uniform: in dower, the Sahibayn distinguish between meaningful and meaningless choice, while Abu Hanifa consistently reverts to mahr al-mithl. In expiation, the Quran uses 'أو' to list alternatives, and the Hanafi school holds that any one suffices. In this lesson, we examine the usul reasoning behind these positions, focusing on the foundational principles of barā'at al-dhimmah (innocence of liability) and the original obligation in marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
State the issue: when a dower is expressed with 'أو' between two amounts or items, does the husband have a valid choice, and what must he give? Recognize the two opposing positions: Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's reasoning
The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the default is barā'at al-dhimmah. If the choice is meaningless (e.g., 1000 or 2000 dirhams), the husband gives the lesser because giving more would exceed what is proven. If the choice is meaningful (different types), he may choose.
They focus on certainty of discharge.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the original obligation in marriage is mahr al-mithl. Deviation to a named dower requires certainty, which 'أو' prevents. Therefore, in all cases with 'أو', mahr al-mithl is due.
He prioritizes the original obligation over nominal options.
4
Apply to examples
Work through the examples: slaves (Sahibayn: lesser value; Abu Hanifa: mahr al-mithl), currency with same type vs. different types (contract must be maintained).
Note the exception when the two currencies differ in attributes (e.g., one prompt, one deferred) – then choice is valid.
5
Extend to expiation
In Quranic expiations (oath, shaving head), 'أو' appears. The Hanafi ruling: the mukhallaf (person) may choose any one option. This is based on the apparent meaning of 'أو' granting choice, and no contrary evidence.
The dalil is Quranic, thubut qati but dalala zanni.

بحث كلمة "أو "
بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث وضرر وعسر ويسر فيصح التخيير، فيعطيها ما شاء، وإن لم يصح التخيير بأن يكون بين القليل والكثير من جنس واحد من النقدين مثلا يقول: "تزوجتك على ألف درهم أو ألفي درهم" يجب الأقل لا محالة؛ إذ لا فائدة للزوج في هذا الاختيار بل نفعه في إعطاء الأقل ألبتة، ولم يعتبر نفعها في قبول الكثير؛ لأن الأصل براءة الذمة، والمال في النكاح ليس أمرًا أصليا حتى تعتبر رعاية الزيادة، وقد فهم من هذا التقرير أن قيد في النقدين اتفاقي؛ لأنه إذا تزوج على هذا العبد أو هذا العبد يجب عندهما العبد الأقل قيمة هكذا قيل، وهذا كله عندهما.
وقالا لها فيعطيها إلخ فيعطي الزوج الزوجة ما شاء؛ لأن موجب "أو " التخيير، وقد أمكن العمل به، فوجب القول به، ثم اعلم أنه إذا تزوج على هذا العبد أو هذا العبد وأحدهما أوكس فالشارح حكم ههنا بأن الزوج فيه مختار عندهما، وسيحكم فيما سيأتي عن قريب أنه يجب فيه عندهما العبد الأقل قيمة وهل هذا إلا تضاد على أن الروايات الفقهية دالة على خلاف ما حكم ههنا في العالمگيرية: لو تزوجها على هذا العبد أو على هذا العبد وأحدهما أوكس حكم مهر مثلها فإن كان مهر مثلها مثل أرفعهما أو أكثر فلها الأرفع لرضاها به وإن كان مثل أو كسهما أو أقل فلها الأوكس لرضاه به وإن كان بينهما فلها مهر مثلها، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة الأوكس في ذلك كله، وعلى هذا الخلاف لو تزوجها على ألف أو ألفين كذا في التبيين. (القمر) وإن لم يصح أي إن لم يفد ثم اعلم أنه لما كان يتوهم من قول المصنف وفي النقدين يجب الأقل أن في النقدين مطلقا يجب الأقل، فإذا قال تزوجتك على ألف درهم أو مائة دينار فينبغي أن يجب الأقل مع أن الأمر ليس كذلك؛ إذ في هذه الصورة يتخير الزوج في أن يعطى أيهما شاء على ما مرّ آنفا دفعه الشارح بهذا القول، وحاصل الدفع: أن المراد من النقدين ليس مطلقا بل النقدان من جنس واحد بحيث لا يكونان مختلفين في الأوصاف كالحلول والأجل أيضًا، فإذا كان الترديد والتخيير بين هذين النقدين فلا فائدة في التخيير، فيجب الأقل لا محالة. (القمر) ولم يعتبر إلخ: دفع دخل تقريره أنه إذا قال: "تزوجتك على ألف درهم أو ألفي درهم" فاعتبرتم نفع الزوج وقلتم بوجوب الأقل ولم يعتبر نفع المرأة حتى يجب الأكثر . (القمر) من هذا التقرير أي وجوب الأقل إذا لم يكن للزوج فائدة في هذا الاختيار. (القمر) من هذا إلخ: أي عدم اعتبار نفع الزوجة في قبول الكثير.(السنبلي)
بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث
التسمية
بحث كلمة "أو "
وعنده يجب مهر المثل في كل من هذه المسائل؛ لأنه هو الموجب الأصلي في النكاح والعدول عنه إلى المسمى إنما يكون عند معلومية التسمية ولم توجد، ولكن في صورة الألف الحالة والألفين النسيئة. إن كان مهر المثل ألفين أو أكثر فالخيار لها، وإن كان أقل من ألف فالخيار للزوج يعطيها أيهما شاء. وفي الكفارة يجب أحد الأشياء عندنا خلافًا للبعض يعني أن في كل كفارة ردد فيها بين الأشياء بكلمة "أو" كما في كفارة اليمين من قوله تعالى: ﴿إِطْعَامُ عَشَرَةِ مَسَاكِينَ مِنْ أَوْسَطِ مَا تُطْعِمُونَ أَهْلِيكُمْ أَوْ كِسْوَتُهُمْ أَوْ تَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ وكما في كفارة حلق الرأس من عذر
(المائدة: (۸۹)
مهر المثل إلخ أي مهر امرأة من قوم أبيها مماثلة لها سناً وجمالاً ومالاً وعقلاً ودينا وبلدا وعصرًا وبكارة وثيابة، فإن لم توجد منهم فمن الأجانب لا مهر أمها وخالتها إلا إذا كانتا من قوم أبيها إلخ من "شرح وقاية" وفي بعض الحواشي : فإن قيل: "إذا تزوجها على ألف درهم أو على ألفين" ينبغي أن يجب الأقل لوضوح أن التخيير من غير تضمن رفق لا يصلح، فينبغي أن يجب الأقل لتيقنه وكون المسمى معلومًا لا مهر المثل، ويجاب بأن الموجب الأصلي في النكاح لمهر المثل، وإنما العدل عنه إلى المسمى وقت التسمية، ولفظ "أو " يمنع التسمية، فوجب المصير إلى الموجب الأصلي في صورة صحة التخيير، فوجب في صورة عدم صحة التخيير أيضًا لعدم القائل بالفصل. (السنبلي) لأنه هو الموجب إلخ فيه كلام لم لا يقولون إن الموجب الأصلي عشرة دراهم مع أن الشارع قدر المهر بها دون مهر المثل كما مرّ إلا أن يقال: إن مهر المثل لما كان واجبًا بنفس العقد على ما مرّ كان هو الموجب الأصلي فتأمل. فالخيار لها إن شاءت أخذت الألف حالة وإن شاءت أخذت الألفين نسيئة؛ لرضاها بالنقصان من مهر المثل، ولا خيار للزوج؛ إذ هي المتبرعة بكل حال على الزوج قدراً أو وصفا. (القمر) وإن كان أقل إلخ: وإن كان مهر المثل أقل من ألفين وأكثر من ألف فلها مهر مثلها. (القمر) فالخيار للزوج لأنه التزم إحدى الزيادتين، فكان له الخيار.(القمر)
أن في كل كفارة إلخ : ومن خصص كصاحب "التنوير" الكفارة في المتن بكفارة اليمين فقد أخطأ. (القمر) من قوله تعالى: ﴿فَكَفَّارَتُهُ أي الفعلة التي تذهب إثم اليمين إِطْعَامُ عَشَرَةِ مَسَاكِينَ مِنْ أَوْسَطِ مَا تُطْعِمُونَ أَهْلِيكُمْ في النوع والقدر وهو نصف صاع عندنا أَوْ كِسْوَتُهُمْ ﴾ (المائدة: ٨٩) عطف على إطعام أو تحرير رقبة. حلق الرأس أي في الإحرام من عذر، قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنْ كَانَ مِنْكُمْ مَرِيضًا مرضًا يحوجه إلى حلق الرأس في الإحرام أَوْ بِهِ أَذىً مِنْ رَأْسِهِ كجراحة وقمل فَفِدْيَةٌ أي فعليه فدية ومِنْ صِيَام ثلاثة أَوْ صَدَقَةٍ على ستة مساكين، لكل مسكين نصف صاع من بر أَوْ نُسُكِ (البقرة : ١٩٦) أي ذبح شاة. (القمر)
Discussion of the word 'aw'. Explanation of the types of the third division: if [the choice] involves harm, hardship, and ease, then the choice is valid, and he gives her whichever he wishes. If the choice is not valid – such as when it is between a small and a large amount of the same type of currency, for example when he says: 'I marry you for one thousand dirhams or two thousand dirhams' – then the lesser is obligatory without exception, because the husband has no benefit in this choice; rather his benefit lies in giving the lesser absolutely, and her benefit in accepting the greater is not considered because the original principle is the innocence of the liability, and wealth in marriage is not an original matter such that consideration of increase would be observed. From this exposition it is understood that the restriction to currencies is incidental; because if he marries on this slave or this slave, according to them (the two) the slave of lesser value becomes obligatory – thus it is said, and all this is according to them. And they (the two) said: 'he gives her' etc. – meaning he (the husband) gives his wife whichever he wishes, because the force of 'aw' is choice, and it is possible to act upon it, so it must be accepted. Then know that if he marries on this slave or this slave and one of them is less in value, the commentator ruled here that the husband has the choice according to them; but later he will rule shortly that the slave of lesser value becomes obligatory. Is this not contradiction? Yet fiqh narrations indicate contrary to what he ruled here. In al-'Alamgiriyya: If he marries her on this slave or on this slave and one is less, the ruling is mahr al-mithl. If mahr al-mithl equals the higher of the two or more, she takes the higher due to her consent; if it equals the lower or less, she takes the lower due to his consent; if it is between them, she takes mahr al-mithl. This according to Abu Hanifa: the lower in all that. And on this disagreement if he marries her on one thousand or two thousand – thus in al-Tabyin. (al-Qamar) 'And if it is not valid' i.e. if it does not benefit [the husband]. Then know that from the author's statement 'and in currencies the lesser is obligatory', one might think that in currencies absolutely the lesser is obligatory; so if he says: 'I marry you for one thousand dirhams or one hundred dinars', it would be incumbent that the lesser is obligatory, but the matter is not so; for in this case the husband chooses whichever he wishes, as passed earlier. The commentator countered this statement, and the gist of the refutation is: what is meant by 'currencies' is not absolute, rather the two currencies are of one kind such that they do not differ in attributes like being on hand and deferred also. If the alternation and choice is between these two currencies, there is no benefit in choice, so the lesser is obligatory inevitably. (al-Qamar) 'And he did not consider' etc.: Refutation of an objection: if he says: 'I marry you for one thousand dirhams or two thousand dirhams', you considered the benefit of the husband and said the lesser is obligatory, and did not consider the benefit of the woman so that the greater would be obligatory. (al-Qamar) 'From this exposition' i.e. the obligation of the lesser when the husband has no benefit in this choice. (al-Qamar) 'From this' etc.: i.e. the non-consideration of the benefit of the wife in accepting the greater. (al-Sunbuli) Explanation of the types of the third division. The naming. Discussion of the word 'aw'. And according to him (Abu Hanifa) mahr al-mithl is obligatory in each of these issues because it is the original obligatory [sum] in marriage, and deviating from it to the named dower only occurs when the naming is known, and it is not found. But in the case of one thousand on hand and two thousand deferred: if mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the choice is hers; if it is less than one thousand, the choice is for the husband – he gives her whichever he wishes. And on expiation, one of the things is obligatory with us, contrary to some others, meaning that in every expiation that alternates between things with the word 'aw', as in the expiation of an oath from His statement: 'Feeding of ten needy persons from the average of what you feed your families or clothing them or freeing a slave' (al-Ma'idah:89) and as in the expiation for shaving the head due to an excuse. (al-Qamar) 'Mahr al-mithl' etc.: i.e. the dower of a woman from her father's people similar to her in age, beauty, wealth, intelligence, religion, country, time, virginity and non-virginity; if not found among them, then from unrelated women – not her mother or aunt unless they are from her father's people – from Sharh al-Wiqayah. And in some marginal notes: If it is said: 'If he marries her for one thousand dirhams or two thousand', it should be that the lesser is obligatory, because clearly a choice that does not include benefit is not valid; so the lesser should be obligatory due to certainty and because the named [dower] is known, not mahr al-mithl. The answer is that the original obligatory in marriage is mahr al-mithl, and deviation from it to the named only occurs at the time of naming, and the word 'aw' prevents naming, so recourse to the original obligatory is necessary in the case where choice is valid; thus it is also necessary in the case where choice is not valid due to the lack of a proponent of distinction. (al-Sunbuli) 'Because it is the obligatory' etc.: There is discussion: why do they not say that the original obligatory is ten dirhams, while the Lawgiver fixed the dower by that, not mahr al-mithl, as passed? Unless it is said that since mahr al-mithl is obligatory by the contract itself, as passed, it is the original obligatory – reflect. Then: The choice is hers: if she wishes, she takes the one thousand on hand, and if she wishes, she takes the two thousand deferred, because she consents to the decrease from mahr al-mithl. The husband has no choice, because she is the one donating in every case to the husband, in amount or description. (al-Qamar) 'And if it is less' etc.: If mahr al-mithl is less than two thousand but more than one thousand, she takes mahr al-mithl. (al-Qamar) Thus the choice is for the husband because he committed to one of the two increases, so he has the choice. (al-Qamar) 'That in every expiation' etc.: Whoever specifies, like the author of al-Tanwir, the expiation in the text as the expiation of an oath, has erred. (al-Qamar) From His statement: 'So its expiation is... feeding ten needy persons from the average of what you feed your families in type and quantity – and it is half a sa' according to us – or clothing them' (al-Ma'idah:89) – it is a conjunctive to feeding, or freeing a slave. 'Shaving the head' i.e. while in ihram due to an excuse. Allah said: 'So whoever among you is sick, a sickness that necessitates shaving the head in ihram, or has an ailment from his head such as a wound or lice, then a ransom: from fasting three [days] or charity to six needy persons, each needy person half a sa' of wheat, or a sacrifice' (al-Baqarah:196) i.e. slaughtering a sheep. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the legal implications of the particle 'أو' (or) in the context of marriage dower (mahr) and expiation (kaffara). It opens by discussing the third division of cases where the dower is stated with 'أو', distinguishing between valid choice (where the options differ beneficially) and invalid choice (where the options are of the same type but different quantities). The primary dispute is between the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn hold that if the choice is meaningful (e.g., different types of items), the husband may give whichever he chooses; if meaningless (e.g., one thousand or two thousand dirhams, same type), the lesser is obligatory because the husband's benefit lies in giving less. They argue that the default is innocence of liability (barā'at al-dhimmah), so the lesser is certain. Abu Hanifa, however, rules that in all cases where the dower is ambiguous due to 'أو', the proper mahr al-mithl (dower of the like) is due, because the original obligation in marriage is mahr al-mithl, and a valid named dower requires certainty which 'أو' prevents. The text then examines exceptions: when the two options differ in attributes (like one on hand and one deferred), the choice is valid and the husband may choose. The discussion extends to expiation (kaffara), where 'أو' appears in the Quranic verses on oath expiation (al-Ma'idah 5:89) and ransom for shaving in ihram (al-Baqarah 2:196). The Hanafi position is that any one of the mentioned options suffices (the mukhayyar is free to choose), contrary to some others who may require a specific order. The passage also includes marginal comments from al-Qamar and al-Sunbuli clarifying points and referencing other works like al-'Alamgiriyya, al-Tabyin, and Sharh al-Wiqayah. Throughout, the reasoning is based on the original principle (al-aṣl) of innocence and the nature of 'أو' as a particle of choice, with the Hanafi school's distinctive methodology of preferring mahr al-mithl when the named dower is uncertain.

Key Terms
أو (aw): A particle of disjunction and choice; in legal contexts, it indicates that the person has the option to choose among the items listed.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of a woman similar to the bride in age, beauty, wealth, intelligence, religion, location, time, virginity, etc., from her father's clan or from unrelated women.
التخيير (al-takhyir): The act of granting choice; in this context, the husband's (or mukhallaf's) right to choose among the stated options.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if a man marries a woman saying, 'I marry you for this slave or this slave,' and one slave is clearly of lesser value, what is the husband required to give?
A) The slave of lesser value
B) The slave of greater value
C) Mahr al-mithl
D) Any slave he chooses

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the particle 'أو' grants a genuine choice only when the options are meaningfully different; otherwise, the lesser or the original obligation (mahr al-mithl) takes effect.

The Particle 'Ba' in Oath Exceptions: Repetition of Permission
Textual analysis of particle 'ba' in oath exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul analysis to distinguish between two oath formulations and derive the ruling on whether permission must be repeated.

Core Idea
The presence of 'ba' requires repeated permission; its absence allows one permission to suffice.

The particle 'ba' may seem minor, but in oath exceptions it determines whether each exit requires separate permission or one permission covers all. This passage shows how Hanafi usul uses literal meanings and metaphors to derive precise rulings.

Guided Path
1
Parse the two formulations
Identify the presence or absence of the particle 'ba' in the exception clause: 'except with my permission' (إلا بإذني) vs 'except that I permit you' (إلا أن آذن لك).
The particle 'ba' is a key indicator of attachment (الإلصاق) in Hanafi usul.
2
Analyze linguistic structure
For 'إلا بإذني', the 'ba' indicates that the exception is an exit attached to permission, making the description 'attached to permission' generalize over all exits, requiring each exit to have its own permission. For 'إلا أن آذن لك', the absence of 'ba' and the non-homogeneousness of permission and exit necessitate interpreting 'except' as a limit (غاية) meaning 'until', so one permission suffices to remove the restriction.
The Hanafi position relies on the literal meaning of 'ba' and the principle that an indefinite noun described by a generalizing attribute becomes general.
3
Apply the generalization principle
In 'إلا بإذني', the exception phrase is interpreted as 'except an exit attached to my permission'. Since 'an exit attached to my permission' is an indefinite noun described by a restrictive attribute, it generalizes over all exits, so any exit not meeting that description is a breach.
This is an application of the usul rule: 'al-nakirah fi siyaq al-ithbat ta'mm' (indefinite in affirmative context generalizes) when described by a qualifying attribute.
4
Consider objections and Hanafi responses
The opposing view argues that both formulations should be treated equally by estimating a deleted 'ba' in the second or interpreting the verb as a time adverb. The Hanafi response refutes these: estimation of 'ba' is not necessary and leads to a confused construction; the time adverb interpretation requires excessive deletion. The metaphor in treating 'except' as a limit is easier and more acceptable.
The glosses emphasize that the construction proposed by opponents is 'confused' (مختل) as reported from Imam Muhammad.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In the first formulation, each exit without specific permission triggers divorce; in the second, after one general permission, all future exits are permitted without further permission.
This shows how a single particle changes the legal outcome.

(القمر)
فلا يحنث بالشك وفيه أن عدم الحنث لماكان مجتهدا فيه، فهو ليس بيقيني حتى لا يزول بالشك كذا قيل. (القمر)
Statement of the divisions of the third division. Discussion of the 'ba'. Because the requirement of the statement is absoluteness, and there is no requirement to deviate from it. And it is not said: The transitive of informing, not absoluteness, is only with 'ba', so the estimation would be: 'If you had informed me that so-and-so came', and it would be like the first; because we say: Estimation of 'ba' is insufficient except for the soundness of meaning without its other effects. i.e., attachment etc. And if he said: 'If you leave the house except with my permission', repetition of permission is required for each exit; because its meaning is: 'If you leave the house, you are divorced, except an exit attached to my permission', and it is an indefinite noun described in the affirmative, so it generalizes by the generality of the description, so what is other than it is forbidden, and whenever she leaves without his permission she is divorced, and perhaps it is for when there is no clue of an immediate oath or the consideration of 'ba' predominates. Unlike his saying: 'except that I permit you' i.e., he says: 'If you leave the house except that I permit you, you are divorced', for then repetition of permission is not required for each exit, rather if permission is found once, it suffices to avoid breach, because 'ba' is not present in it and the exception is not correct; because permission is not of the same kind as exit, so it is in the sense of a limit, and for a limit, its existence once suffices; so the prohibition of exit is lifted by the existence of permission once. It is absoluteness, whether lying or truthful. (Al-Qamar) Transitivity of informing: i.e., to the second object, not the first. (Al-Muhashi) We say etc.: This is a response after admission; otherwise, someone might say: The restriction derived from his statement that transitivity of informing is only with 'ba' is denied; for informing is transitive to the second object by itself. (Al-Qamar) For soundness of meaning etc., i.e., the transitivity of informing from the first object to the second object without its other effects, and it is a change from absoluteness to restriction. And 'perhaps it is' etc. means that the generality of exit and the condition of repetition of permission for each exit is only when there is no clue of an immediate oath, or if there is but the consideration of 'ba' predominates. But if there is a clue of an immediate oath and the consideration of 'ba' does not predominate, then repetition of permission for each exit is not required, rather the speech is interpreted as the specific exit, as previously explained in the section on immediate oaths, so remember. (Al-Qamar) Sufficient to avoid breach: So after permission once, if she leaves without permission, divorce does not occur. (Al-Qamar) Not of the same kind as exit: i.e., not among the individuals of exit. (Al-Qamar) So it is in the sense of a limit: i.e., in the sense of 'to' metaphorically, and the appropriateness is that the limit restricts the extension of the limited, just as the exception restricts the exception from. (Al-Qamar)

Statement of the divisions of the third division. Discussion of the 'ba'. And it is objected that the estimation of a limit is forced, and better is the estimation of 'ba', so the meaning would be: 'except an exit with my permission', so its ultimate result and the ultimate result of his saying 'except with my permission' are one, so repetition of permission is required for each exit. Or it is said: The present tense with 'an' is interpreted as a verbal noun, and the verbal noun may occur as an adverb of time, as is said: 'I come to you at the rising of the star' i.e., at the time of its rising. So the meaning would be: 'Do not exit at any time except at the time of permission', so permission is required for each exit. And the first response is that the estimation of his saying: 'except an exit with my permission' is a speech that is confused, with no known aspect of validity. And the second response is that then he would be in breach if she leaves without permission, while on the first estimation he is not, so he is not in breach due to doubt. i.e., that 'except' is in the sense of 'to'. After permission once. 'Once'. By estimation of limit: i.e., making 'except' in the sense of 'to' is forced because it is rare in occurrence. (Al-Qamar) And the better etc.: For the deletion of 'ba' is common with 'anna' and 'in'. (Al-Qamar) And the first response etc.: And it can also be responded that estimation is contrary to the principle, and necessity does not call for it, and metaphor in the word 'except' even if contrary to principle, is easier than deletion, especially if deletion is frequent, like deletion of 'ba' and the word 'exit'. (Al-Qamar) 'A speech that is confused' etc.: Thus narrated from Imam Muhammad, and Allah knows best the intended meaning of His servant regarding the aspect of confusion. And my teacher, Mawlana al-Mufti Muhammad Asghar, and my paternal uncle, the Imam of the Usuliyyun, may Allah illuminate his resting place, explained the aspect of confusion: The particle of attachment requires an attached thing in the speech of the Arabs, and its deletion is common due to the presence of indication, and the deleted thing in his saying 'except with my permission' is the exit by which the exception is realized, as if he said: 'except an exit attached to my permission', and the exception is valid. But here, there is no mention of 'ba' in the speech, so deletion of 'exit' without evidence is not valid. Therefore, what is in some glosses, i.e., the gloss of Mulla Irfan on 'Al-Da'ir', that the confusion is accepted, is not to be listened to. (Al-Qamar) 'Confusion' etc. It was said against it: There is no confusion in it on the estimation of 'ba'. The correct response is that it is a weighting by multiplicity of evidences, but consideration is not by quantity but by strength. Do you not see that if there is one verse on one side and two verses on the other, the single verse is not abandoned, and it is not said: The two verses conflict, so the other verse remains free from conflict. And it was responded that the intent of the author of 'Al-Mabsut' is that such a construction has not been heard, not that there is corruption in terms of meaning, and in it is reflection. (Al-Sunbuli) And the second response etc.: And it can be responded that this would require much deletion, i.e., deletion of the excepted-from and deletion of the time from the verbal noun, so reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'So he is not in breach due to doubt' and in it that since the non-breach is a matter of ijtihad, it is not certain so as not to be removed by doubt, as was said. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the particle 'ba' in the context of conditional divorce oaths. The author discusses two formulations: 'except with my permission' (إلا بإذني) and 'except that I permit you' (إلا أن آذن لك). The main issue is whether permission must be repeated for each act of leaving the house. The text argues that in the first formulation, the presence of 'ba' (indicating attachment) implies that each exit requires a separate permission, because the exception is an indefinite noun described by the attribute of being attached to permission, and that attribute generalizes. In the second formulation, the absence of 'ba' and the fact that 'permission' is not of the same kind as 'exit' leads to interpreting 'except' as a limit (ghaya), like 'until', so a single permission suffices to cover all future exits. The author also addresses objections, such as the claim that both formulations should be treated the same because the underlying meaning is similar. Responses are given, including grammatical arguments about the rarity of 'except' as a limit, the common deletion of 'ba' in certain constructions, and the principle that a metaphor is easier than deletion. The glosses further clarify points, such as the definition of 'modification' and the Hanafi position that the ruling is based on the explicit wording rather than inferred meanings. The passage concludes by noting that if there is doubt (shakk), the original innocence (non-breach) prevails, but since the matter is subject to ijtihad, it is not absolute certainty.

Key Terms
الباء (al-bā'): The particle 'ba' used for attachment (الإلصاق) in Arabic grammar; in this passage, it indicates that the exception is directly attached to the permission.
الغاية (al-ghāyah): A limit or endpoint; here, 'except' (إلا) is interpreted figuratively as meaning 'until' or 'except for the time of'.
الحنث (al-ḥinth): Breach of an oath; violation of the conditional divorce statement, resulting in divorce.
الاستثناء (al-istithnā'): Grammatical exception; in this passage, the phrase 'except with my permission' is analyzed as an exception structure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She must obtain permission for each exit, or she will be divorced.
B) She may leave any number of times after that one permission without being divorced.
C) The divorce is invalid because the oath is ambiguous.
D) She is divorced immediately upon hearing the oath.

Key Takeaway
The presence or absence of the particle 'ba' in an oath exception fundamentally changes the ruling on whether permission must be repeated.

Temporal Adverbials 'Qabl' and 'Ba'd' in Legal Declarations
Analysis of temporal adverbials in divorce and debt acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul analysis of temporal adverbials 'qabl' and 'ba'd' to derive legal rulings in divorce and debt acknowledgment.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'before' and 'after' are relational terms whose legal effect depends on the locus's capacity for consecutive events.

This lesson delves into the linguistic analysis of temporal adverbials in legal Arabic. Understanding how 'qabl' and 'ba'd' function in declarations of divorce and debt acknowledgment is crucial for accurate istinbat (derivation of rulings). We will unpack the Hanafi approach, which treats these as relational attributes (idāfī) that impose logical necessities on the legal consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the declaration and context
Determine whether the declaration is about divorce (talāq) or debt acknowledgment (iqrār). Each context has different loci (mahall) and thus different rules.
In divorce, the locus is the wife; in debt, the locus is the liability (dhimmah).
2
Assess the locus's capacity for sequential events
For divorce, check if the wife is cohabited (mawtū'a) or not. A non-cohabited wife has no 'iddah and cannot sustain consecutive divorces; a cohabited wife can. For debt, the dhimmah can sustain multiple obligations.
This step applies the principle of qabliyya/bad'iyya as relational attributes.
3
Apply the linguistic principle of relational attributes
The words 'qabl' and 'ba'd' imply the existence of the related event. In divorce, saying 'after the previous divorce' connects the new divorce to the past one, so both fall together. In debt, 'before a dirham' can be interpreted either as an attribute of the first dirham (one dirham total) or as a separate obligation (two dirhams), leading to ikhtilaf.
This step uses the Hanafi usul rule that al-idāfa tuḥaqqiq al-muḍāf ilayh.
4
Derive the ruling based on context and linguistic analysis
Synthesize the analysis to state the ruling: for a non-cohabited wife, both divorces fall together; for a cohabited wife, they fall sequentially as per 'iddah. For iqrār, the majority Hanafi view interprets 'qabl' as an attribute (صفت) leading to one dirham, but a minority view holds it as a separate obligation (دين مستقل) leading to two dirhams.
The muftā bihi for debt acknowledgment is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث ۳۹۰ بحث أسماء الظروف في الحال الآتية فتقع الأولى ولا يعلم حال الآتية، ومعنى الثاني: أنت طالق واحدة التي كانت بعد الواحدة الأخرى الماضية، فتقعان معًا، وهذا كله في الطلاق وأما في الإقرار فيلزم في قوله: له علي درهم واحد قبل درهم درهم واحد وفي الصور الأخر يلزمه درهمان هكذا قالوا. "وعند" للحضرة، فإذا قال لغيره : "لك عندي ألف درهم كان وديعة؛ لأن الحضرة تدل على الحفظ دون اللزوم؛ لأن "عند" يكون للقرب، والقرب المتيقن هو قرب الأمانة دون الدين؛ لأنه محتمل، ولهذا إذا وصل به لفظ الدين بأن يقول: "لك" عندي ألف دينا" يكون دينًا. أي لاحتمال الدين ولا يعلم حال الآتية: هذه مسامحة والأولى أن يقول: لا يقع الطلاق بعد؛ لأنها غير موطوءة ولا عدة لها فليس هي محلاً لوقوع الطلاق بعد طلاق. (القمر) فتقعان معا لأنه طلق واحدة بقوله: "أنت طالق واحدة" ووصفها بأنها بعد الواحدة الأخرى الماضية، وإيقاع الطلاق في الماضي إيقاع في الحال، فتقع هذه أيضًا مع الأولى (القمر) وهذا كله في الطلاق أي لغير الموطوءة، وأما إذا كانت موطوءة فيقع في الصور الأربع (أي قبلها واحدة، وبعدها واحدة وقبل ،واحدة وبعد واحدة اثنتان لوجود العدة، سواء أضيف القبل أو البعد إلى الظاهر أو المضمر كذا في الدر المختار"، والسر أن كون الشيء قبل شيء آخر يقتضي وجود ذلك الشيء الآخر؛ لأن القبلية من الإضافيات، فيقع طلاقان. (القمر) فيلزم إلخ لأن القبل نعت للأول، فكأنه قيل: "له علي درهم واحد قبل درهم" يجب "علي" في الاستقبال فيلزمه درهم واحد هكذا نقل صاحب كشف البزدوي"، وقال صاحب "التلويح": إنه لو قال: له" علي درهم واحد قبل درهم يجب درهمان كما في الصور الأخر، وقال بعض محشيه أي شيخ الإسلام: يصح عقلاً ودليلاً، فإنه يمكن أن يكون معناه درهم قبل درهم في الحال لا في الاستقبال.(القمر) وفي الصور الأخر إلخ: أي لو قاله لي درهم قبله درهم فعليه در همان كما هو الظاهر، ولو قال: بعد درهم فيلزمه در همان؛ لأن معناه بعد درهم قد وجب علي، وكذا لو قال بعده ،درهم فيلزمه در همان؛ لأن معناه بعده درهم قد وجب علي، والسر أن الدرهم بعد الدرهم يجب دينًا على الذمة لبقاء المحل، وأما الطلاق بعد الطلاق في الصور السابقة فلا يقع؛ لأن الزوجة غير موطوءة ولا عدة لها، فهي ليست محلاً للطلاق بعد طلاق. (القمر)
Statement of the divisions of the third division. 390. Research on nouns of adverbs. In the case of the future, the first falls and the state of the future is not known. The meaning of the second: You are divorced once which was after the other previous once, so they both fall together. And all this is in divorce. As for in acknowledgment, it is binding in his statement: 'He has against me one dirham before a dirham' is one dirham. In the other forms, two dirhams are binding, thus they said. And 'ind' is for presence. So if he says to another: 'You have with me a thousand dirhams', it is a deposit because 'presence' indicates preservation without liability, because 'ind' is for proximity, and the certain proximity is the proximity of trust not of debt, because it is probable. For this, if he connects to it the word 'debt' by saying 'you have with me a thousand as debt', it becomes a debt. (commentary) And he does not know the state of the future: this is lenient, and it is better that he says: The divorce does not occur afterwards because she is not cohabited and has no waiting period, so she is not a locus for the occurrence of divorce after divorce. (al-Qamar) So they both fall together because he divorced once by his saying 'You are divorced once' and described it as after the other previous once, and effecting divorce in the past is effecting in the present, so this also falls with the first. (al-Qamar) And all this is in divorce, i.e., for the non-cohabited woman. As for if she is cohabited, it occurs in the four forms (i.e., before it one, and after it one, and before one and after one two due to the waiting period, whether the before or after is attached to the explicit or implicit pronoun as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar). And the secret is that something being before something else necessitates the existence of that other thing, because 'beforeness' is relational, so two divorces occur. (al-Qamar) So it is binding etc. because 'before' is an attribute of the first, so as if it was said: 'He has against me one dirham before a dirham' requires 'against me' in the future, so one dirham is binding. Thus narrated the author of Kashf al-Bazdawi. And the author of al-Talwih said: if he said 'He has against me one dirham before a dirham', two dirhams are binding as in the other forms. And some of its commentators, i.e., Shaykh al-Islam, said: it is valid rationally and evidentially, because it can mean a dirham before a dirham in the present not in the future. (al-Qamar) And in the other forms etc.: i.e., if he said 'I have a dirham before it a dirham', then two dirhams are upon him, as is apparent. And if he said 'after a dirham', then two dirhams are binding because its meaning is 'after a dirham has become obligatory upon me'. Similarly, if he said 'after it a dirham', then two dirhams are binding because its meaning is 'after it a dirham has become obligatory upon me'. And the secret is that the dirham after the dirham becomes a debt on the liability due to the continuation of the locus. As for divorce after divorce in the previous cases, it does not occur because the wife is not cohabited and has no waiting period, so she is not a locus for the occurrence of divorce after divorce. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage is a detailed textual analysis of how the Arabic temporal adverbs 'qabl' (before) and 'ba'd' (after) function in legal declarations, particularly in divorce (talāq) and debt acknowledgment (iqrār). The commentator expands on the base text (matn) which likely stated the basic rulings. The key principle is that 'before' and 'after' are relational terms that imply the existence of the related event. In divorce, if a man says to his non-cohabited wife 'You are divorced once which was after the previous one,' both divorces fall together because 'after' connects the new divorce to the past one, and since she is not cohabited and has no 'iddah, she cannot be a locus for consecutive divorces. In debt acknowledgment, if someone says 'He has against me one dirham before a dirham,' this is interpreted as one dirham because 'before' qualifies the first dirham as an attribute, not as a separate debt. However, there is an ikhtilaf: some scholars like the author of al-Talwih and Shaykh al-Islam argue that it could mean two dirhams if 'before' is interpreted as a separate obligation in the present. The passage also touches on the word 'ind' (at/with), which by default implies custody (amāna) unless explicitly linked to debt (dayn). This analysis is based on linguistic principles and the nature of these particles in Arabic. The commentary follows the structure of the matn and then adds clarifications from various sources like Kashf al-Bazdawi, al-Talwih, and al-Durr al-Mukhtar.

Key Terms
قبل (qabl): A temporal adverb meaning 'before', used to indicate precedence. In legal declarations, it qualifies the following noun as an attribute or indicates a separate obligation depending on construction.
بعد (ba'd): A temporal adverb meaning 'after', used to indicate subsequence. In legal declarations, it implies the existence of the preceding event and can create a new obligation.
عند (ind): A preposition meaning 'at' or 'with', indicating presence or proximity. By default, it implies custody (amāna) unless qualified by 'dayn' (debt), in which case it implies liability.
القبلية (al-qabliyya): The quality of being before, considered a relational attribute (idāfī) that necessitates the existence of the other entity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a divorce declaration to a non-cohabited wife, if the husband says 'You are divorced once which was after the previous one,' how many divorces occur?
A) One divorce
B) Two divorces
C) Three divorces
D) No divorce

Key Takeaway
The legal effect of temporal adverbials 'qabl' and 'ba'd' depends on their relational nature and the capacity of the locus for sequential events.
