Classifying Khabar Wahid by Subject Matter
Classifying the subject matter of khabar into five types under huquq Allah and huquq al-ibad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the subject matter of khabar wahid into the five types under huquq Allah and huquq al-ibad, and explain how this classification affects acceptance of khabar wahid.

Core Idea
Khabar wahid is evaluated differently based on whether it deals with rights of Allah or rights of servants.

In this lesson, we explore the third division of khabar wahid: classification by its subject matter (mahall). This division is crucial because it determines how strictly a khabar is applied. The Hanafi school distinguishes between rights of Allah (huquq Allah) and rights of servants (huquq al-ibad), each with subcategories. Understanding this taxonomy helps you evaluate the strength of evidence for different types of rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories
The subject matter of khabar is first divided into huquq Allah (rights of Allah) and huquq al-ibad (rights of servants).
This division is independent of the chain of transmission.
2
Break down huquq Allah
Huquq Allah are subdivided into: (1) penalties (uqubat) such as hadd punishments, and (2) non-penalties such as acts of worship.
Penalties require stronger evidence.
3
Break down huquq al-ibad
Huquq al-ibad are subdivided into three: (a) pure obligation (ilzam mahd) like debts, (b) no obligation at all (like recommendations), and (c) obligation in some respects but not others (e.g., contracts).
4
Note the scope and concession
This division applies to any khabar wahid, even from the common people, but it is a well-known concession (musamaha) of the Salaf, following Fakhr al-Islam.
The classification is not about the narrator but the subject matter.
5
Understand the implication for acceptance
For huquq Allah, especially penalties, Hanafi usul requires stronger evidence; khabar wahid may be rejected if it contradicts a definitive text. For huquq al-ibad, khabar wahid is more readily accepted.
This accords with the principle that rights of Allah are based on caution (ihtiyat).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان التقسيم الثالث
والتقسيم الثالث في بيان محل الخبر الذي جعل الخبر فيه حجة، وهو إما حقوق الله تعالى وهو نوعان: العقوبات وغيرها، وإما حقوق العباد، وهو ثلاثة أقسام: ما فيه إلزام محض، أو لا إلزام فيه أصلاً، أو فيه إلزام من وجه دون وجه، فهذه خمسة أنواع، وهذا التقسيم لمطلق الخبر الواحد أعم من أن يكون خبر الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم، أو أصحابه، أو عامة الخلق من أهل السوق وهي من المسامحات المشهورة لجمهور السلف اقتداءً بفخر الإسلام.
صدقة أي إذا كان الغرض منها أي من النفقة على نفسه العبادة (القمر) مردودًا أما الأول: فلأن الخبر الواحد مظنون والكتاب قطعي متنا وسندا، فلا اعتداد به بمقابلته، وأما الثاني؛ فلأن السنة المعروفة قطعي الثبوت، وفوق خبر الواحد فلها الاعتبار، وأما الثالث؛ فلأن الكثيرين كانوا حاضرين في تلك الحادثة، والواحد منهم يخالفهم، وهم كانوا بخلوص الاعتقاد طالبي قوله الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم وفعله، فمخالفتهم لا تعبأ بها لوقوع الشبهة فيه، وأما الرابع؛ فلأن الصحابة منه هم الأصول في الدين، ولم يتهموا بترك الاحتجاج بالحجة، فترك الصحابة المحاجة به عند ظهور الاختلاف بينهم دليل باهر على أن هذا الحديث سهو من الراوي بعدهم، أو منسوخ، أو فيه علة أخرى، فلا يعمل به. (القمر)
كما في النوع الأول وهو ما إذا كان نقصان في الناقل، وهذا تفسير لقول المصنف له أيضا. (القمر) الأول: هو أن يكون النقصان في الناقل. (المحشي) في بيان محل أي الحادثة التي ورد فيها. (القمر) المسامحات إلخ لأن البحث بحث خبر الوصول وأصحابه لا خبر عامة الخلق. (القمر)
قال البغوي في تفسيره تحت قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أَنْفَقْتُمْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ فَهُوَ يُخْلِفُهُ وَهُوَ خَيْرُ الرَّازِقِينَ﴾ (سبأ: ٣٩) أنا عبد الواحد المليحى، أنا أبو منصور السمعاني، أنا أبو جعفر الرباني، أنا حميد بن زنجوية، أنا أبو الربيع، أنا عبد الحميد بن الحسن الهلالي، أنا محمد بن المنكدر عن جابر بن عبد الله قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "كل معروف صدقة، وكل ما أنفق الرجل على نفسه وأهله كتب له صدقة" الحديث. [إشراق الأبصار: ٢١]
Statement on the third division. The third division is concerning the subject matter of the report in which the report is made a proof. It is either the rights of Allah Almighty, which are two types: penalties and other than penalties, or the rights of servants, which are three types: that which contains pure obligation, that which contains no obligation at all, or that which contains obligation in some respects but not others. So there are five types. This division applies to absolute khabar wahid, whether it is a report of the Messenger of Allah, or his Companions, or the common people from the marketplace. This is from the well-known concessions of the majority of the Salaf, following the example of Fakhr al-Islam. [Commentary on 'sadaqa': i.e., if the purpose of spending on oneself is worship. (Al-Qamar) Rejected: As for the first, because khabar wahid is speculative while the Book is definitive in text and chain, so it is not considered in opposition to it. As for the second, because the well-known Sunnah is definitive in transmission and is above khabar wahid, so it is given consideration. As for the third, because many people were present at that incident, and one of them contradicts them, and they were, with purity of belief, seekers of the saying and action of the Messenger of Allah, so their contradiction is not paid attention to due to suspicion. As for the fourth, because the Companions among them are the foundations in religion and are not accused of abandoning proof with evidence. So the Companions' abandonment of arguing with it when difference appeared among them is a clear indication that this hadith is a mistake from the narrator after them, or abrogated, or has another defect, so it is not acted upon. (Al-Qamar) As in the first type, which is when there is a defect in the transmitter. This is an explanation of the author's statement also. (Al-Qamar) The first: that the defect is in the transmitter. (Al-Muhashshi) In the explanation of the place, i.e., the incident in which it occurred. (Al-Qamar) The concessions etc., because the discussion is the discussion of the report of the one who has access and his companions, not the report of the common people. (Al-Qamar) Al-Baghawi said in his tafsir under the verse: 'And whatever you spend of good, He will replace it, and He is the best of providers' (Saba: 39): ... from Jabir ibn Abdullah that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Every act of kindness is charity, and whatever a man spends on himself and his family is recorded as charity.'
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage presents the third division of khabar wahid based on its subject matter (mahall al-khabar). The author classifies reports into two broad categories: rights of Allah (huquq Allah) and rights of servants (huquq al-ibad). Rights of Allah are further divided into penalties (uqubat) such as hadd punishments, and non-penalties (like acts of worship). Rights of servants are three: matters of pure obligation (e.g., debts), matters with no obligation (e.g., recommendations), and matters of obligation in some respects but not others (e.g., certain contracts). This gives a total of five types. The author notes that this division applies to khabar wahid and is a well-known concession among the Salaf. The commentary then repeats the earlier discussion of the four indicators for rejecting khabar wahid, linking it to the earlier lesson. Finally, a supporting hadith from al-Baghawi is cited to illustrate that spending on oneself can be charity.

Key Terms
حقوق الله (huquq Allah): Rights that pertain to Allah, including penalties (e.g., hadd) and acts of worship (e.g., prayer).
حقوق العباد (huquq al-ibad): Rights of servants, divided into three: pure obligation (e.g., debts), no obligation (e.g., voluntary acts), and mixed (e.g., contracts).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the third division, into how many types is the subject matter of khabar divided?
A) Two: rights of Allah and rights of servants
B) Five: two under rights of Allah and three under rights of servants
C) Three: obligations, recommendations, and prohibitions
D) Four: penalties, worship, transactions, and punishments

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of khabar wahid depends on its subject matter: rights of Allah require stricter evidence than rights of servants.

Partial Binding Effect: Conditions for News of Dismissal and Restriction
Explaining the third division of sunna: reports with partial binding effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi positions on the conditions for accepting news with partial binding effect and evaluate the competing usul arguments.

Core Idea
News with partial binding effect requires either two informants or one upright informant according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn accept any discerning informant.

In this passage, we encounter the third division of sunna reports—those that have a binding effect from one aspect but not another. The case in point is news about the dismissal of an agent or restriction of a permitted slave. Abu Hanifa imposes a conditional half of testimony, while his two disciples argue for complete relaxation due to necessity. Let's walk through the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the third division
Recognize that khabar is divided into three types: fully binding, non-binding, and partially binding. The third type is the focus here.
Partial binding means ilzam from one aspect only, like news of dismissal.
2
Understand the two aspects
From the principal's side, dismissal is his own right, so no ilzam on him. From the agent's side, dismissal imposes liability, so ilzam exists.
This duality is key to the ruling.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's position
He requires one of the two halves of testimony (shatr min shatray al-shahada): either two informants or one upright (adl) informant.
This is a middle ground between full conditions and none.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's objection
They argue that necessity in mu'amalat demands flexibility; requiring conditions would cause hardship. They accept any reliable report.
They also point out that the need is already alleviated by not requiring conditions for the original messenger.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text notes that in some commentaries of Sahih Muslim, the Sahibayn's view is considered more apparent (al-azhar).
This shows the dynamic nature of tarjih in later scholarship.

وإن كان فيه أي في محل الخبر من حقوق العباد إلزام إلخ. (القمر) وحجر المأذون إلخ: الحجر لغة: المنع وشرعا منع من نفاذ تصرف ،قولي وسببه ،صغر وجنون ورق كذا في "الدر المختار". Statement of the third division: The Prophet, peace be upon him, used to accept the news of a gift from both the righteous and the wicked. But if there is in it (the news) binding effect from one aspect and not from another, like news of dismissal of an agent and restriction of a slave who is permitted to trade. For from the aspect that the principal and the master act in their own right by dismissal and restriction as they act by agency and permission, there is no binding effect at all. And from the aspect that the action is confined to the agent and slave after dismissal and restriction, and liability attaches to them in that, there is binding harm on the agent and slave. Therefore, one half of testimony is stipulated according to Abu Hanifa, meaning number or uprightness (adala), i.e., it is necessary that the informant be two or one upright, observing the similarity of both sides. For if it were purely binding (by dismissal and restriction) both halves would be stipulated, and if there were no binding at all nothing would be stipulated from them. So we gave a share of number and uprightness to both sides. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) nothing is stipulated in it; rather restriction and dismissal are established by the news of every discerning person absolutely. The following commentary explains: (al-Qamar) 'and restriction of the slave' etc. (al-Qamar) 'acts in his own right' etc. (al-Sanbali) 'by dismissal and restriction' etc. (al-Qamar) 'it is confined' etc. (al-Qamar) 'one half is stipulated' so the report of a single fasiq is not accepted. (al-Qamar) 'We gave a share' etc. so the stipulation of one half is due to similarity to binding, and the lack of stipulation of both is due to similarity to non-binding. (al-Qamar) 'according to them nothing is stipulated' because in transactions there is necessity for agency and dismissal, so if one half of testimony were stipulated it would become difficult. And it can be said that necessity is repelled by non-stipulation regarding the messenger and agent. In some commentaries of Muslim it is said that their view is more apparent. This is perhaps taken from the hadith of Burayda and Salman mentioned earlier. And al-Tirmidhi narrated...
Source pages p. 536

Commentary
This passage is the third division of sunna reports, focusing on news that has partial binding effect, such as the news of dismissing an agent or restricting a permitted slave. The author explains that this news has two aspects: from the principal's perspective it is not binding (he acts in his own right), but from the agent's perspective it imposes liability. Abu Hanifa takes a middle position requiring either two witnesses or one upright witness, because it resembles both binding and non-binding. The two imams (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require no conditions at all, arguing that necessity in transactions demands flexibility; otherwise it would be impractical. They also note that the need is already met by not requiring conditions in the case of the original messenger or agent. The commentary by al-Qamar further clarifies technical terms and supports the view of the two imams as stronger. The hadith about accepting gifts from polytheists is cited as evidence that the Prophet accepted news from all, but that is for gifts, not for binding legal changes.

Key Terms
إلزام (ilzam): Binding legal effect that imposes a duty or liability on someone.
شطرا الشهادة (shatray al-shahada): The two halves of testimony: number (two witnesses) and 'adala (uprightness).
حجر (hajr): Legal restriction preventing a person from conducting financial transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is required for the acceptance of news about the dismissal of an agent?
A) Two upright witnesses
B) Either two informants or one upright informant
C) No conditions at all
D) One informant, regardless of uprightness

Key Takeaway
The binding effect of a report can be graded; partial ilzam leads to moderate conditions, but necessity in transactions may relax them entirely.

The Exile of the Fornicator: Policy or Hadd? Hanafi Use of Companion Action
Explaining Hanafi use of Companion action to interpret the exile hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument that Umar's exile of a fornicator was policy and not part of the hadd punishment, and apply this method to other hadiths where a Companion's action seems contrary to a clear text.

Core Idea
Companion's action contrary to a clear hadith indicates abrogation or policy, not invalidation.

This lesson examines a classical debate between Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the punishment for unmarried fornicators. The hadith prescribes flogging and exile for a year. While Shafi'is consider exile part of the hadd, Hanafis argue that Caliph Umar's later practice shows it was only discretionary policy. We will explore how the Hanafi school uses the actions of Companions to interpret and sometimes override the apparent meaning of a hadith, applying istihsan and the presumption of abrogation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and the dispute
State the hadith (flogging and exile) and the Shafi'i position that exile is part of the hadd.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof from Umar's action
Explain that Umar exiled a man who later apostatized, then swore never to exile again, proving it was not a fixed hadd.
The key evidence is the oath; if exile were hadd, he would not have sworn to abandon it.
3
Evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i reliance on the hadith
Hanafis argue the hadith is clear and known to the caliphs, but Umar's action indicates policy, not denial. They suggest abrogation or reinterpretation.
4
Distinguish between apparent and hidden hadith
Note that if a hadith is subtle (like the laugh-wudu hadith), a Companion's contrary action does not indicate criticism. But if it's clear, it suggests abrogation.
This distinction is crucial for understanding when Companion action affects a hadith.
5
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis do not enforce exile as part of hadd, while Shafi'is do.
This affects judges and legal systems that follow different schools.

بيان طعن يلحق الحديث
باب أقسام السنة وأبو موسى الأشعري الله لم يعمل به وذلك لا يوجب كونه جرحًا عليه؛ لأنه من الحوادث النادرة التي تحتمل الخفاء على أبي موسى الأشعريه والطعن المبهم من أئمة الحديث لا يجرح الراوي عندنا بأن يقول: هذا الحديث مجروح أو منكر أو نحوهما فيعمل
كنفي العدالة
به، إلا إذا وقع مفسراً بما هو جرح متفق عليه الكل لا مختلف فيه بحيث يكون جرحًا عند بعض دون بعض، ومع ذلك يكون الجرح صادرًا ممن اشتهر بالنصحية دون التعصب؛ لأن المتعصبين قد أخلوا الدين كثيرًا، ويجعلون المكروه حراما، والمندوب فرضًا، فلا يعتبر بجرح هؤلاء القاصرين حتى لا يقبل الطعن بالتدليس، وهو في اللغة: كتمان عيب السلعة عن المشتري، وفي اصطلاح المحدّثين: كتمان التفصيل في الإسناد بأن يقول: حدثنا فلان عن فلان إلخ، ولا يقول:
لم يعمل به روى الطحاوي عن أبي موسى أن مذهبه إيجاب الوضوء من القهقهة. كذا قال العلي القارئ (القمر) وذلك أي عدم عمل أبي موسى الأشعريه على ذلك الحديث. (القمر)
لا يجرح إلخ لأن العدالة أصل في كل مسلم نظراً إلى العقل والدين لا سيما الصدر الأول، فلا يترك الحديث بالجرح المبهم لجواز أن يعتقد الجارح ما ليس بجرح في الواقع جرحًا، فلا بد في قبول الجرح من تفصيله.(القمر) أو منكر وقال بحر العلوم مولانا عبد العلي : إن الطعن بأن الراوي عند جميع أئمة الحديث متروك الحديث، أو : بأن حديثه عند أئمة الحديث منكر جرح مفسر، فهو يجرح الراوي ،ألبتة، ثم اعلم أن أئمة الحديث إنما يكتبون في كتبهم جرحًا مطلقًا، فهذا الجرح ليس بمبهم، بل سببه معلوم عندهم لكنهم لا يصرحون به حياء ومروءة، وربما يصرحون أيضا بسبب الجرح كأن يقولوا: هو كذاب وواضع الحديث، وأمثال ذلك، والمنكر حديث رواه غير ضابط قد بعد عن درجة الضابط، كذا قال ابن الصلاح، وله حدود آخَرُ مذكورة في أصول الحديث. (القمر) ونحوهما : كأن يقول: إنه مطعون. (القمر) عند بعض دون بعض كالطعن من الحنفي على الشافعي بأكل متروك التسمية عامدًا ، فإن مذهبه الحِلّ فيه. (القمر) ممن اشتهر إلخ أي بكونه خاليا من النفسانية، وناصحاً للدين. (القمر) لأن المتعصبين إلخ أي الذين من عادتهم التشديد حتى يَعُدّون الجرح القليل كثيرًا، ويعينون الجرح فيما ليس بجرح كابن الجوزي وأمثاله. (القمر) حتى لا يقبل إلخ تفريع على أنه لا يقبل إلا الجرح المتفق عليه.(القمر)
Section on Divisions of Sunnah. Explanation of criticism that affects hadith. I did not see him raise his hands except in the opening takbir, so abandoning it is evidence of its abrogation. The action of a Companion contrary to it necessitates criticism if the hadith is apparent and not subtle. The obligation of the hadith is upon them. From here begins criticism coming from other than the narrator. Its example is what was narrated by Ubadah ibn al-Samit: 'The unmarried person with the unmarried person: flogging of one hundred and exile for a year.' Al-Shafi'i adheres to it and makes exile part of the hadd. We say: Indeed Umar exiled a man who apostatized and joined the Byzantines, i.e., the hadd of zina for the unmarried, and he swore that he would never exile anyone. So if exile had been a hadd, he would not have sworn to abandon it. Thus it is known that the exile from him was policy, not a hadd. And the hadith of the hudud was apparent, not hidden from the caliphs who were appointed to enforce hudud. And he made an exception for what could be hidden from them, for it does not necessitate criticism in it, like the hadith of the obligation of wudu from laughing out loud in prayer narrated by Zayd ibn Khalid al-Juhani. The hidden hadith. From both sides, so each one must be from him. At most, one of them is abrogated, and the apparent is the abrogation of the raising, for in the beginning many actions and words were permissible, then abrogated, so it is not far that this is of that kind. As for the absence of raising, it is an original absence, so it does not accept abrogation, and it is compatible with humility. (Al-Qamar) The Companion: He only restricted it to the Companion because the action of a non-Companion from the imams of transmission contrary to the hadith does not necessitate criticism absolutely, but there is detail which the author will explain later in his statement: 'And the ambiguous criticism' etc. (Al-Qamar) In the criticism: i.e., in criticism affecting the hadith from other than the narrator. (Al-Qamar) The exile: i.e., exile from the country to a place the distance of travel. Thus said al-Malik. (Al-Qamar) He exiled: i.e., from the country a man, namely Rabi'ah ibn Umayyah, who joined the Byzantines and became Christian. Thus narrated Abd al-Razzaq from Ibn al-Musayyab. (Al-Qamar) The exile from him: i.e., the exile from the country from Umar. (Al-Qamar) To it: i.e., to his statement: If the hadith is apparent. (Al-Qamar) Then it: i.e., then the action of the Companion contrary to the hadith that could be hidden from them. (Al-Qamar) Like the hadith of obligation etc.: Said al-Ali al-Qari: As for their statement that Zayd ibn Khalid narrated it, it is not found in any of the books in the hands of scholars now, and the imams narrated it from Abu Hanifa without the path of Zayd. Muhammad narrated it from the mursal of al-Hasan, and others narrated it from the path of Ma'bad. (Al-Qamar) Ibn. Its takhrij has been mentioned. Its takhrij. Its takhrij. Explanation of criticism affecting hadith. Section on Divisions of Sunnah. And Abu Musa al-Ash'ari did not act upon it, and that does not necessitate that it be a defect in him, because it is from the rare incidents that could be hidden from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. And ambiguous criticism from the imams of hadith does not impugn the narrator with us by saying: This hadith is criticized or munkar or similar, so it is acted upon. Except if it occurs explained as a defect agreed upon by all, not disputed, such that it is a defect according to some and not others, and with that the defect is issued by one known for sincerity without bigotry, because the bigots have corrupted the religion much, and they make the disliked forbidden and the recommended obligatory, so the criticism of these deficient ones is not considered. Thus even criticism by tadlis is not accepted. Tadlis linguistically is concealing a defect of merchandise from the buyer, and in the terminology of the hadith scholars: concealing detail in the chain by saying 'So-and-so narrated from so-and-so' etc., without saying: He did not act upon it. Al-Tahawi narrated from Abu Musa that his school is obligation of wudu from laughing out loud. Thus said al-Ali al-Qari. (Al-Qamar) That: i.e., the non-action of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari on that hadith. (Al-Qamar) It does not impugn etc. because integrity is a basis for every Muslim in view of reason and religion, especially the early period. So the hadith is not abandoned due to ambiguous criticism, because it is possible that the criticizer believes what is not a defect in reality to be a defect. So for the acceptance of criticism, its specification is necessary. (Al-Qamar) Or munkar. And said Bahr al-Ulum Mawlana Abd al-Ali: Indeed, the criticism that the narrator is according to all imams of hadith abandoned in hadith, or that his hadith is according to the imams of hadith munkar, is explicit criticism, so it impugns the narrator absolutely. Then know that the imams of hadith only write in their books absolute criticism. This criticism is not ambiguous, but its reason is known to them, though they do not state it out of modesty and chivalry. Sometimes they also state the reason for the criticism, such as saying: 'He is a liar and a fabricator of hadith,' and the like. And the munkar hadith is one narrated by a person who is not precise, having moved away from the degree of precision, as said by Ibn al-Salah, and it has other definitions mentioned in usul al-hadith. (Al-Qamar) And the like: such as saying 'He is criticized.' (Al-Qamar) According to some not others, like the criticism of a Hanafi against a Shafi'i for eating meat on which the name of Allah was deliberately omitted, for his school permits it. (Al-Qamar) From one known etc.: i.e., being free from selfishness and a sincere adviser to religion. (Al-Qamar) Because the bigots etc.: i.e., those whose habit is to be strict until they consider a small defect as great, and they designate a defect in what is not a defect, like Ibn al-Jawzi and his likes. (Al-Qamar) So that it is not accepted etc. This is a branching from that only agreed-upon criticism is accepted.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary explaining the rules for accepting or rejecting hadith based on criticism and the actions of the Companions. The text first addresses the example of the hadith regarding flogging and exile for an unmarried fornicator. The Hanafi school argues that the exile mentioned in the hadith was not part of the hadd punishment but rather a discretionary policy by Caliph Umar, as evidenced by his later oath to never exile anyone. This shows that a Companion's action contrary to a clear hadith does not necessarily invalidate the hadith; instead, it indicates abrogation or policy, as long as the hadith is apparent and not subtle. The passage then transitions to the concept of 'ambiguous criticism' (طعن مبهم) from hadith scholars. According to Hanafis, such vague statements like 'this hadith is criticized' or 'this narrator is munkar' do not impugn the reliability of a narrator unless the criticism is explicitly explained and agreed upon by all. The reason is that integrity is the default for every Muslim, and ambiguous criticism may arise from bias or misunderstanding. Therefore, only explicit criticism from a sincere, non-bigoted source is accepted. The commentary also defines 'tadlis' (concealing flaws in the chain) and 'munkar' hadith, emphasizing that these are not accepted as valid criticism without detail. The overall Hanafi position is to preserve the presumption of integrity and to require clear evidence before rejecting a narrator or hadith.

Key Terms
النفي (al-nafy): Exile from one's town as a punishment; in this context, refers to the banishment of a fornicator for a year.
الحد (al-hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law for certain crimes, cannot be changed or reduced.
السياسة (al-siyasa): Discretionary policy or public interest-based ruling by the ruler, not a fixed legal punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what does Caliph Umar's oath not to exile anyone after the Rabi'ah incident indicate?
A) Umar rejected the hadith of exile.
B) Umar considered exile a discretionary policy, not a fixed hadd.
C) Umar forgot the hadith due to old age.
D) Umar intended to enforce the hadith differently.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses Companion action to interpret clear hadiths as indicating abrogation or discretionary policy, not as rejection of the hadith.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Hanafi Rule on Ambiguous Criticism of Hadith Narrators (الطعن المبهم)
Explaining Hanafi conditions for accepting narrator criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which ambiguous criticism of a narrator is accepted in the Hanafi school, and distinguish between accepted and rejected forms of criticism.

Core Idea
Ambiguous criticism from hadith scholars does not impugn a narrator unless it is explicit, agreed upon, and from a sincere critic.

This lesson focuses on the Hanafi position regarding vague criticism (الطعن المبهم) of hadith narrators. While some schools accept general remarks like 'this narrator is weak', the Hanafi school requires explicit explanation and consensus. We will explore the rationale based on the presumption of integrity in every Muslim, especially early Muslims, and the potential for bias. The lesson also covers related concepts like tadlis and munkar.

Guided Path
1
Define ambiguous criticism
Explain that it is vague, unspecified criticism like 'this hadith is criticized' or 'this narrator is munkar'.
Ambiguous criticism leaves doubt about the exact defect.
2
State the Hanafi rule
Ambiguous criticism does not impugn the narrator (لا يجرح الراوي).
The default is integrity (عدالة أصل).
3
List the conditions for acceptance
The criticism must be explicit (مفسر), agreed upon by all (متفق عليه), not disputed, and from a critic known for sincerity without bigotry.
If disputed, it is not accepted; if from a bigot, it is rejected.
4
Apply the rule to examples
Show that criticism like 'he is munkar' is not accepted unless clarified and agreed; also reject criticism from biased scholars.
Tadlis is a form of ambiguous criticism and is not accepted.
5
Differentiate between explicit and ambiguous
Note that if an imam says 'he is a liar' that is explicit; but if they only say 'he is criticized' it is ambiguous.
Explicit criticism must be specific about the defect.

Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary explaining the rules for accepting or rejecting hadith based on criticism and the actions of the Companions. The text first addresses the example of the hadith regarding flogging and exile for an unmarried fornicator. The Hanafi school argues that the exile mentioned in the hadith was not part of the hadd punishment but rather a discretionary policy by Caliph Umar, as evidenced by his later oath to never exile anyone. This shows that a Companion's action contrary to a clear hadith does not necessarily invalidate the hadith; instead, it indicates abrogation or policy, as long as the hadith is apparent and not subtle. The passage then transitions to the concept of 'ambiguous criticism' (طعن مبهم) from hadith scholars. According to Hanafis, such vague statements like 'this hadith is criticized' or 'this narrator is munkar' do not impugn the reliability of a narrator unless the criticism is explicitly explained and agreed upon by all. The reason is that integrity is the default for every Muslim, and ambiguous criticism may arise from bias or misunderstanding. Therefore, only explicit criticism from a sincere, non-bigoted source is accepted. The commentary also defines 'tadlis' (concealing flaws in the chain) and 'munkar' hadith, emphasizing that these are not accepted as valid criticism without detail. The overall Hanafi position is to preserve the presumption of integrity and to require clear evidence before rejecting a narrator or hadith.

Key Terms
الطعن المبهم (al-taʿn al-mubham): Vague criticism of a hadith or narrator without specifying the reason, such as saying 'this hadith is criticized' or 'this narrator is munkar'
التدليس (al-tadlis): Concealing a defect in the chain of transmission by saying 'So-and-so narrated from so-and-so' without specifying that they did not directly meet
المنكر (al-munkar): A hadith narrated by a person who lacks precision (ضابط) and is far from the degree of reliability

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a condition for accepting criticism of a narrator?
A) The critic must be a famous scholar.
B) The criticism must be agreed upon by all scholars.
C) The criticism must mention the word 'weak'.
D) The criticism must be from a student of the narrator.

Key Takeaway
Ambiguous criticism does not impugn a narrator; explicit, agreed-upon criticism from a sincere scholar is required to overturn the presumption of integrity.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

Preference of Prohibitory Over Permissive When Texts Conflict
Explains the rule of preference for prohibitory over permissive texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of preferring the prohibitory text (hazir) over the permissive (mubih) when they conflict, and justify it using the principles of ibaha asl or ihtiyat.

Core Idea
When prohibitory and permissive texts conflict, the prohibitory prevails to avoid repeated abrogation or as a precaution.

Earlier in the text, we saw how conflicting analogies in the 'iddah case are resolved by naskh. Now the discussion moves to a more general usul rule: when a prohibitory text and a permissive text conflict and their chronological order is unknown, the Hanafi school gives precedence to the prohibitory. This lesson unpacks the rationale behind that rule, including the concept of original permissibility (ibaha asl) and the alternative justification of precaution (ihtiyat).

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting texts
Determine which text is prohibitory (hazir) and which is permissive (mubih) in the given ruling. For example, in the hadith example, the general prohibition of prayer at certain times is hazir, and the exception for Mecca is mubih.
The conflict is between the general prohibition and the specific permission.
2
Check if naskh is possible
If the historical order of the texts is known, the later text abrogates the earlier. If not, apply the rule of preference. In the hadith example, both are from the Prophet, so naskh is not easily determined.
When order is unknown, the rule of hazir vs mubih applies.
3
Apply the rule: prefer the hazir
Give precedence to the prohibitory text. According to the Hanafi position, this avoids the need for multiple abrogations (if ibaha asl is considered a divine ruling) or is simply a precaution (ihtiyat) because refraining from the prohibited is obligatory.
The justifications differ, but the outcome is the same.
4
Justify with ibaha asl or ihtiyat
Explain that permissibility (ibaha) is the original state of things based on Quran 2:29. If we follow the mubih, we would need two abrogations; following the hazir needs only one. Alternatively, the precautionary approach: leaving the permissible has no sin, but doing the prohibited is sinful.
The commentary notes that the precautionary justification is stronger.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التعارض بيان وقوع التعارض بين القياسين فعليه يقول: تعتد بأبعد الأجلين احتياطا، أي إن كان وضع الحمل من قريب تعتدّ أربعة أشهر وعشراً، وإن كان وضع الحمل من بعيد تعتدّ به لعدم العلم بالتاريخ، وابن مسعود رضي الله عنه يقول: تعتد بوضع الحمل، وقال محتجاً على علي عليه السلام: من شاء باهلته أن سورة النساء القُصرى أعني سورة الطلاق التي فيها قوله: ﴿وَأُولاتُ الْأَحْمَالِ نزلت بعد التي في سورة البقرة، فلما علم التاريخ كان قوله: ﴿وَأُولاتُ الْأَحْمَالِ أَجَلُهُنَّ أَنْ يَضَعْنَ حَمْلَهُنَّ﴾ ناسخا لقوله: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنْكُمْ﴾ في قدر ما تناولاه، فيعمل به، وهكذا قال عمر رضي الله عنه لو وضعت وزوجها على سرير لانقضت عدتها، وحلّ لها أن تتزوج، وبه أخذ أبو حنيفة رحمه الله والشافعي رضي الله عنه جميعا. أو دلالةً، عطف على قوله: صريحا أي من قبل اختلاف الزمان دلالةً كالحاظر والمبيح فإنهما إذا اجتمعا في حكم يعملون على الحاظر، ويجعلونه مؤخرًا دلالة عن المبيح، وذلك؛ لأن الإباحة أصل في الأشياء فلو عملنا بالمحرم كان النص المبيح موافقا للإباحة الأصلية واجتمعتا، ثم يكون النص المحرم ناسخا للإباحتين معًا، وهو معقول، بخلاف ما إذا عملنا بالمبيح؛ لأنه حينئذ يكون النص المحرم ناسخًا للإباحة الأصلية، ثم يكون النص المبيح ناسخًا للمحرم، فيلزم تكرار النسخ، وهو غير معقول، وهذا أصل كبير لنا يتفرّع عليه كثير من الأحكام، وهذا على قول من جعل الإباحة أصلاً في الأشياء، وقيل: الحرمة أصل فيها، وقيل: التوقف أولى وذلك: أي العلم بالحاظر وجعله مؤخرًا عن المبيح. (المحشي) أصل في الأشياء: لقوله تعالى: ﴿ خَلَقَ لَكُمْ مَا فِي الْأَرْضِ جَمِيعا﴾ (البقرة: ۲۹) (القمر) واجتمعتا: أي النص المبيح والإباحة الأصلية.(القمر) ناسخا إلخ هذا موقوف على أن الإباحة الأصلية حكم شرعي، وأما إذا كانت بمعنى عدم الحرج في الفعل والترك بسبب فقد الحكم الشرعي فلا يكون الحاظر المقدّم ناسخا؛ لأن النسخ عبارة عن انتهاء حكم شرعي، بل مثبتا للحظر ابتداءً، فلا يلزم تكرار النسخ. نعم، يلزم تكرار التغيّر، فالأولى أن يقول : إذا تعارض الحاظر والمبيح يُعمل بالحاظر احتياطا؛ لأن الكف عن المحرم واجب ولا مؤاخذة في ترك المباح ومثاله: ما روى أبو داود أنه قال أبو ذر : سمعت رسول الله عليه الصلاة والسلام يقول : لا صلاة بعد الصبح حتى تطلع الشمس، ولا بعد العصر حتى تغرب الشمس إلا بمكة، فهذا الحديث مبيح للصلاة بعد العصر في مكة، ويعارضه حديث ظاهر رواه الترمذي عن عقبة بن عامر : ثلاث ساعات نهانا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن نصلي فيهن وأن تقبر فيهن موتانا حين تطلع الشمس بازغة حتى ترتفع، وحين تقوم قائم الظهيرة حتى تميل الشمس، وحين تتضَيَّفُ للغروب حتى تغرب، فعملنا بهذا المحرم. (القمر) النسخ: فيكون الشيء ناسخًا مرّةً ومنسوخا مرّةً أخرى. (المحشي) وهذا: أي أن الحاظر والمبيح إذا اجتمعا يعمل بالحاظر. (القمر) وهذا على قول من إلخ قلت: وجه لزوم تكرار النسخ اعترض عليه الإمام فخر الإسلام بأن هذا موقوف على كون الإباحة أصلاً، ونحن لا نقول به، فإن الإنسان لم يُترك سدًى، فلا إباحة أصلاً حتى يقرّره المبيح أو ينسخه المحرم، فالأحسن في التوجيه أن يقال: فيه الاحتياط، فإنه لو كان المقدّم المحرم والمتأخر المبيح ففي الاجتناب عنه لا حرج ولا ذنب بخلاف عكسه، فإنه لو عمل بالإباحة وقع في الحرج، وهو منقول عن أمير المؤمنين علي عليه السلام في مسألة الجمع بين الأختين بملك اليمين، بحر العلوم (السنبلي) وقيل الحرمة إلخ القائل بعض المعتزلة، وفيه: أنه إن أراد العقاب على الانتفاع به فباطل؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا كُنَّا مُعَذِّبِينَ حَتَّى نَبْعَثَ رَسُولاً﴾ (الإسراء: ١٥) تأمل. قالوا: إن الأشياء مملوكة لله تعالى، والتصرف في ملك الغير لا يجوز إلا بإذنه، قلنا: إن التصرف في ملك الغير إذا لم يضره جاز كالاستصباح مصباح رجل، والاستطلال بظل جدار رجل.(القمر) وقيل التوقف أولى: لأن العقل لاحظ له في معرفة الأحكام فليتوقف فيه إلى أن يرد الشرع بالإباحة والحرمة. (القمر)
Chapter on conflict. Explanation of the occurrence of conflict between two analogies. So he says: She observes 'iddah by the longer of the two periods as a precaution, meaning if the delivery of the pregnancy is soon, she observes 'iddah of four months and ten days, and if the delivery of the pregnancy is far, she observes 'iddah by it due to lack of knowledge of the date. Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) says: She observes 'iddah by delivery. And he argued against Ali (peace be upon him): Whoever wishes, I will imprecate him that Surah an-Nisa al-Qusra, meaning Surah at-Talaq which contains His words: 'And those who are pregnant...' was revealed after that which is in Surah al-Baqarah. When the history became known, His words: 'And those who are pregnant... their term is that they give birth' abrogated His words: 'And those who die among you' to the extent that they covered, so it is acted upon. And thus Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said: If she gives birth while her husband is on the bier, her 'iddah ends and it becomes permissible for her to marry. And Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) and al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him) both adopted this. Or by indication, coordinated with his saying: explicitly, i.e., due to difference of time by indication, like the prohibitory and the permissive, for when they come together in a ruling, they act upon the prohibitory and make it later by indication over the permissive. And that is because permissibility is the original state in things. If we act upon the prohibitory, the permissive text agrees with the original permissibility and they combine, then the prohibitory text abrogates both permissions together, which is reasonable. Unlike if we act upon the permissive, because then the prohibitory text abrogates the original permissibility, then the permissive text abrogates the prohibitory, so repeated abrogation becomes necessary, which is unreasonable. And this is a great principle for us from which many rulings derive. And this is according to the one who considers permissibility as original in things. And it is said: prohibition is original in them. And it is said: suspension is better. That is: knowledge of the prohibitory and making it later than the permissive. (Al-Muhashi) Original in things: due to His saying: 'He created for you all that is in the earth' (al-Baqarah 29). (Al-Qamar) They combined: meaning the permissive text and the original permissibility. (Al-Qamar) Abrogating etc.: This depends on the original permissibility being a divine ruling. But if it is in the sense of no harm in doing or leaving due to absence of divine ruling, then the prioritized prohibitory does not abrogate, because abrogation is the termination of a divine ruling; rather, it establishes the prohibition initially, so repeated abrogation does not become necessary. Yes, repeated change becomes necessary. So it is better to say: When the prohibitory and permissive conflict, act upon the prohibitory as a precaution, because refraining from the prohibited is obligatory and there is no blame in leaving the permissible. Its example: What Abu Dawud narrated that Abu Dharr said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) say: 'No prayer after the dawn until the sun rises, and no prayer after the afternoon until the sun sets except in Mecca.' So this hadith permits prayer after the afternoon in Mecca. And it is opposed by a clear hadith narrated by al-Tirmidhi from Uqba ibn Amir: 'Three hours that the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) forbade us from praying in them and from burying our dead in them: when the sun rises until it rises high, and when the sun is at its zenith until it declines, and when it inclines towards setting until it sets.' So we act upon this prohibitory. (Al-Qamar) Abrogation: a thing is abrogating once and abrogated once. (Al-Muhashi) This: meaning that when the prohibitory and permissive come together, act upon the prohibitory. (Al-Qamar) This is according to the one etc. I say: The aspect of necessity of repeated abrogation was objected to by Imam Fakhr al-Islam on the grounds that this depends on permissibility being original, and we do not hold that, for man was not left neglected; there is no permissibility at all for the permissive to establish or the prohibitory to abrogate. So the better justification is to say: there is precaution in it, for if the prohibitory is prioritized and the permissive is later, then in abstaining there is no hardship or sin, contrary to its opposite, for if one acts upon the permissive, he falls into hardship. And this is transmitted from the Commander of the Faithful Ali (peace be upon him) in the issue of combining two sisters by right hand possession. (Al-Sunbuli) And it is said: prohibition etc. The one who says that is some of the Mu'tazila. And therein: if he intends punishment for benefiting from it, it is false due to His saying: 'And We were not to punish until We send a messenger' (al-Isra 15). Reflect. They said: Things are owned by Allah Almighty, and disposing of the property of another is not permissible except with his permission. We say: Disposing of the property of another if it does not harm him is permissible, like lighting a lamp from a man's lamp, and benefiting from the shade of a man's wall. (Al-Qamar) And it is said: Suspension is better, because reason has no role in knowing the rulings, so one should suspend judgment until the law comes with permissibility and prohibition. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul discusses the rule when a prohibitory textual evidence (hazir) and a permissive (mubih) conflict in a specific ruling. The author begins by illustrating the concept with the example of the pregnant widow's 'iddah: there is a conflict between two analogies—one based on the verse of 'iddah for widows (four months and ten days) and the other on the verse for pregnant women (until delivery). The correct view, according to the Hanafis and Shafi'is, is that the later verse (Surah Talaq) abrogates the earlier (Surah Baqarah), so the 'iddah ends with delivery. This is an example of conflict between texts resolved by naskh. The author then transitions to the general principle: if a prohibitory and permissive text conflict and we know which one is later, we apply the later; but if not, we give precedence to the prohibitory based on the reasoning that permissibility is the original state of things (ibaha asliyya). If we were to follow the permissive text, it would require the prohibitory text to abrogate the original permissibility, and then the permissive text to abrogate the prohibitory—two abrogations, which is irrational. Following the prohibitory requires only one abrogation. The commentary (al-Muhashi, al-Qamar) challenges this by noting that original permissibility is not a divine ruling subject to abrogation; rather, it is the absence of ruling. Therefore, the prohibitory text simply establishes a prohibition, and no abrogation occurs. The better justification is precaution (ihtiyat): refraining from what is prohibited is obligatory, while leaving the permissible has no sin. An example is given from hadith: the general prohibition of prayer after Asr is qualified by the exception of Mecca. The prohibitory general prohibition is given precedence over the permissive exception in cases of conflict regarding non-Mecca times, but for Mecca, the permissive applies. The passage ends with a note that this rule applies according to those who hold permissibility as original; some say prohibition is original (Mu'tazila), and some prefer tawaqquf. The Hanafi position is the first, though the better justification is precaution.

Key Terms
الحاظر (al-hazir): The prohibitory textual evidence (such as a command of prohibition).
المبيح (al-mubih): The permissive textual evidence (such as a command of permissibility).
الإباحة الأصلية (al-ibaha al-asliyya): The original state of permissibility in all things before any divine ruling.
النسخ (al-naskh): The abrogation of a divine ruling by a later divine ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle discussed, when a prohibitory (hazir) and permissive (mubih) text conflict and their historical order is unknown, which text is given precedence?
A) The permissive (mubih)
B) The prohibitory (hazir)
C) Both are abandoned
D) Tawaqquf (suspension)

Key Takeaway
When a prohibitory and permissive text conflict and order is unknown, the Hanafi school prefers the prohibitory, justified primarily by precaution (ihtiyat) since refraining from the prohibited is obligatory and there is no penalty for leaving a permissible act.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Affirmer is Preferable to the Negator: A Key Usul Rule
Explains the usul rule that the affirmer (muthbit) takes precedence over the negator (nafi).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule 'al-muthbit awla min al-nafi' by identifying which evidence constitutes an affirmer or negator in meaning, and evaluate the dispute between al-Karkhi and Ibn Aban.

Core Idea
The affirmer adds knowledge; the negator only maintains the status quo.

When two pieces of evidence conflict, one affirming a temporary ruling and the other negating it, which takes precedence? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi usul principle that the affirmer (al-muthbit) is preferred over the negator (al-nafi), not because of wording but because it provides additional knowledge (ziyadat 'ilm). We'll examine the positions of al-Karkhi and Ibn Aban, and learn to distinguish between literal and legal meanings of affirmation and negation.

Guided Path
1
Define the terms
State the definitions of muthbit and nafi as given in the text: muthbit establishes an additional accidental ruling not previously present; nafi negates the additional ruling and keeps the original.
The text emphasizes that these are based on legal meaning, not wording.
2
Identify the dispute
Note the disagreement: al-Karkhi holds that the muthbit is always preferable; Ibn Aban and Qadi Abd al-Jabbar hold they are equal and then one must resort to tarjih based on narrator reliability.
The Hanafi imams sometimes acted by muthbit, sometimes by nafi, prompting the need for a rule.
3
Understand the nuance of meaning
Recognize that classification depends on meaning, not the presence of a negative particle. Example: 'I returned the deposit' negates liability (nafi in meaning); 'I did not return the deposit' affirms liability (muthbit in meaning).
Al-'ibrah li al-ma'na, not li al-lafz.
4
Apply the rule to scenarios
Practice identifying muthbit and nafi in given scenarios and then applying the rule of preference according to al-Karkhi.
Remember: the affirmer always wins in the Hanafi view.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: in cases like the option of emancipation or marriage of a Muhrim, preferring muthbit or nafi leads to different rulings.
Later lessons will discuss specific cases.

وأصحاب الشافعي
وعند ابن أبان يتعارضان أي يتساويان، فبعد ذلك يُصار إلى الترجيح بحال الراوي،
في العدالة والإتقان
والمراد بالمثبت ما يثبت أمرًا عارضا زائدا لم يكن ثابتا فيما مضى، وبالنافي ما ينفي الأمر
الزائد ويبقيه على الأصل، ولما وقع الاختلاف بين الكرخي وابن أبان، ووقع الاختلاف في عمل أصحابنا أيضًا، ففي بعض المواضع يعملون بالمثبت وفي بعضها بالنافي أشار المصنف له إلى قاعدة في ذلك ترفع الخلاف عنهم، فقال:
وقد طَوّلتُ الكلام إلخ حيث قال بعد ذكر المذاهب: إن جعل المحرم ناسحًا بناء هي قول من جعل الإباحة أصلاً في الأشياء كالكرخي وأبي بكر الرازي وطائفة من فقهاء الحنفية والشافعية وجمهور المعتزلة، ولسنا نقول بكون الإباحة أصلاً في الوضع؛ لأن عباد الله تعالى لم يتركوا مُهملاً في شيء من الزمان، ولو كان الإباحة أصلاً لكانوا مهملين غير مكلفين، وإنما جعل المبيح أصلاً والمحرم ناسحًا بناء على زمان الفترة بين عيسى ومحمد عليهما السلام قبل شريعتنا، فإنه كان الإباحة أصلاً حينئذ، ثم بعث نبينا عليه، فبين الأشياء المحرمة وبقي ما سواها حلالاً مباحًا، كذا في حواشي البزدوي. (القمر) أولى إلخ لاشتماله على زيادة علم (القمر) بما سبق: أي بما ذكره من وجوه المخلص عن المعارضة. (القمر) وعند ابن أبان والقاضي عبد الجبار من المعتزلة. (القمر) يتعارضان لاستوائهما في شرائط صحة الخبر أي العقل والضبط والإسلام والعدالة. (القمر)
يصار إلى الترجيح إلخ وإن لم يكن الترجيح فيطرحان ويرجع المجتهد إلى أدلة أخرى.(القمر) والمراد بالمثبت :إلخ لما كان المتبادر من المثبت ما لا يكون مشتملا على حرف السلب، ومن النافي ما اشتمل عليه، وليس الأمر كذلك شرعًا، فإن العبرة للمعنى ألا ترى أن المودع إذا قال: رددت الوديعة" يكون هذا نفيًا للضمان على المودع وإن كان إثباتًا لفظًا، وقول المودع: "ما رددت الوديعة" إثبات للضمان بسبب حبس الوديعة
عنده في الحال وإن كان نفيًا لفظاً، فأشار الشارح إلى أنه ليس المراد ما هو المتبادر ، بل المراد بالمثبت إلخ. (القمر) في عمل أصحابنا يعني أبا حنيفة وأبا يوسف ومحمد أبا حنيفة وأبا يوسف ومحمد صله. (القمر) ففي بعض المواضع إلخ كما في مسألة
خيار العتق على ما سيجيء. (القمر) وفي بعضها كما في مسألة جواز نكاح المحرم على ما سيجيء.(القمر)
Chapter on Conflict. Explanation of conflict between two qiyas. Until evidence of permission or prohibition is established. And I have elaborated on it in the tafsir 'al-Ahmadi'. And 'the affirmer is preferable to the negator' is an independent rule, not related to what preceded. Meaning, when the affirmer and negator conflict, the affirmer is more worthy of being acted upon than the negator according to al-Karkhi. And the companions of al-Shafi'i. And according to Ibn Aban, they conflict, i.e., they are equal; then after that one resorts to tarjih based on the state of the narrator in reliability and precision. And the meaning of 'affirmer' (al-muthbit) is that which establishes an additional accidental matter that was not established previously, and 'negator' (al-nafi) is that which negates the additional matter and keeps it upon the original. When disagreement occurred between al-Karkhi and Ibn Aban, and disagreement also occurred in the practice of our scholars, so in some places they act by the affirmer and in some by the negator, the author pointed to a rule in that which removes disagreement from them, saying: And I have elaborated etc., where he said after mentioning the schools: That making the prohibiter abrogating is built upon the opinion of those who make ibaha original in things, like al-Karkhi, Abu Bakr al-Razi, a group of Hanafi and Shafi'i jurists, and most Mu'tazila. And we do not say that ibaha is original in the beginning, because the servants of Allah were never left neglected at any time; and if ibaha were original, they would be neglected and not obligated. Rather, we make the permiter original and the prohibiter abrogating based on the time of the interregnum between Jesus and Muhammad (peace be upon them) before our Shari'a, for then ibaha was original. Then our Prophet was sent, and he explained the prohibited things, and the rest remained lawful and permissible. Thus in the glosses of al-Bazdawi. (Al-Qamar) 'Prefereable' because it includes an increase of knowledge. (Al-Qamar) 'With what preceded': i.e., with what he mentioned of ways of salvation from conflict. (Al-Qamar) 'And according to Ibn Aban and al-Qadi Abd al-Jabbar from the Mu'tazila.' (Al-Qamar) 'They conflict due to equality in the conditions of the soundness of the report, i.e., reason, precision, Islam, and uprightness.' (Al-Qamar) 'One resorts to tarjih etc. And if no tarjih, they are both set aside and the mujtahid returns to other evidences.' (Al-Qamar) 'And the meaning of affirmer etc. Because the immediate understanding of affirmer is that which does not contain a negative particle, and of negator is that which contains it. But the matter is not so legally, for consideration is given to meaning. Do you not see that the depositary, if he says: 'I returned the deposit', this is a negation of liability from the depositary even though it is affirmation in wording; and the depositary's saying 'I did not return the deposit' is an affirmation of the liability for detaining the deposit pending at that moment even though it is negation in wording. Thus the expositor indicated that the intended meaning is not the immediate understanding, but the intended meaning is as described.' (Al-Qamar) 'In the practice of our scholars' meaning Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them. (Al-Qamar) 'So in some places they act by the affirmer, as in the issue of the option of emancipation, as will come; and in some places by the negator, as in the issue of the lawfulness of the marriage of a Muhrim, as will come.' (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage introduces an independent usul rule: al-muthbit awla min al-nafi (the affirmer is preferable to the negator). It is independent of the previous discussion on hazir and mubih. The rule applies when there is conflict between two evidences: one that affirms an additional temporary ruling (al-muthbit) and one that negates it (al-nafi). The affirmer is considered preferable because it adds knowledge (ziyadat 'ilm). The text reports a disagreement: al-Karkhi (a leading Hanafi usuli) holds that the affirmer is always preferable, while Ibn Aban (a Shafi'i usuli) and Qadi Abd al-Jabbar (Mu'tazili) hold that the two are equal, and then one must resort to tarjih based on the narrator's reliability. The passage also clarifies the technical meaning of muthbit and nafi: the affirmer is not necessarily the one with no negative particle; rather, it is about the meaning (al-'ibrah li al-ma'na). For example, the depositary saying 'I returned the deposit' is literally affirmative but actually negates liability (so it is nafi in meaning), while saying 'I did not return the deposit' is literally negative but affirms liability (so it is muthbit in meaning). The passage then notes that the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) sometimes acted by the affirmer and sometimes by the negator in specific cases (like option of emancipation and marriage of a Muhrim), indicating that a general rule was needed to remove inconsistency. The author (likely al-Bazdawi or his commentator) hints at such a rule.

Key Terms
المثبت (al-muthbit): An evidence that establishes an additional accidental ruling that was not previously present.
النافي (al-nafi): An evidence that negates the additional ruling and keeps the original state.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): Weighing one evidence over another using external criteria (narrator reliability, etc.) when they are otherwise equal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Aban, what should be done when a muthbit and a nafi evidence conflict?
A) The muthbit is always preferred.
B) They are considered equal and then tarjih is used based on narrator reliability.
C) The nafi is always preferred.
D) Both are rejected and the mujtahid follows his personal opinion.

Key Takeaway
The rule 'al-muthbit awla min al-nafi' guides a mujtahid to prefer the evidence that provides additional knowledge, defined by meaning not wording.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

Defining the Affirmer and Negator: The Rule of Preference
Defining muthbit/nafi and stating al-Karkhi's unconditional preference rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of muthbit and nafi in Hanafi usul and explain the basic rule that the affirmer is preferred over the negator according to al-Karkhi.

Core Idea
The affirmer is preferred because it adds knowledge, but only if the negator lacks evidentiary basis.

In usul al-fiqh, when two reports or evidences conflict, a key principle is that the one affirming an additional matter is preferred over the one simply denying it. But this principle is not absolute; its application depends on the nature of the negation. This lesson introduces the definitions of muthbit and nafi based on legal effect, and presents the foundational rule as articulated by al-Karkhi.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context of conflict
The rule is invoked when there is a conflict (ta'arud) between an affirming evidence and a denying evidence. Identify the scenario where both cannot be acted upon simultaneously.
2
Define the affirmer (muthbit)
The affirmer is that which establishes an incidental additional attribute that was not previously established. It is defined by its legal effect, not its literal wording.
Example: 'I returned the deposit' is negatory in effect though affirmative in wording.
3
Define the negator (nafi)
The negator is that which denies the additional attribute and keeps the matter on its original state. Again, defined by effect, not wording.
Example: 'I did not return the deposit' is affirmative in effect though negative in wording.
4
State al-Karkhi's rule
According to al-Karkhi, the affirmer is preferred and acted upon first when it conflicts with a negator. This is based on the idea that the affirmer always has evidentiary basis, while the negator may lack it.
This unconditional preference is the starting point.

Section on contradiction. Explanation of the occurrence of contradiction between two analogies. ... until the evidence of permissibility or prohibition is established. And I have elaborated on it in the commentary 'al-Ahmadi'. And the affirmer is more deserving than the negator. This is an independent principle with no connection to what preceded, meaning if the affirmer and negator conflict, then the affirmer is more deserving of being acted upon than the negator according to al-Karkhi. And the followers of al-Shafi'i. And according to Ibn Aban, they conflict, i.e., they are equal, then after that, preference is given based on the state of the narrator in terms of reliability and precision. And what is meant by the affirmer is that which affirms an incidental additional matter that was not previously established, and by the negator is that which negates the additional matter and keeps it on its original state. Since there was a disagreement between al-Karkhi and Ibn Aban, and there was also disagreement in the practice of our scholars, for in some instances they act on the affirmer and in some instances on the negator, the author pointed to a rule in this regard that removes the disagreement from them. He said: And I have elaborated on it etc. ... The principle: The negator, if it is of the type that is known by its evidence, ...
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the usul principle regarding contradiction between an affirmer (muthbit) and a negator (nafi). The author explains the positions of early Hanafi scholars: al-Karkhi (followed by Shafi'is) holds that the affirmer is preferred and acted upon first, while Ibn Aban holds that they are equal and require external preference (tarjih) based on the narrator's reliability. The commentary resolves the apparent conflict in Hanafi practice by stating that the preferred ruling depends on whether the negator is based on evidence or on mere istishab (presumption of continuity). Two scenarios are identified: (1) if the negator is known by a clear evidence or its state is ambiguous but the narrator is known to have relied on evidence, then it is like the affirmer and they conflict, requiring tarjih—this aligns with Ibn Aban. (2) If the negator is not of that type and is based on mere istishab (which is not a valid proof), then the affirmer is preferred without conflict—this aligns with al-Karkhi. Thus the Hanafi school actually combines both views by conditioning the rule. The commentary also provides the definition of muthbit and nafi based on legal effect, not literal wording, citing the example of a depositary's statement.

Key Terms
المثبت (al-muthbit): That which affirms an incidental additional matter that was not previously established.
النافي (al-nafi): That which negates the additional matter and keeps it on its original state.
التعارض (al-ta'arud): Conflict between two evidences that are equal in terms of conditions of validity, requiring preference or external resolution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what defines an 'affirmer' (muthbit) in a legal report?
A) Its literal wording includes a positive statement
B) Its legal effect establishes an additional attribute
C) It comes from a more reliable narrator
D) It is based on istishab

Key Takeaway
The affirmer is preferred over the negator only when the negator is not based on evidence; otherwise both conflict and require external preference.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
The Ikhtilaf Between al-Karkhi and Ibn Aban and the Hanafi Resolution
Resolving the ikhtilaf between al-Karkhi and Ibn Aban by conditioning the rule on the negator's evidentiary basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the positions of al-Karkhi and Ibn Aban, and apply the conditional Hanafi rule to determine when the affirmer is preferred.

Core Idea
The negator is equal to the affirmer only if it is based on evidence; otherwise the affirmer prevails.

The simple rule 'the affirmer is preferred' faces a challenge from Ibn Aban, who argued that if both sides come from reliable narrators, they are equal. This lesson explores that ikhtilaf and how the Hanafi school resolved it through a conditional rule. Understanding this resolution is essential for correctly analyzing conflicting reports in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Recall al-Karkhi's unconditional rule
Al-Karkhi holds that the affirmer is always preferred. This is the starting view.
2
Introduce Ibn Aban's objection
Ibn Aban argues that if the negator is also based on a valid evidence (e.g., a reliable hadith), then both are equal and we must seek external tarjih based on narrator qualities.
He assumes both sides meet the conditions of a valid report: rationality, precision, Islam, reliability.
3
Understand the Hanafi resolution
The commentary resolves that there are two scenarios: (1) If the negator is known by evidence or its narrator is known to rely on evidence, then it conflicts with the affirmer (Ibn Aban applies). (2) If the negator is based on mere istishab (presumption) or its basis is unknown and the narrator relied on apparent presumption, then the affirmer is preferred (al-Karkhi applies).
Thus the Hanafi school combines both views conditionally.
4
Apply to examples
The source mentions two examples: the option of emancipation (khiyar al-ataq) and the validity of marriage by a pilgrim. In the first, the negator is evidence-based, so they conflict; in the second, the negator is istishab-based, so the affirmer prevails.
These examples show the practical thamarah al-khilaf.

الراوي النفي

فيه أي في تعارض المثبت والنافي. (القمر) على الاستصحاب أي الإبقاء على ما كان عليه. (القمر) يشتبه حاله إلخ معنى اشتباه الحال أنه يعرف تارة بالدليل وتارة بالأصل. (السنبلي) هاتين الصورتين إلخ أي في صورة كونه من جنس ما يعرف بدليله وفي صورة كونه مشتبه الحال. قوله: مثل الإثبات إلخ، يعني كان النفي مثل الإثبات، فيتعارضان كلاهما أي النفي والإثبات ويطلب الترجيح لأحدهما خارج ليندفع التعارض ، وقوله : "وإلا" "فلا" معناه إن لم يكن النفي من أحد القسمين المذكورين، فلا يكون النفي مثل الإثبات، وهكذا إذا كان النفي مشتبه الحال لكن لا يعرف أن الراوي اعتمد دليل المعرفة، ولما لم يكن النفي مثل الإثبات فلا تعارض بينهما ، بل الإثبات يكون مرجّحا ؛ لأنه أولى لكونه ثابتًا بالدليل. (السنبلي) إلى دفعه أي بالترجيح من وجه آخر (القمر) مذهب ابن أبان أي ثبوت التعارض بين المثبت والنافي والرجوع إلى الترجيح، وقال ابن الملك: إن ابن أبان كان من أصحاب الحديث ثم غلب عليه الرأي، تفقه على محمد بن الحسن، وكان موته سنة إحدى وعشرين ومائتين. (القمر) فلا يكون إلخ لأنه لا دليل على النفي، بل هو مبني على الاستصحاب الذي ليس بحجة. (القمر) مذهب الكرخي: أي ترجيح المثبت على النافي، قال ابن الملك: إن الكرخي ولد سنة ستين ومائتين، ومات سنة أربعين وثلاث مائة (القمر) مثالين أحدهما ما إذا كان النفي من
جنس ما يعرف بدليله وثانيهما ما إذا كان يشتبه حاله لكن عرف أن الراوي اعتمد على دليل المعرفة. (القمر)
Section on contradiction. Explanation of the occurrence of contradiction between two analogies. ... until the evidence of permissibility or prohibition is established. And I have elaborated on it in the commentary 'al-Ahmadi'. And the affirmer is more deserving than the negator. This is an independent principle with no connection to what preceded, meaning if the affirmer and negator conflict, then the affirmer is more deserving of being acted upon than the negator according to al-Karkhi. And the followers of al-Shafi'i. And according to Ibn Aban, they conflict, i.e., they are equal, then after that, preference is given based on the state of the narrator in terms of reliability and precision. And what is meant by the affirmer is that which affirms an incidental additional matter that was not previously established, and by the negator is that which negates the additional matter and keeps it on its original state. Since there was a disagreement between al-Karkhi and Ibn Aban, and there was also disagreement in the practice of our scholars, for in some instances they act on the affirmer and in some instances on the negator, the author pointed to a rule in this regard that removes the disagreement from them. He said: And I have elaborated on it etc. ... The principle: The negator, if it is of the type that is known by its evidence, ...
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the usul principle regarding contradiction between an affirmer (muthbit) and a negator (nafi). The author explains the positions of early Hanafi scholars: al-Karkhi (followed by Shafi'is) holds that the affirmer is preferred and acted upon first, while Ibn Aban holds that they are equal and require external preference (tarjih) based on the narrator's reliability. The commentary resolves the apparent conflict in Hanafi practice by stating that the preferred ruling depends on whether the negator is based on evidence or on mere istishab (presumption of continuity). Two scenarios are identified: (1) if the negator is known by a clear evidence or its state is ambiguous but the narrator is known to have relied on evidence, then it is like the affirmer and they conflict, requiring tarjih—this aligns with Ibn Aban. (2) If the negator is not of that type and is based on mere istishab (which is not a valid proof), then the affirmer is preferred without conflict—this aligns with al-Karkhi. Thus the Hanafi school actually combines both views by conditioning the rule. The commentary also provides the definition of muthbit and nafi based on legal effect, not literal wording, citing the example of a depositary's statement.

Key Terms
المثبت (al-muthbit): That which affirms an incidental additional matter that was not previously established.
النافي (al-nafi): That which negates the additional matter and keeps it on its original state.
الاستصحاب (al-istishab): Presumption of continuity; the existing state is presumed to remain until evidence indicates otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi usul, when does the affirmer (muthbit) take precedence over the negator (nafi)?
A) Always, as per al-Karkhi
B) Only when the negator is based on istishab, not evidence
C) Never, as per Ibn Aban
D) Only when the narrator is reliable

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule for affirmer-negator conflict is conditional: prefer the affirmer unless the negator is based on evidence, then seek tarjih.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Preferring Ithbat over Nafy in Conflicting Reports
Explaining rule of preference between conflicting nafy and ithbat reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of preferring affirmation (ithbat) over negation (nafy) when the negation is based solely on the original state (istishab), and distinguish between cases where the negative report also has direct evidence.

Core Idea
Affirmation (ithbat) based on direct evidence prevails over negation (nafy) based on original presumption.

In Hanafi usul, when two reports conflict, not all negations are equal. A negation that merely relies on the apparent state or istishab is weaker than an affirmation that comes from direct testimony. This principle is illustrated by the case of Barirah, where the report of her husband's freedom (ithbat) outweighed the report of his slavery (nafy). However, in the case of the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah, both reports had direct evidence, so narrator reliability became decisive. This lesson walks through the reasoning and the resulting tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting reports and their bases
Determine which report is a negation (nafy) and which is an affirmation (ithbat). For Barirah, the report that her husband was a slave is nafy; the report that he was free is ithbat. For Maymunah, the report that the Prophet was muhrim is nafy of halal; the report that he was halal is ithbat.
Barirah's case: nafy relies on original state (he was a slave). Maymunah's case: nafy relies on observable signs (muhrim appearance).
2
Examine the evidence for the nafy
Check whether the nafy is based solely on istishab (original presumption) or has direct evidence. In Barirah, the nafy has only istishab; in Maymunah, the nafy is based on the muhrim's appearance, which is direct evidence.
If nafy has only istishab, it is weaker. If it has direct evidence, it is equal to ithbat.
3
Apply the rule of precedence
If nafy has only istishab, ithbat prevails. If both have direct evidence, the reports are equally strong, and tarjih (preponderance) must be made by narrator reliability or other factors.
Hanafi rule: al-ithbat muqaddam 'ala al-nafy 'inda al-ta'arud idha kana al-nafy bi-mujarrad al-istishab.
4
Analyze Barirah's case
The nafy (slave) is based only on the original state. Thus, the ithbat (free) prevails. The Hanafi position grants Barirah the option (khiyar) to annul the marriage if her husband is free.
This is a straightforward application of the rule.
5
Analyze Maymunah's case
Both reports have direct evidence: the nafy (muhrim) from appearance, the ithbat (halal) from testimony. They conflict equally. Tarjih is needed: the Hanafi school prefers Ibn Abbas's narration (muhrim) over Yazid ibn al-Asamm (halal) due to narrator reliability.
Al-Shafi'i prefers the ithbat (halal) based on consensus that marriage in ihram is invalid.

فصل في التعارض
بيان وقوع التعارض بين القياسين على أن زوجها كان عبدًا في الحقيقة وإنما وقع الاختلاف في الحرية العارضة كان خبر أي بعد العبودية العبودية نافيًا للحرية العارضة ومبقيًا له على الأصل، وخبر الحرية مثبتاً للأمر العارضي، أي لزوج بريرة فخبر النفي وهو ما روي أنها أعتقت وزوجها عبد * مما لا يعرف إلا بظاهر الحال، وهو أنه كان عبدًا في الأصل، فالظاهر أنه بقي كذلك وليست للعبد علامة ودليل يعرف بها ويميّز عن الحرّ، فلم يعارض الإثبات وهو ما روي أنها أعتقت وزوجها حرّ؟ ** لأن من أخبر بالحرية لا شك أنه وقف عليها بالإخبار والسماع فكان عمله مستندا إلى دليل، أي الحرية الطارئة فأصحابنا له ههنا عملوا بالمثبت وأثبتوا الخيار لها حين كون زوجها حرا.
