Chapter on Conflict: Explanation of the occurrence of conflict between two analogies: that her husband was in reality a slave, but the disagreement occurred about the accidental freedom. The report [of slavery] is a negation of the accidental freedom and maintaining him on the original state, and the report of freedom is an affirmation of the accidental matter, i.e., concerning Barirah's husband. So the report of negation—which is what was narrated that she was freed and her husband was a slave—is not known except by the apparent state, i.e., that he was originally a slave, so the apparent state is that he remained as such, and there is no mark or evidence for a slave by which he is known and distinguished from a free person. So it did not oppose the affirmation—which is what was narrated that she was freed and her husband was free?—because the one who reported freedom, there is no doubt that he came to know it by report and hearing, so his action was based on evidence, i.e., the accidental freedom. So our companions here acted upon the affirmative and established the choice for her when her husband was free. i.e., for the emancipated woman. And the negation in the hadith of Maymunah is an example of the negation being of the type that is known by its evidence. That is, the Prophet ﷺ was in ihram and married Maymunah himself, but they disagreed whether he remained in ihram at the time of marriage or broke it. It was said he broke it, then married, and al-Shafi'i took this, because marriage in ihram is not permissible just as intercourse is not permissible by consensus. And it was said he remained in ihram at the time of marriage (i.e., in ihram). And 'the report of freedom etc.' is coordinated with his statement 'the report of slavery'. The annotation (al-Qamar): 'except by the apparent state etc.' means the report of his being a slave is not known by its evidence, nor is its state ambiguous, but it is known that the narrator relied on a proof of knowledge. When both matters were negated, this report which is negation does not oppose the report of freedom which is affirmation, rather the affirmation is more appropriate. And it is what is narrated in the six books: she was freed and her husband was free. (al-Sanbali: 'and there is no mark for a slave etc.': knowledge of being a slave is by istishab of the past state.) (al-Qamar: 'to evidence': i.e., the evidence of freedom, which is emancipation.) (al-Qamar: 'when her husband was free etc.': and since their statement is in the case where the husband is free, in the case where the husband is a slave their statement applies by primary reasoning.) (al-Sanbali: 'or broke it? i.e., the ihram.) (al-Qamar: 'it was said he broke it etc.' in Sahih Muslim and Sunan Ibn Majah from Yazid ibn al-Asamm: Maymunah told me: 'He married her while he was halal.' Likewise in al-Subh al-Sadiq. (al-Qamar: 'by consensus i.e., between us and al-Shafi'i.) (al-Qamar: 'and it was said he remained etc.': narrated by the authors of the six books from Ibn Abbas. Likewise in al-Subh al-Sadiq.) (al-Qamar: 'and it is reported in a long hadith of Muslim from Aishah that Barirah's husband was a slave, previously mentioned from the narration of al-Nasa'i.' [Ishraq al-Absar: 24] ** In a narration from Aishah that he was free, narrated by Abu Dawud and others. [Ishraq al-Absar: 24] that the Prophet... Chapter on Conflict: Explanation of the occurrence of conflict between the two analogies: that he married her. Abu Hanifa took this, as he allows marriage for the muhrim even though intercourse is prohibited. So ihram, although it is a contingent matter in humans and halal is the original state, the narrators agreed that he definitely performed ihram. The disagreement is only about its continuation or breaking. The report of ihram is a negation of the accidental halal upon him, and the report of halal is an affirmation of the contingent matter. So the report of negation in the chapter of Maymunah's hadith—what was narrated that he was muhrim—is known by its evidence, which is the appearance of a muhrim: wearing unstitched cloth, not trimming nails, not shaving hair. This is knowledge based on evidence. So it opposed the affirmation—what was narrated that he married her while he was halal—because the one who reported this, no doubt he saw upon him the dress of the non-muhrims and their appearance. So when the two reports conflict equally, there is need to give preponderance to one of them by the state of the narrator. And the narration of Ibn Abbas that he did not marry her while muhrim is more appropriate than the narration of Yazid ibn al-Asamm about her. (al-Qamar: 'So ihram etc.': a rebuttal of an anticipated objection: that ihram is an accidental matter, so its report is affirmative, as it affirms an additional accidental matter, not that it is a negation.) (al-Qamar: 'and the disagreement is only about its continuation etc.': all the narrations from both groups agree that his marriage was not in the original halal, but the Companions knew that the Prophet sent Abu Rafi' his freed slave and a man from the Ansar, and they married him to Maymunah bint al-Harith while he was in Medina before he assumed ihram. Likewise in Sharh al-Husami.) (al-Qamar: 'for the accidental halal': i.e., the halal established after freeing from ihram.) (al-Qamar: 'for the contingent matter': i.e., the halal that supervenes upon ihram.) (al-Qamar: 'the two reports': i.e., the report of his being muhrim and the report of his being halal.) (al-Muhashi: 'equally': because the negation is established by evidence, so it becomes like the affirmation.) (al-Qamar: 'Yazid ibn al-Asamm etc.': al-Zuhri said: 'We do not know Ibn al-Asamm, he is a Bedouin who urinates on his shank.' Also the chain of negation is stronger because its narrators are all jurists as al-Tahawi said. Also Malik narrated in al-Muwatta from Sulayman ibn Yasar. Saheeh al-Bukhari no. 1740, chapter on marriage of a muhrim, and Muslim no. 1410, chapter on prohibition of marriage of a muhrim and dislike of his proposal, from Ibn Abbas. ** The Shaykh al-Imam Muhyi al-Sunnah and the majority hold that he married her halal, and the matter of his marriage appeared [as if] he was muhrim, then he consummated with her while halal at Sarif on the way to Mecca. It is not hidden from you that most hadith scholars hold that he married her while muhrim and consummated while halal, so what the Shaykh mentioned is subject to consideration. [Ishraq al-Absar: 25,24]
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of a key Hanafi usul principle regarding the resolution of conflicting reports (ta'arud). The principle states: when a report negating something (nafy) is based solely on the apparent state (zahir al-hal) or original presumption (istishab), and a report affirming something (ithbat) is based on direct knowledge (khabar or sama'), the affirming report is given precedence. The text illustrates this with two case studies from hadith. The first case is Barirah: narrations conflict on whether her husband was a slave or free at the time of her emancipation. The negation (slave) rests on the original state (he was a slave), while the affirmation (free) rests on actual reporting. Since the affirmation is based on direct evidence, it prevails, and the Hanafi ruling grants Barirah the option (khiyar) to annul the marriage if her husband is free. The second case is the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah: here both reports—that he was muhrim (negating halal) and that he was halal (affirming halal)—are supported by evidence. The report of ihram is known by observable signs (dress, grooming), and the report of halal is known by a narrator's testimony. Thus they conflict equally, requiring a preponderance (tarjih) based on the narrator's reliability. The Hanafi position, following Abu Hanifa, favors the report that he was muhrim (Ibn Abbas's narration), while al-Shafi'i favors the report that he was halal (Yazid ibn al-Asamm). The text also notes additional details from commentary sources like al-Qamar and al-Sanbali.

Key Terms
التعارض (al-ta'arud): Conflict between two evidences that appear to be contradictory, requiring resolution by tarjih or other means.
النفي (al-nafy): A report that negates a particular attribute or ruling, often based on the original state or absence of evidence.
الإثبات (al-ithbat): A report that affirms a particular attribute or ruling, typically based on direct testimony or knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle explained in this passage, which report is given preference: a report that affirms a ruling based on direct testimony or a report that negates it based on the original state (istishab)?
A) The report based on original state (istishab) is always preferred.
B) The report based on direct testimony is preferred because it involves additional knowledge.
C) Both are equal and neither can be used.
D) Preference depends on the number of narrators.

Key Takeaway
Ithbat over nafy is the default when nafy lacks independent evidence; when both have evidence, narrator reliability becomes the tiebreaker.

Tarjih Between Conflicting Reports: The Marriage of Maymunah
Analyzing conflicting reports about the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah while in ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of tarjih to resolve conflicting reports by evaluating narrator reliability and contextual interpretation.

Core Idea
When hadiths conflict, prefer the stronger narrator and harmonize the weaker proof — as Hanafis did for the marriage of Maymunah.

This lesson centers on a classic usul al-fiqh dispute: did the Prophet marry Maymunah while in ihram or while halal? The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, holds that marriage in ihram is valid and that the Prophet married her while halal. The resolution of this conflict involves applying tarjih by examining the narrators' reliability and reinterpreting an opposing hadith. Understanding this case will sharpen your ability to evaluate conflicting evidence in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting reports
Locate the two reports: one stating the Prophet married while muhrim (Yazid ibn al-Asamm) and one stating he married while halal (Ibn Abbas). Recognize that both are ahad hadiths.
2
State the Hanafi position on marriage in ihram
Abu Hanifa ruled that a marriage contract is valid for a muhrim, though intercourse is prohibited. This sets the legal framework for interpreting the evidence.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
3
Apply Hanafi tarjih criteria
Compare the narrators: Ibn Abbas is preferred over Yazid due to superior memory (ḍabṭ), knowledge (fiqh), justice (adalah), and piety (wara'). This is the key reason for preferring the report of halal marriage.
The Hanafi school emphasizes narrator attributes in tarjih, as seen here and in many other cases.
4
Analyze the conflicting hadith 'La yankihu al-muhrim'
The hadith appears to prohibit marriage for a muhrim. Hanafis interpret 'nikah' as intercourse, not the contract, relying on contextual evidence (qarinah) from the reports about Maymunah.
This is a case of takhsis (specification) of a general prohibition.
5
Determine the practical outcome (thamarah al-khilaf)
The dispute has real-world consequences: according to Hanafis, a muhrim can validly marry; according to Shafi'is, the marriage is invalid. This shows the importance of usul methodology.
The Hanafi position is considered the more reliable (rajih) due to the strength of the evidence.

فصل في التعارض
بيان وقوع التعارض بين القياسين
أنه عليها تزوجها
وبه أخذ أبو حنيفة ملكه حيث يحلّ النكاح للمحرم وإن حرم الوطء، فالإحرام وإن كان أي في الإحرام عارضًا في بني آدم والحلّ أصلاً، لكنه اتفقت الرواة أنه علي كان أحرم البتة، وإنما الاختلاف في إبقائه ونقضه كان خبر الإحرام نافيًا للحلّ الطارئ عليه، وخبر الحلّ مثبتا للأمر العارض، فخبر النفي في باب حديث ميمونة لها وهو ما روي وهو محرم مما يعرف بدليله وهو هيأة المحرم من لبس غير المخيط وعدم تقلّم الأظافير وعدم حلق الشعر، فهذا علم مستند إلى دليل، فعارض الإثبات وهو ما روي أنه عليه تزوجها وهو حلال؛ لأن أخبر بهذا لا شك أنه قد رأى عليه لباس المحلّلين من وزِيّهم، فلما تعارض الخبران على السواء احتيج إلى ترجيح أحدهما بحال الراوي. وجعل رواية ابن عباس ما وهو أنه لا تزوجها وهو محرم أولى من رواية يزيد بن الأصم فيها عليها من فالإحرام إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أن الإحرام أمر عارضي، فخبره مثبت فإنه أثبت أمرًا عارضا زائدا لا أن يكون نافيا. (القمر) وإنما الاختلاف في إبقائه إلخ فإنه اتفقت عامة الروايات من الفريقين على أن نكاحه ما كان في الحلّ الأصلي، لكن في معرفة الصحابة للمستغفرين أن النبي بعث أبا رافع مولاه ورجلاً الأنصار، وزوجاه ميمونة بنت الحارث لها ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالمدينة قبل أن يحرم، كذا في "شرح الحسامي". (القمر) للحلّ الطارئ: أي الحلّ الثابت بعد التحلّل من الإحرام. (القمر) للأمر العارض: أي الحلّ الطارئ على الإحرام. (القمر) الخبران: أي خبر كونه محرمًا وكونه حلالاً.(المحشي) على السواء لأن النفي ثبت بالدليل فصار مثل الإثبات. (القمر) يزيد بن الأصم إلخ : قال الزهري: ما ندري ابن الأصم أعرابي بَوّال على ساقه، وأيضًا سند النفي أقوى فإن رواته كلهم فقهاء كما قال الطحاوي، وأيضًا روى مالك في "الموطأ" عن سليمان ابن يسار قال : أخرجه البخاري رقم: ١٧٤٠ ، باب تزويج المحرم، ومسلم رقم: ١٤١٠ ، باب تحريم نكاح المحرم وكراهة خطبته، عن ابن عباس ها. ** قال الشيخ الإمام محي السنة الله والأكثرون على أنه تزوّجها حلالاً، وظهر أمر تزويجها وهو محرم، ثم بنى بها وهو حلال بسرف في طريق مكة. لا يخفى عليك أن أكثر المحدثين على أنه الا الله نكحها وهو محرم، وبنى بها وهو حلال، فما ذكره الشيخ محل نظر . بيان وقوع التعارض بين القياسين
أنه عليها تزوّجها وهو حلال لأنه لا يعدله في الضبط والإتقان، فصار خبر النفي ههنا معمولا بهذه الوتيرة.
وطهارة الماء وحلّ الطعام من جنس ما يعرف بدليله مثال لكون الراوي مما اعتمد على دليل المعرفة، وفي العبارة مسامحة، والأولى أن يقول : وطهارة الماء وحلّ الطعام من جنس ما تشتبه حاله لكن إذا عرف أن الراوي اعتمد دليل المعرفة يكون من جنس ما يعرف بدليله، وبيانه أن الأصل في الماء الطهارة، وفي الطعام الحلّ، فإذا تعارض مخبران فيه فيقول أحدهما: إنه نجس أو حرام فلا شك أنه خبر مثبت للأمر العارض ما أخبر به قائله إلا أي الماء أي الطعام أي النجاسة والحرمة بالدليل ثم جاء آخر يقول إنه طاهر أو حلال، فلا بد من أن يتفحص من حاله، فإن أي الماء أي الطعام كان خبره بمجرد أن الأصل فيه الطهارة أو الحل لم يقبل خبره؛ لأنه نفي بلا دليل . الآخر أي في الماء أي في الطعام أي للأمر العارض
= بعث النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أبا رافع مولاه ورجلاً من الأنصار فزوجا بنت الحارث، ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه بالمدينة قبل أن يخرج، ففيه نفي للإحرام، وعلى هذا قال الشيخ بن الهمام: إن هذا الإخبار بالأصل فيرجح عليه رواية ابن عباس ا لكونه عن الدليل وما استدلّ به الشافعي له من قول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم "لا ينكح المحرم" رواه ابن الهمام بأنه عارض رواية ابن عباس هم نكاح أم المؤمنين ميمونة وهو محرم، وابن عباس أقوى ضبطا وفقها وعدالة وورعا؛ فالترجيح له، ولو سُلّم التساوي تساقطا ووجب الرجوع إلى القياس، وهو مؤيد لنا؛ لأن النكاح كالشراء للتسري، وهو غير ممنوع بالإحرام كذا في كتب الحنفية. (السنبلي) لأنه لا يعدله إلى أي لأن يزيد بن الأصم لا يعدل ابن عباس له في الضبط، وقوة ضبط ابن عباس دليل على عدم غلطه، وقد قال عمرو بن دينار للزهري: إن يزيد بن الأصم أعرابي بَوّال على عقبيه، أتجعله مثل ابن عباس؟ و لم ينكر عليه الزهري، كذا في "الكشف" و"فتح القدير". (القمر)
فصار خبر النفي إلخ لكن بقي أنه وقع النهى الصريح من نكاح المحرم فتعارض القول والفعل، روي: "المحرم لا ينكح ولا يُنكح" كما في صحيح مسلم، ويمكن أن يقال: إن هذه الرواية محمولة على الوطء أي لا يطأ، ولا يمكن من الوطء، كذا في "فتح الغفار". (القمر) والأولى إلخ فإن ما هو جنس ما يعرف بدليله قد مرّ مثاله آنفا، وهذا ليس من جنس ما يعرف بدليله. (القمر) لكن إذا عرف إلخ توجيه لعبارة المصنف يحله. (القمر) يقول إلخ: هذا الخبر نفي للأمر العارض أي النجاسة والحرمة. (القمر)
Chapter on Conflict. Explanation of the occurrence of conflict between two analogies. He married her while in ihram? And Abu Hanifa took [the ruling] that marriage is permissible for a muhrim even though intercourse is prohibited. So ihram, even though it is a temporary condition in humans and permissibility is the original [state], but all narrators agree that Ali was definitely in ihram, and the difference is only in its abrogation. The report of ihram negates the temporary permissibility, and the report of permissibility affirms the temporary matter. So the report of negation in the context of the hadith of Maymunah—which is narrated that he [married] while in ihram—is known by its evidence, which is the appearance of a muhrim: wearing unstitched clothes, not trimming nails, not shaving hair. This is knowledge based on evidence. Then the affirmation [report] opposes it, i.e., what is narrated that he married her while halal, because the one who reported this undoubtedly saw him wearing the clothes of those who are halal. So when the two reports conflict equally, preference of one over the other is needed based on the condition of the narrator. And the narration of Ibn Abbas—that he did not marry her while in ihram—was considered preferable over the narration of Yazid ibn al-Asamm. (Then commentary). And the hadith: The Prophet sent Abu Rafi' and a man from the Ansar to marry Maymunah bint al-Harith while he was in Medina before he left for ihram. (Commentary) For the temporary permissibility: i.e., the permissibility after leaving ihram. For the temporary matter: i.e., the permissibility that occurs due to ihram. The two reports: i.e., the report of him being muhrim and the report of him being halal. Equally because negation is established by evidence, so it becomes like affirmation. Yazid ibn al-Asamm etc.: Al-Zuhri said: We don't know Ibn al-Asamm, a Bedouin who urinates on his legs. Also the chain of negation is stronger because all its narrators are jurists as said by al-Tahawi. Also Malik narrated in al-Muwatta' from Sulayman ibn Yasar that... (then text continues). And the most hadith scholars say that he married her while halal. (Then discussion of the hadith 'The muhrim should not marry' etc. and the Hanafi interpretation that it refers to intercourse).
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the conflict (ta'arud) between two reports concerning the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah: one report states he married her while in the state of ihram (sacred state for Hajj/Umrah), and another states he married her while halal (non-muhrim). The text presents the Hanafi methodology for resolving such conflicts, which is based on tarjih (preference) by examining the reliability of the narrators. Abu Hanifa's position is that marriage for a muhrim is valid (though intercourse is prohibited), and the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah occurred when he was not in ihram. The Hanafi scholars give precedence to the narration of Ibn Abbas (who reported he was halal) over that of Yazid ibn al-Asamm (who reported he was muhrim) because Ibn Abbas is superior in memory, knowledge, and piety. Additionally, the report that the Prophet sent Abu Rafi' to arrange the marriage while he was still in Medina (before entering ihram) supports the halal status. The text also addresses the apparent contradiction with the explicit hadith 'The muhrim should not marry nor give in marriage' (Sahih Muslim). Hanafi scholars interpret this hadith as referring to the prohibition of sexual intercourse while in ihram, not the marriage contract itself. The passage follows the commentator's order by first stating the conflict, then presenting the evidence and arguments, and finally discussing the tarjih criteria. The commentary inserts marginal notes (e.g., from 'al-Qamar' and 'al-Muhashi') that clarify terms and strengthen the Hanafi position. The author also uses qiyas (analogy) to support the Hanafi view: marriage is like purchasing a concubine (which is permissible for a muhrim), so marriage should also be permissible.

Key Terms
التعارض (al-ta'āruḍ): The apparent contradiction between two proofs (here, two reports) that cannot both be true literally.
الترجيح (al-tarjīḥ): Giving preference to one conflicting evidence over another based on certain criteria, such as the reliability of the narrator.
خبر (khabar): A report or narration (hadith) about the Prophet's action or statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Hanafi scholars prefer the narration of Ibn Abbas over that of Yazid ibn al-Asamm regarding the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah?
A) Because Ibn Abbas was a relative of the Prophet.
B) Because Ibn Abbas had more wives.
C) Because Ibn Abbas was superior in memory, knowledge, justice, and piety.
D) Because Yazid ibn al-Asamm was not a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi resolution of the Maymunah marriage conflict exemplifies the usul al-fiqh principle that when hadiths conflict, tarjih based on narrator reliability and contextual interpretation yields the correct ruling.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Preference Between Contradictory Reports: The Hanafi Tarjih Rules
Explains how to resolve contradiction between two reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules of tarjih to resolve apparent contradictions between two reports by identifying factors such as narrator reliability, affirmation vs negation, and evidence basis, while excluding multiplicity of narrators as a valid ground.

Core Idea
The Hanafi tarjih prioritizes quality over quantity: a single reliable narrator outweighs many weak ones.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary explains how to resolve contradictions between two reports (khabarayn) or analogies. The key principle is that a report based on direct evidence (dalil) is preferred over one relying solely on the original principle (asl). Similarly, a report that affirms a ruling (muthbit) is stronger than one that denies it (nafi) without evidence. The passage also addresses the dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding the role of multiplicity of narrators, firmly siding with the Hanafi position that individual narrator reliability, not numbers, determines preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contradictory reports
Determine what two reports are in apparent conflict. For example, one report says water is pure, another says it is impure; or one says marriage in ihram is allowed, another says it is prohibited.
2
Check the basis of each report
Is the report based on direct evidence (dalil) or mere original principle (asl)? A report based on evidence is stronger. For instance, stating impurity because an impurity was seen is stronger than merely assuming purity.
The passage gives the example of Ibn Abbas's narration of the Prophet's marriage in ihram, which is based on actual observation.
3
Apply the muthbit-over-nafi rule
If one report affirms a new ruling (e.g., impurity, prohibition) and the other denies it (e.g., purity, permissibility), the affirming report is preferred if it has evidence; the denying report must also be based on evidence or the original principle.
In the example of water, the report claiming impurity is muthbit and is given precedence over the nafi report that merely relies on original purity.
4
Evaluate narrator reliability vs multiplicity
Hanafis give preference to the more reliable, knowledgeable narrator, not to the report with more narrators. The case of Ibn Abbas (single narrator) being preferred over Abu Rafi (multiple narrators) illustrates this. Multiplicity of narrators is not a valid ground for tarjih.
The passage cites the practice of Umar and other Companions who rejected the hadith 'Innama al-ma' min al-ma'' despite its many narrators, in favor of Aisha's single narration.

(القمر)  فصل في التعارض ٥٦٩ بيان وقوع التعارض بين الخبرين فحينئذ كان خبر النجاسة والحرمة أولى؛ لأنه مثبت وإن كان خبره بالدليل وهو أنه أخذه الآخر من العين الجارية أو الحوض العشر في العشر وجعله بنفسه في الإناء الطاهر الجديد أو الغسيل بحيث لا يشك في طهارته ولم يفارقه منذ ألقى الماء فيه حتى يتوهم أنه ألقى فيه النجاسة أحد، فحينئذٍ كان هذا النفي من جنس ما يعرف بدليله. بيان وقوع التعارض بين الخبرين] كالنجاسة والحرمة، فوقع التعارض بين الخبرين، فوجب العمل بالأصل والطهارة، وقد بالغنا في تحقيق الأمثلة حينئذ بما لا مزيد عليه. أي في الماء وهو أي في الطعام الحل ثم يقول المصنف له والترجيح لا يقع بفضل عدد الرواة وبالذكورة والأنوثة والحرية، أي بكثرة عدد الرواة يعني إذا كان في أحد الخبرين المتعارضين كثرة الرواة وفي الآخر قلتها، أو كان راوي أحدهما فحينئذٍ كان هذا النفي إلخ فيُنظر ويسأل عن مبنى الإخبار، فإن أخبر أنه بالأصل فيعمل بالنجاسة، وإن أخبر أنه بالدليل تعارضا والاستصحاب مرجّح فيعمل بالطهارة التي هي الأصل؛ لأن الاستصحاب وإن لم يكن حجة لكن يصلح مرجّحا ، وإن جهل عمل بالنجاسة؛ لأنها أقوى، وقد يطالب بالفرق بينها وبين مسألة سؤر الحمار، فإن مقتضاها أن يقرر الأصول أيضا، فيحكم بطهارة الماء وعدم زوال الحدث بعد استعماله، فيجب ضم التيمم، ويجاب بأن هناك التعارض في الأدلة الشرعية وهي مثبتة للأحكام؛ فيمكن أن يحكم بالمشكوكية، بخلاف ما نحن فيه؛ فإنه خبر لا يثبت حكمًا أصلاً، فلا يخرج به حكم المشكوكية، فتأمل. (السنبلي) كالنجاسة إلخ: أي مثل معرفة النجاسة والحرمة فإنه يكون بالدليل (القمر) بين الخبرين أي خبر الطهارة والحلّ، وخبر النجاسة والحرمة في الماء والطعام. (القمر) فوجب إلخ : فإن الأصل وإن لم يصلح علة لكنه صلح مرجّحًا. (القمر) والترجيح: أي ترجيح أحد الخبرين على الآخر. (القمر) والترجيح لا يقع إلخ كما أن رواة "إنما الماء من الماء" كانت أكثر وقد رجّح أمير المؤمنين عمر الله وغيره من الصحابة خبر أم المؤمنين لها وحدها، فلم يعتبروا التقوي بكثرة الرواة، ولعلّ هذه القوة ضعيفة مراتبها متفاوتة، ففي اعتبارها نوع من العسر، والله يريد اليسر، أقول: وينقض هذا أي القول بكثرة العدد بكثرة الاجتهاد، فإن عدم الترجيح بها اتفاق بيننا وبينكم مع أنه إلى اليقين بالإجماع كما أنه ينتهي كثرة الرواة إلى القطع، فما ذهب إليه الجمهور من أن الظن يتقوى بتدريج بكثرة الرواة أبطله عدم الترجيح بكثرة الاجتهاد. (السنبلي) ينتهي
Chapter on contradiction. It is an explanation of the occurrence of contradiction between two analogies... (the text continues with detailed discussion of examples and rulings) ...and preference does not occur by multiplicity of narrators, masculinity, femininity, or freedom.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary discusses the rules of preference (tarjih) when two reports (khabarayn) or two analogies (qiyasayn) appear to contradict each other. The author begins by stating that when reports conflict, the one based on direct evidence (dalil) is preferred over one based solely on the original principle (asl). He gives examples: the narration of Ibn Abbas regarding the Prophet marrying Maymunah while in ihram is preferred over Abu Rafi's narration because Ibn Abbas is stronger in memory and understanding. Similarly, for water and food, if one report says it is impure/haram and another says it is pure/halal, the one affirming impurity/haram is preferred if it is based on evidence, while the one merely relying on the original purity/permissibility is rejected. The passage also clarifies that preference is not given based on a larger number of narrators, as shown by the practice of Umar and the Companions who favored a single narration over many. The discussion includes responses to Shafi'i arguments and references to Hanafi works like al-Kashf and Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
تعارض (ta'āruḍ): The apparent conflict between two proofs that cannot both be applied simultaneously
ترجيح (tarjīḥ): Giving preference to one evidence over another due to a stronger aspect (e.g., more reliable narrator, stronger evidence)
خبر النفي (khabar al-nafy): A report that denies or negates a ruling, such as saying water is pure when no impurity is seen
خبر الإثبات (khabar al-ithbāt): A report that affirms a ruling, such as saying water is impure

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, which factor is NOT considered a valid ground for preference when two reports contradict each other?
A) The narrator being more knowledgeable and accurate
B) The report being muthbit (affirming) rather than nafi (negating)
C) The greater number of narrators
D) The report relying on evidence (dalil) rather than mere original principle (asl)

Key Takeaway
When reports conflict, Hanafi tarjih gives weight to narrator reliability, evidence-based reports, and affirming reports—not to the quantity of narrators.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Tarjih by Number and Narrator Attributes
Explaining that mere number, gender, and freedom do not give tarjih; only 'adalah and itqan matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that tarjih is based on 'adalah and dhabt, not on number, gender, or freedom, and identify the exception for situational knowledge (inkishaf).

Core Idea
Tarjih by number is rejected; preference is by integrity and precision, as the Companions practiced.

When two ahad reports conflict, which one should be preferred? Some schools look to the number of narrators, but the Hanafi school takes a different path. In this passage, we learn that mere quantity, gender, or freedom does not tip the scales—what matters is the narrator's integrity and precision (dhabt), along with situational factors that affect observation. The dispute with Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i is resolved by istihsan, relying on the practice of the Salaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The passage begins by stating that differences in gender (masculine vs feminine) or status (free vs slave) do not give preference to one report over another because the relevant quality is 'adalah, which does not vary by these attributes.
The author is refuting a potential misunderstanding that such social attributes might matter.
2
Understand the rule on number
The author then addresses the role of number: for two ahad reports, mere numerical majority does not give preference if both sides have equal numbers. However, if one side has two narrators and the other one, the two are preferred, provided they are equal in other qualities.
This shows that two is better than one, but not because of mere counting; it reflects a minimal threshold for probability.
3
Analyze the opposing view and the Hanafi response
Some scholars (Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and Imam al-Shafi'i) argued that greater number of narrators increases the probability of truth, citing an analogy from testimony about water purity. The Hanafis reject this by istihsan, noting that the Companions never gave preference by number but by memory and precision.
The analogy with testimony is rejected because testimony and narration have different rules.
4
Apply the eclipse prayer example
The passage gives a concrete example: the report of men about the eclipse prayer (one bow per rak'ah) is preferred over Aisha's report (two bows per rak'ah) because the men were closer to the imam and had better visibility. This shows that tarjih can be based on situational knowledge (inkishaf), not on personal attributes like gender or number.
Aisha's report is not rejected due to her gender but due to her distance from the action.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in Hanafi fiqh, when two ahad reports conflict, the one with more narrators is not automatically preferred; instead, the integrity and precision of the narrators are paramount. This contrasts with the Shafi'i position, which generally prioritizes numerical majority.
This difference can lead to opposite rulings on the same issue.

فصل في التعارض بيان وقوع التعارض بين الخبرين مذكرًا والآخر مؤنثاً، أو راوي أحدهما حرا والآخر عبدا لم يترجح أحد الخبرين على الآخر بهذه المزيّة؛ لأن المعتبر في هذا الباب العدالة وهي لا تختلف بالكثرة والذكورة والحرية، فإن أي ترجيح الخبر عائشة كانت أفضل من والجماعة القليلة العادلة أفضل من الكثيرة العاصية، وفي قوله: "فضل عدد الرواة" إشارة إلى أن عددًا لا يترجّح على عدد بعد أن كان في درجة الآحاد ، وأما إن كان في جانب واحد، وفي جانب اثنان يترجّح خبر اثنين على خبر الواحد، وقال بعضهم: يترجّح جهة الكثرة على جانب القلة تمسكًا بما ذكر محمد الله في مسائل الماء، ولكنا تركناه بالاستحسان. أكثر الرجال، وبلالا لانه كان أفضل من أكثر الحرائر، لم يترجح أحد إلخ إلا في خبر كان حاله أكشف على الرجال من النساء، فيعتبر خبر الرجال حينئذ لا خبر النساء كما روي أنه عليه صلّى صلاة الكسوف وركع في كل ركعة ركوعًا واحدا، فعملنا به وتركنا ما روت عائشة أنه يركع في كل ركعة ركوعين؛ لأن النساء كانت متأخرات عن الرجال في صفوف المسجد، والرجال كانوا قريبي الإمام، فحاله يكون منكشفًا على الرجال انكشافاً تاماً لقربهم، لا على النساء لبعدهن عن الإمام، كذا قيل. (القمر) كانت أفضل أي في العدالة والضبط والإتقان. (القمر) كان أفضل أي في العدالة والإتقان. (القمر) والجماعة القليلة إلخ هذا يبطل الأصل الإنجليزي من تصويب كثرة الرأي وإن كانت الكثرة للجهال، إلا أن محمدًا والإمام الشافعي عملها ذهبا إلى الترجيح بكثرة عدد الحصول قوة الظن بالصدق بكثرة المخبرين. (السنبلي) أفضل إلخ فإنه يحصل من الجماعة القليلة العادلة قوة الظن، بخلاف الكثرة العاصية فلا اعتداد بالكثرة، وبه اندفع ما قال الإمام محمد الله وجمهور الشافعية: من الترجيح بكثرة الرواة الحصول قوة ظن الصدق بكثرة المخبرين (القمر) بعد أن كان أي كل واحد من الخبرين، وفائدة هذا القيد أن خبرًا إذا وصل درجة التواتر فله ترجيح على غيره. (القمر) يترجح خبر اثنين إلخ وفيه أن خبر الاثنين من الآحاد على ما مرّ. (القمر) بما ذكر محمد الله: أي في كتاب الاستحسان من "المبسوط"، وهو ترجيح قول الاثنين على الواحد، فإن الواحد إذا أخبر بطهارة الماء أو حلّة الطعام مثلاً، والاثنان أخبرا بنجاسة الماء أو حرمة الطعام فيعمل بخبرهما لا بخبره، فكذا الحال في باب الأخبار والروايات فلكثرة الرواة ترجيح (القمر) ولكنا تركناه: أي تركنا ترجّح جانب الكثرة على جانب القلّة بالاستحسان، فإن الصحابة له وغيرهم من السلف لم يرجّحوا بكثرة العدد في باب العمل بالأخبار والروايات كما رجحوا بزيادة الضبط والإتقان كذا في "الكشف". (القمر)
Chapter on conflict. Explanation of occurrence of conflict between two reports: [One report] being masculine and the other feminine, or one narrator being free and the other a slave, neither report is given precedence over the other by this quality; because what is considered in this chapter is integrity (adalah), and it does not differ by quantity, masculinity, or freedom. For any preference of the report of Aisha was better than... and a small upright group is better than a large sinful multitude. In his statement: 'preference of the number of narrators' there is an indication that a number does not take precedence over a number after both are in the degree of ahad. But if there is one on one side and two on the other, the report of two is given precedence over the report of one. Some said: the side of multitude is given preference over the side of few, adhering to what Muhammad [ibn al-Hasan] mentioned in the issues of water, but we left it by istihsan. Most men, and Bilal because he was better than most free women, no one is given preference except in a report where the situation was more evident to men than women, then the report of men is considered, not the report of women. As it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) performed the solar eclipse prayer and bowed once in each rak'ah, so we acted upon it and left what Aisha narrated that he bowed twice in each rak'ah; because women were behind the rows in the mosque, and men were near the imam, so his situation was fully evident to men due to their proximity, not to women due to their distance from the imam. Thus it is said. (al-Qamar) 'was better' means in integrity, memory, and precision. (al-Qamar) 'was better' means in integrity and precision. (al-Qamar) 'and a small upright group' etc. This invalidates the English principle of approving the multitude of opinion even if the majority are ignorant, except that Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i went to preference by multitude of number because of achieving strength of probability of truthfulness through many informants. (al-Sunbuli) 'better' etc. For a small upright group produces strength of probability, unlike a sinful multitude, so the multitude is not regarded. And by this what Imam Muhammad [ibn al-Hasan] and the majority of Shafi'is said is refuted: that preference is by number of narrators due to achieving strength of probability of truthfulness through many informants. (al-Qamar) 'after both are' i.e., each of the two reports. The benefit of this restriction is that if a report reaches the level of tawatur, it is given precedence over others. (al-Qamar) 'the report of two is given precedence' etc. And it means that the report of two is from ahad as has passed. (al-Qamar) 'by what Muhammad mentioned' i.e., in the book of Istihsan from al-Mabsut: it is giving preference to the statement of two over one, for when one informs of the purity of water or the permissibility of food, for example, and two inform of its impurity or prohibition, then action is taken on their report, not his. So similarly in the chapter of reports and narrations, multitude of narrators gives preference. (al-Qamar) 'but we left it' i.e., we left giving preference to the side of multitude over the side of few by istihsan. For the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) and others of the Salaf did not give preference by number in the chapter of acting upon reports and narrations, as they gave preference by increase of memory and precision. Thus in al-Kashf. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 571

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on conflict between reports, focusing on the criteria for tarjih (preference). The author states that mere differences in the narrator's gender (masculine/feminine) or status (free/slave) do not give one report preference over another, because the relevant quality is 'adalah (integrity), which does not vary by these attributes. However, a small group of upright narrators is better than a large group of sinful ones. The author then discusses the role of number: if both reports are at the level of ahad, one number does not outweigh another equal number, but if one side has two narrators and the other one, the two are preferred. Some scholars, like Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani and Imam al-Shafi'i, argued for preference by greater number based on the principle that many informants increase the probability of truth. The Hanafis, however, reject this and rely on istihsan, noting that the Companions never gave preference by sheer number but by greater precision and memory. An illustrative example is given from the eclipse prayer: the report from men (who were closer to the imam) is preferred over the report from Aisha (who was behind), because men had better visibility, not because of any inherent superiority. This passage guards against mistakenly thinking that number or personal attributes of narrators automatically give a report more weight; instead, the focus is on the qualifying attributes of integrity and precision.

Key Terms
التعارض (al-ta'āruḍ): The apparent conflict between two or more textual evidences (here two ahad reports) that cannot both be acted upon simultaneously without preference or reconciliation.
الترجيح (al-tarjīḥ): Giving preference to one evidence over another due to a superior quality in its chain or text, making it more likely to be correct.
العدالة (al-'adālah): Integrity of a narrator: being a trustworthy Muslim who avoids major sins and does not persist on minor sins, and is upright in character.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is the report of the men about the eclipse prayer preferred over the report of Aisha?
A) Because men are more truthful than women
B) Because men were closer to the imam and thus had better visibility of his actions
C) Because the men's report had more narrators
D) Because Aisha was not present during the prayer

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, tarjih between conflicting ahad reports is based on the narrators' integrity and precision, not on number, gender, or freedom, as shown by the practice of the Companions and the eclipse prayer example.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

Nature of Istithna': Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Bayan or Mu'arada
Dispute on nature of istithna': Hanafi vs Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the nature of istithna', apply the Hanafi principle that istithna' is bayan, and evaluate the Quranic proof used by the Hanafis.

Core Idea
Istithna' in Hanafi usul is bayan, not mu'arada; it explains, it does not oppose.

The nature of istithna' (exception) is a key point of contention between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools of usul al-fiqh. This lesson examines both positions and the arguments they employ. You will learn why Hanafis view exception as a form of bayan (explanation) that clarifies the scope of a general statement, while Shafi'is view it as mu'arada (opposition) that cancels the initial ruling. The practical difference appears in cases like excepting a different genus.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
What does each school say about istithna'? State the Hanafi position (bayan) and the Shafi'i position (mu'arada).
2
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
How does the example '1000 dirhams except 100' support the opposition view? Identify the apparent contradiction.
The Shafi'i argues that the affirmation and negation cancel each other.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
How does the Quranic verse (al-Ankabut 14) prove that istithna' must be bayan? Focus on the fact that it is a report (khabar).
Reports cannot be opposed because that would create falsehood.
4
Understand the linguistic argument
How does the definition of istithna' as 'extraction' and 'speaking about what remains' support the Hanafi view?
Linguistic consensus: 'istithna' from negation is affirmation, from affirmation is negation'.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in rulings? Consider the case of excepting a different genus (e.g., '1000 dirhams except a garment').
Hanafi: invalid; Shafi'i: valid (deduct value).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكر أقسام بيان تغيير
فصل في أقسام البيان وعند الشافعي به يمنع الحكم بطريق المعارضة، يعني أن المستثنى قد حكم عليه أوّلاً في الكلام السابق، ثم أخرج بعد ذلك بطريق المعارضة، فكان تقدير قوله: "لفلان علي ألف
درهم إلا مائة" فإنها ليست عليّ، فإن صدر الكلام يوجبها والاستثناء ينفيها، فتعارضا أي المائة فتساقطا، وقيل: فائدته تظهر فيما إذا استثنى خلاف جنسه كقوله: "لفلان علي ألف
الخلاف
أي المائة
درهم إلا ثوبًا "فعندنا لا يصح الاستثناء؛ لأنه لا يصح بيانًا، وعنده يصح، فينقص من الألف قدر قيمة الثوب؛ لأن عمل الاستثناء كالدليل المعارض وهو بحسب الإمكان، والإمكان ههنا في نفي مقدار قيمته، ولا يخلو هذا عن خدشة لإجماع أهل اللغة على أن الاستثناء من النفي إثبات، ومن الإثبات نفي هذا دليل للشافعي ليه على أن عمل الاستثناء بطريق المعارضة، لأن النفى والإثبات يتعارضان معا.
ولأن قوله: "لا إله إلا الله" للتوحيد، ومعناه.
بطريق المعارضة إلخ : فالمستثنى يدلّ على حكم معارض للحكم السابق. (القمر)
فتعارضا فتساقطا إلخ فيمنع حكم السابق، وهو الإيجاب على المائة، بل يكون الإيجاب الذي هو حكم السابق على الباقي، وهو تسعمائة. (السنبلي) فتساقطا : فلم يثبت الحكم في المستثنى. (القمر) لأنه لا يصح بيانا: لكونه خلاف الجنس. (القمر) في نفي إلخ أي في نفي مقدار قيمة الثوب عن الألف. (القمر)
عن
خدشة لعل الخدشة أنه إذا وجب ردّ الثوب على القيمة تصحيحًا للاستثناء، فلا ضرورة إلى جعل الاستثناء معارضة، بل يجعل عبارة عما وراء المستثنى كذا قيل وقيل: إن الخدشة أن عمل الاستثناء بالمعارضة عند الشافعي له إنما هو في المتصل، وهذا من قبيل المنقطع. (القمر)
عن
خدشة إلخ أي جعل صحة الاستثناء في هذه الصورة من ثمرة قول الشافعي له لا يخلو عن ضعف؛ لأن المعارضة لا يتحقق إلا في محل واحد وههنا متغايران؛ لأن الحكم في صدر الكلام في الدراهم ونفيه بعد، فهو في الثوب، أو نقول : وجه الخدشة أنا لو سلمنا أن عمل الاستثناء كالدليل المعارض لكن لا نسلم أن رعاية الاستثناء يجب عليكم في كل صورة واعتبار التعارض فيه يلزمكم بحسب الإمكان حيثما يوجد حرف الاستثناء، بل إذا تحقق الإثبات والنفي في محل واحد في صورة الاستثناء فحكمه عندكم التساقط، ولا ضرورة في اعتبار التعارض بحسب الإمكان حتى نفرض التعارض ههنا باعتبار قيمة الثوب (السنبلي) بطريق المعارضة: أي أن حكم الاستثناء معارض للحكم السابق. (القمر) للتوحيد : أي الإقرار بوجوده تعالى ووحدته. (القمر)

أي الاستثناء
ذكر أقسام بيان تغيير
فصل في أقسام البيان النفي والإثبات، فلو كان تكلما بالباقي لكان نفيًا لغيره لا إثباتًا له؛ لأن المعنى حينئذ إله غير الله، فيكون نفيًا لغير الله لا إثباتًا لله الذي هو المقصود، وبخلاف ما لو حملنا على سبيل المعارضة؛ إذ يكون المعنى حينئذٍ لا إله إلا الله فإنه موجود. ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَبِثَ فِيهِمْ أَلْفَ سَنَةٍ إِلَّا خَمْسِينَ عَاما أي لبث نوح عليه في القوم ألف
(العنكبوت : ١٤ ) .
سنة إلا خمسين عاما الذي كان قبل الدعوة أو خمسين عاما الذي عاش فيه بعد غرقهم، فلو حملنا هذا الكلام على المعارضة لكان كذبًا في الخبر والقصة.
أي في القوم
وسقوط الحكم بطريق المعارضة في الإيجاب يكون لا في الإخبار فعملنا أن ليس عمل الاستثناء على المعارضة كما زعم الشافعي له. ولأن أهل اللغة قالوا: الاستثناء استخراج وتكلّم بالباقي بعد الاستثناء كما قالوا: إنه من النفي
النفي أي نفي إلهية غيره تعالى قال: والإثبات أي إثبات إلهيته تعالى (القمر) لا إثباتًا لله إلخ: لوجود السكوت عن إثبات إلهيته تعالى، فإنه صار كأنه لم يتكلم بالإثبات (القمر) لو حملنا إلخ لأنه إذا حملنا على النفي والإثبات ومنعنا حكم السابق على سبيل المعارضة، فثبت عدم حكم السابق على المستثنى. (السنبلي)
فلو حملنا هذا الكلام إلخ بأنه حكم أولا أنه عاش ألف سنة، ثم نفي عنه خمسين عاما. (القمر) بطريق المعارضة إلخ خلاصة دليلنا أنه تعالى استثنى الخمسين عن الألف في الإخبار عن لبث نوح عليه في قومه قبل الطوفان، فلو كان عمل الاستثناء بطريق المعارضة لما استقام الاستثناء في الإخبار ولا اختص بالإيجاب كدليل الخصوص؛ وذلك لأن صحة الخبر عما كان بناء على وجود المخبر به في الزمان الماضي، والمنع بطريق المعارضة إنما يتحقق في الحال، لا في زمان الماضي، وكذا في الإخبار عن أمر في المستقبل لا يتصوّر المنع بطريق المعارضة أيضًا؛ لأنه ليس بموجود، فثبت أن جعله معارضًا لا يستقيم في الإخبار؛ لأن التكلم بما بقي بحكمه لم تقبل الامتناع، بخلاف الإنشاء لأنه إثبات في الحال فإذا عارضه مانع يحتمل أن لا يثبت ألا ترى أنه لو ثبت حكم الألف بجملة، ثم عارضه الاستثناء في الخمسين لزم كونه نافيًا لما أثبته أوّلاً، فلزم الكذب في أحد الأمرين، إما الأوّل أو الثاني، عن ذلك. (السنبلي) في الإيجاب إلخ أي في الإنشاء يكون لا في الإخبار؛ لأن حكم الإنشاء قابل للرفع دون حكم الإخبار، وإلا لزم الكذب تعالى الله عن ذلك علوا كبيرًا . (القمر) استخراج: أي طلب خروج
تعالى الله
المستثنى عن المستثنى منه. (القمر) وتكلم بالباقي إلخ : أي ليس لمنع الحكم على سبيل المعارضة. (القمر)
Mention of sections of bayan taghyir. Chapter on types of bayan: According to al-Shafi'i, it prevents the ruling by way of opposition, meaning that the excepted thing was first ruled upon in the previous speech, then it is extracted afterwards by way of opposition. So the interpretation of his statement: 'So-and-so owes me one thousand dirhams except one hundred' is that it is not owed by me. For the first part of the speech obligates it, and the exception negates it. So they oppose each other, i.e., the hundred, and they fall. And it is said: its benefit appears when one excepts something of a different genus, like his statement: 'So-and-so owes me one thousand dirhams except a garment.' Then according to us, the exception is not valid because it is not valid as a bayan. According to him, it is valid, so he deducts from the thousand the value of the garment, because the operation of exception is like a counter-evidence, and it is according to possibility, and possibility here is in negating the amount of its value. This is not free from a defect due to the consensus of the people of language that exception from negation is affirmation, and from affirmation is negation. This is evidence for al-Shafi'i that the operation of exception is by way of opposition, because negation and affirmation oppose each other. And because his statement: 'There is no god but Allah' is for tawhid, and its meaning... [continues with marginal commentary]. ... And for us is His statement: 'He remained among them a thousand years except fifty years' (al-Ankabut: 14). So if we applied this statement to opposition, it would be a lie in the report and the story. And the dropping of the ruling by way of opposition is in obligation (insha') not in reports (ikhbar). So we know that the operation of exception is not on opposition as al-Shafi'i claimed. And because the people of language said: Exception is extraction and speaking about what remains after exception, as they said: it is from negation...
Source pages p. 582

Commentary
This passage from Noorulanwaar explains the Hanafi position on the nature of istithna' (exception) in legal language, arguing against Imam al-Shafi'i's view that it operates via mu'arada (opposition). The author begins by presenting the Shafi'i view: the excepted item initially receives a ruling, then the exception opposes that ruling, causing them to cancel out. He gives examples like 'I owe you 1000 dirhams except 100' where the exception opposes the affirmation. Then he presents the Shafi'i argument that if the exception is of a different genus (e.g., a garment instead of dirhams), it is still valid and deducts the value. The Hanafi response follows. First, a rational objection: if exception were opposition, then the Quranic verse about Nuh's age (1000 minus 50) would be false because affirming 1000 then opposing 50 would create a contradiction in a report. But reports are about past facts and cannot be opposed; opposition only works in commands (insha'). Second, linguistic consensus: exception is defined as 'extraction' (istikhraj) and speaking about the remainder, not as opposition. The phrase 'La ilaha illa Allah' is explained as negation of others and affirmation of Allah, not simply as two opposing statements. Thus, the Hanafis maintain that istithna' is a form of bayan (explanation) that clarifies the scope of the general statement without contradicting it. The practical difference (thamara) appears in cases like excepting a different genus: Hanafis invalidate it, Shafi'is validate it by deducting value.

Key Terms
الاستثناء (al-istithnā'): Exception: extracting something from a general statement, with the meaning of speaking about what remains after the extraction.
المعارضة (al-mu'āraḍa): Opposition or contradiction between two rulings, causing them to cancel out.
البيان (al-bayān): Elucidation or clarification of a general statement by specifying what is excluded.
الخبر (al-khabar): A report or informative statement about a past or future event; it must be true or false.
الإنشاء (al-inshā'): A performative statement that creates a ruling (e.g., commands, prohibitions); it can be subject to opposition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how does istithna' (exception) operate in legal language?
A) By opposition (mu'arada) that cancels the initial ruling.
B) By explanation (bayan) that extracts the excepted item without contradiction.
C) By abrogation (naskh) of the general statement.
D) By restriction (takhsis) only in commands, not reports.

Key Takeaway
Istithna' in Hanafi usul is a form of bayan (explanation) that clarifies the scope of a general statement without involving opposition.

Tabdil as Bayan and the Hanafi Proof of Naskh
Explains tabdil and proves naskh against Jewish objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi concept of tabdil as a division of bayan, state the proof for naskh, and identify the proper locus of naskh.

Core Idea
Tabdil is a change in the perceived ruling due to changing benefits, while naskh is permissible and proven by Quran and reason.

In this passage, the author explores tabdil (change/alteration) as one of the divisions of bayan (clarification). Using the analogy of killing to illustrate how divine decrees appear to change from a human perspective, he then defends the permissibility and occurrence of naskh (abrogation) against the objections of the Jews. He also defines the proper subject of naskh, excluding eternal rulings and temporally limited ones.

Guided Path
1
Understand tabdil as a type of bayan
Identify that tabdil is a division of bayan meaning a change in the ruling from the perspective of people, while in God's knowledge it was always predetermined. The analogy of killing shows how a life term appears cut short but was fixed in divine knowledge.
This parallels the concept of qada and qadar.
2
Analyze the analogy of killing
The author compares divine decree to a person killing another: the killer changes the perceived life term of the victim, but God had already decreed the moment of death. This illustrates how tabdil does not imply change in God's knowledge.
It shows that human perception of change does not affect divine immutability.
3
Identify the dispute with Jews and the Hanafi response
The Jews argue that naskh implies foolishness (safah) and ignorance in God, aiming to protect the eternity of Moses' law. The Hanafi response uses Quran 2:106 and a rational analogy: God as a wise physician who changes prescriptions according to changing needs.
The physician analogy is a rational proof (dalil aqli) that naskh is consistent with wisdom.
4
Define the mahall al-naskh and its conditions
The passage defines the proper locus of naskh: a ruling that is possible to exist and not exist, i.e., a practical, contingent ruling. Eternal matters like faith and disbelief cannot be abrogated, nor can temporally limited rulings be considered naskh when they expire.
This definition helps distinguish between true naskh and natural expiration of a command.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا بمنزلة القتل إذا قتل إنسان إنسانًا، فإنه بيان لموته المقدرة في علم الله تعالى وتبديل بيان التبديل في حق الناس؛ لأنهم يظنون أنه لو لم يقتل لعاش إلى مدة أخرى، فقد قطع القاتل عليه أي باعتبار ظنهم أجله، ولهذا يجب عليه القصاص والدية في الدنيا والعقاب في الآخرة. وهو جائز عندنا بالنص الذي تلونا قبل ذلك خلافًا لليهود لعنهم الله تعالى- فإنهم يقولون: تلزم منه سفاهة الله تعالى والجهل بعواقب الأمور، وهو لا يصلح للألوهية، وغرضهم من ذلك أن لا تنسخ شريعة موسى عليه بشريعة أحد، ويكون دينه مؤبدا، ونحن نقول: إن الله تعالى حكيم يعلم مصالح العباد وحوائجهم، فيحكم كل يوم على حسب علمه ومصلحته كالطبيب يحكم للمريض بشرب دواء وأكل غذاء اليوم، ثم غدًا بخلاف ذلك، فإنه لا يحكم بسفاهته، بل هو عاقل حاذق يعطي كل يوم على ما يجد مزاجه فيه، و لم يقل من المريض: إني أبدلّك غذاءً بغذاء أو دواء آخر، وقد صح أن في شريعة آدم عليا كان نكاح الجزء أعني حوّاء حلالاً، وكذا نكاح الأخوات للأخ حلالاً، ثم نسخ في شريعة نوح علينا. ومحله حكم يحتمل الوجود والعدم في نفسه بأن يكون أمرًا ممكنا عمليًا ولا يكون واجبًا لذاته كالإيمان، ولا ممتنعا لذاته كالكفر، فإن وجوب الإيمان وحرمة الكفر لا ينسخ في دين من الأديان، ولا يقبل النسخ، ولم يلتحق به ما ينافي النسخ من توقيت. وقد قالوا في نظيره: تَمَتَّعُوا فِي دَارِكُمْ ثَلاثَةَ أَيَّام خطاباً لقوم صالح عليه، وتَزْرَعُونَ سَبْعَ سنينَ دَأَبا حكايةً عن قول يوسف عليه كل ذلك غلط، لأنه من الأخبار والقصص، والأولى في نظيره قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْفُوا وَاصْفَحُوا حَتَّى يَأْتِيَ اللَّهُ بِأَمْرِهِ﴾ (البقرة: ١٠٩)
This is like killing: if a person kills another, it is a clarification of his death predestined in God's knowledge and a change (tabdil) of the clarification of change in the view of people, because they assume that if he had not been killed, he would have lived for another term, so the killer has cut off his term according to their assumption. Therefore, retaliation and blood money are required in this world and punishment in the Hereafter. And it (tabdil) is permissible according to us by the text we recited before, contrary to the Jews—may God curse them—for they say: It implies foolishness of God and ignorance of consequences, and it is not fitting for divinity. Their aim is that the law of Moses should not be abrogated by the law of anyone, and his religion be made eternal. And we say: God is wise, knowing the interests and needs of His servants; He decrees every day according to His knowledge and wisdom, like a physician who prescribes for a patient a medicine and a diet today, and tomorrow the opposite; he is not considered foolish but is a clever expert who gives each day according to what he finds in his temperament. And the patient does not say: 'I have changed your diet for another diet or another medicine.' And it is established that in the law of Adam (AS), marriage to one's own part (i.e., Eve) was permissible, and likewise marriage to sisters was permissible for a brother, then it was abrogated in the law of Noah (AS). And its proper locus (mahall) is a ruling that is possible to exist and not exist in itself, i.e., it must be a practical possible matter, not existentially necessary like faith, nor existentially impossible like disbelief, for the obligation of faith and the prohibition of disbelief are not abrogated in any religion, and do not accept abrogation. Nor is attached to it that which is incompatible with abrogation, such as temporal limitation (tawqit). They said regarding its equivalent: 'Enjoy yourselves in your abode for three days' as addressed to the people of Salih, and 'You will sow for seven years continuously' as a narration from the saying of Yusuf—all that is incorrect, because it is from reports and stories. The more appropriate example is the verse: 'So pardon and forgive until God brings His command' (Quran 2:109).
Source pages p. 592

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the division of bayan (clarification/statement) into tabdil (change/alteration). The author uses the analogy of killing to illustrate tabdil: when someone is killed, from the perspective of people, his life term is changed (cut short), whereas in God's knowledge his death time was fixed. This tabdil is permissible according to Muslims by the textual proof (Quran 2:106) mentioned earlier, contrary to the Jews. The Jews argue that tabdil implies God's foolishness and ignorance, and they deny naskh (abrogation) to preserve the eternity of Moses' law. The Hanafi response is that God is wise and changes laws according to changing benefits, just as a wise physician changes prescriptions. Historical examples from the shariahs of Adam and Noah confirm that naskh occurred. The passage then defines the proper locus (mahall) of naskh: it must be a legal ruling that is possible to exist and not exist, not like the obligation of faith (always required) or the prohibition of disbelief (always prohibited). Moreover, temporally limited rulings (muwaqqat) cannot be abrogated before their time; after their time they expire naturally, which is not called naskh. Examples of temporal limitations are given but critiqued as not true legal rulings (being reports or stories). The preferred example is Quran 2:109 which commands pardon until God's command comes, implying a temporary ruling that was later abrogated by the command to fight.

Key Terms
تبديل (tabdīl): A division of bayan meaning the change of a ruling in the view of people due to a change in benefit, while in God's knowledge it was always predetermined.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation: the lifting of a legal ruling by a later divine address.
محل النسخ (maḥall al-naskh): The proper subject of abrogation: a legal ruling that is possible to exist and not exist, not eternal or temporally limited.
توقيت (tawqīt): Temporal limitation: a ruling specified for a certain time, which cannot be abrogated before that time, and after which it expires naturally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the proper locus (mahall) of naskh?
A) Any ruling that is eternally obligatory or prohibited
B) A ruling that is temporally limited (muwaqqat)
C) A ruling that is possible to exist and not exist, not being eternally necessary or impossible
D) A ruling that is based on rational necessity

Key Takeaway
Naskh is a valid mechanism in Islamic law, grounded in divine wisdom and proven by both revelation and reason.

Ijtihad Ruling Not Overturned by Subsequent Revelation
Derives a usul rule from the Badr captives incident

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that an ijtihadi ruling remains valid even if a later revealed text contradicts it, by analyzing the Badr captives incident and distinguishing between revelation after vs. before the ruling.

Core Idea
An ijtihadi ruling stands despite later textual contradiction, provided the text came after the ruling was executed.

One of the most delicate issues in usul al-fiqh is the relationship between ijtihad and revelation. Does a later revealed text automatically overturn a prior ijtihadi ruling? The Hanafi school, drawing on the incident of the captives of Badr, establishes a clear principle: if the revelation comes after the ruling was implemented, the ruling remains valid and its consequences (like ownership of spoils) are not undone. This lesson unpacks that principle and its derivation from the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ijtihadi ruling
Locate in the passage the ijtihadi ruling made by the Prophet (ﷺ) before revelation. It was his decision to accept ransom from the captives of Badr.
2
Identify the revealed text
Find the Quranic verses that came after the ruling (Surah al-Anfal 8:67-69). Note their content: they criticize the action but then permit eating the spoils.
3
Analyze the effect on the ruling
Observe that the Prophet (ﷺ) did not reverse his ruling; he ordered the companions to eat the spoils and did not demand return of the ransom. The revelation did not annul the previous decision.
The passage emphasizes that the ruling was 'not overturned' despite the criticism.
4
Derive the usul principle
Generalize: if a revealed text appears after an ijtihadi ruling, the ruling remains valid. The basis is that the revelation itself allowed the spoils, implying legal effectiveness of the prior ijtihad.
This is the Hanafi rule: the ijtihadi ruling is not annulled by later nass.
5
Contrast with the opposite case
Understand the second scenario: if the text existed before the ijtihad but was unknown, the ruling is invalid. The passage distinguishes between 'revelation after ruling' (no annulment) and 'appearance of text contrary to opinion' (annulment).
This distinction is crucial for correct application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أقسام الوحي
فصل في أفعال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالوا: قبلنا، فلما أخذوا الفداء نزل عليه قوله تعالى: مَا كَانَ لِنَبِيٍّ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهُ أَسْرَى حَتَّى يُشْخِنَ فِي الْأَرْضِ تُرِيدُونَ عَرَضَ الدُّنْيَا وَاللَّهُ يُرِيدُ الْآخِرَةَ وَاللَّهُ عَزِيزٌ حَكِيمٌ لَوْلَا كِتَابٌ مِنَ اللَّهِ سَبَقَ لَمَسَّكُمْ فِيمَا أَخَذْتُمْ عَذَابٌ عَظِيمٌ فَكُلُوا مِمَّا غَنِمْتُمْ حَلالاً طَيِّباً وَاتَّقُوا اللَّهَ إِنَّ اللَّهَ غَفُورٌ رَحِيمٌ فبكى
(الأنفال: ٦٧ - ٦٩ )
، 
رسول الله ، وبكى الصحابة كلهم وقال لو نزل العذاب ما نجا أحدٌ منا إلا عمر
ومعاذ بن سعد، فظهر أن الحق هو رأي عمر منه نه، وأن النبي عليه أخطأ حين عمل برأي أبي بكر الله لكنه لم يقرّر على الخطأ، بل تنبه عليه بإنزال الآيات، وأمضى الحكم على الفداء، وأمر بأكله، ولم يأمر بردّ الفداء وحرمته، وهذا هو الفرق بين نزول النص بخلاف
الرأي وبين ظهوره بخلافه، فإن في الأول لا ينقض الرأي بالنص، وفي الثاني ينقض به.
وهذا كالإلهام أي الفرق بين اجتهاد النبي عليه وغيره من المجتهدين كالفرق بين إلهام أي اجتهادة
فقالوا قبلنا وقد وقع ذلك، فإنه قتل يوم أحد سبعون من الصحابة له كذا في "صحيح البخاري".(القمر) حتى يُثخن أي يبالغ في قتل المشركين والأسارى جمع الأسير. وعرض الدنيا أي متاعها. (القمر) كتاب من الله: أي لو لا حكم الله سبق في اللوح المحفوظ، وهو أن المجتهد لا يؤاخذ وإن أخطأ.(القمر)
إلا عمر لكون رأيه مطابقا للوحي في ذالك (السنبلي) ومعاذ بن سعد وفي "معالم التنزيل": وسعيد بن معاذ، فإنه قال يا رسول الله، الإثخان في القتل أحب إلي من استيفاء الرجال. (القمر) فظهر أن الحق إلخ وظهر أيضا أن الحكم الاجتهادي لا ينقض وإن يظهر الخطاء ، وأن ما يؤخذ بالحكم الاجتهادي حلال طيب وإن يظهر الخطاء . (القمر) وبين ظهوره أي ظهور النص، بخلاف الرأي،
وقيل: أي ظهور ما وقع في الرأي بخلاف النص. (القمر) في الأول : أي في نزول النص بخلاف الرأي. (القمر) في الأول إلخ وجه عدم نقض الرأي نزول النص بعد الحكم على الرأي، ولهذا أمر بأكله، ولم يَرُدّ الفداء، ولم يأمر بحرمته، ووجه نقض الرأي في الثاني هو تقدّم النص على الرأي. (السنبلي وفي الثاني: أي ظهور النص بخلاف الرأي وقيل أي ظهور الرأي بخلاف النص ينقض الرأي به أي بالنص. (القمر)
أخرج ذلك القصة البغوي في تفسيره وابن أبي شيبة وأحمد والترمذي وحسنه وابن المنذر وابن أبي حاتم والطبراني وابن مردوية والحاكم وصححه والبيهقي في الدلائل عن الأعمش عن عمرو بن مُرّة عن أبي عبيد الله بن مسعود ده بألفاظ تقارب هذا. [إشراق الأبصار ٢٧]
عن عبد الله
Explanation of the divisions of revelation. Chapter on the actions of the Prophet, peace be upon him: They said: we accepted. When they took the ransom, the revelation descended upon him: 'It is not for a prophet to have captives until he has made slaughter in the land. You desire the goods of this world, but Allah desires the Hereafter. And Allah is Exalted in Might, Wise. If not for a decree from Allah that preceded, you would have been struck for what you took by a great punishment. So eat from what you have captured, lawful and good, and fear Allah. Indeed, Allah is Forgiving and Merciful.' (Surah al-Anfal 8:67-69). So the Messenger of Allah wept, and all the companions wept, and he said: 'If the punishment had descended, none of us would have been saved except Umar and Mu'adh ibn Sa'd.' So it became clear that the truth was the opinion of Umar, and that the Prophet erred when he acted on the opinion of Abu Bakr, but he was not settled upon error; rather, he was alerted to it by the sending down of the verses, and he carried out the ruling on the ransom and ordered them to eat it, and did not order the return of the ransom or its prohibition. This is the difference between the revelation of the text contrary to the opinion and the appearance of the opinion contrary to the text. In the first case, the opinion is not annulled by the text; in the second, it is annulled by it. This is like inspiration [ilham], i.e., the difference between the ijtihad of the Prophet and that of other mujtahids is like the difference between inspiration and ijtihad. They said: we accepted, and that occurred: seventy of the companions were killed on the day of Uhud because of it. Such is in Sahih al-Bukhari. (Al-Qamar): 'until he makes slaughter' i.e., he kills many of the polytheists. 'captives' plural of captive. 'goods of this world' i.e., its benefits. (Al-Qamar): 'a decree from Allah' i.e., if not for a judgment from Allah that preceded in the Preserved Tablet, which is that the mujtahid is not held accountable even if he errs. (Al-Qamar): 'except Umar' because his opinion agreed with revelation in that. (Al-Sunbulī): 'and Mu'adh ibn Sa'd' and in 'Ma'alim al-Tanzil': 'Said ibn Mu'adh' as he said: O Messenger of Allah, killing many is more beloved to me than taking men. (Al-Qamar): 'So it became clear that the truth...' etc. And it also became clear that the ijtihadi ruling is not annulled even if error appears, and that what is taken by the ijtihadi ruling is lawful and good even if error appears. (Al-Qamar): 'and between its appearance' i.e., the appearance of the text contrary to the opinion, and it is said: the appearance of what occurred in the opinion contrary to the text. (Al-Qamar): 'in the first' i.e., in the revelation of the text contrary to the opinion. (Al-Qamar): 'in the first etc.' The reason for not annulling the opinion is the revelation of the text after the ruling on the opinion, and for this he ordered its eating, and did not return the ransom, and did not order its prohibition. The reason for annulling the opinion in the second is the precedence of the text over the opinion. (Al-Sunbulī): 'and in the second' i.e., the appearance of the text contrary to the opinion, and it is said: the appearance of the opinion contrary to the text, the opinion is annulled by it, i.e., by the text. (Al-Qamar): Al-Baghawi narrated that story in his tafsir, and Ibn Abi Shaybah, Ahmad, al-Tirmidhi (who deemed it hasan), Ibn al-Mundhir, Ibn Abi Hatim, al-Tabarani, Ibn Mardawayh, al-Hakim (who deemed it sahih), and al-Bayhaqi in al-Dala'il, from al-A'mash from 'Amr ibn Murrah from Abu 'Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud, with similar wording. [Ishraq al-Absar 27] From 'Abdullah.
Source pages p. 612

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule derived from the historical incident of the captives of Badr. It clarifies the distinction between two scenarios: (1) when a revealed text (nass) comes down after an ijtihadi ruling has been made, and (2) when the text already existed but the mujtahid was unaware of it. In the first scenario, the ijtihadi ruling is not overturned; it remains valid because it was based on valid ijtihad at the time. The Prophet's ruling to accept ransom was not reversed even after the Quranic verses showed it was a mistake; instead, the spoils were declared lawful. In the second scenario, if the text had already been revealed but the mujtahid contradicted it, then the ijtihad is invalid and must be overturned. The passage also draws an analogy to inspiration (ilham): the Prophet's ijtihad is like his inspiration, both being decisive for him, whereas the ijtihad of ordinary mujtahids is like the inspiration of awliya (saints) — it is not absolutely binding. The commentary emphasizes that the ijtihadi ruling is not annulled even if error becomes apparent, and that what is taken based on ijtihad is lawful. This principle is fundamental in Hanafi usul: a mujtahid's prior ruling remains effective despite later evidence of error, to maintain legal stability.

Key Terms
اجتهاد (ijtihad): Independent legal reasoning to derive a ruling from the sources when no clear text exists.
نص (nass): A clear textual ruling from the Quran or Sunnah that is explicit and unambiguous.
إلهام (ilham): Inspiration; a form of divine guidance not conveyed through formal revelation (wahy).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Badr captives incident, what happens if a revealed text comes after an ijtihadi ruling that is contrary to it?
A) The ijtihadi ruling is annulled and the spoils must be returned.
B) The ijtihadi ruling remains valid and the spoils are lawful.
C) The ruling is invalid but the spoils are still forbidden.
D) The ruling is suspended until a consensus is reached.

Key Takeaway
An ijtihadi ruling is not overturned by a later revealed text that contradicts it; the ruling remains valid and its consequences (like ownership of spoils) are lawful.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Taqlid of a Companion: Hanafi Position and Dispute
Dispute over the binding authority of Companion statements in legal derivation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on taqlid of a Companion, distinguish the views of al-Karkhi and al-Shafi'i, and apply the rule to examples like the minimum of menstruation.

Core Idea
A Companion's statement overrides qiyas because their proximity to revelation gives their opinions stronger authority.

This passage addresses a fundamental dispute in usul al-fiqh: does the statement of a Companion constitute a binding proof for later jurists? The Hanafi school affirms it, the Shafi'i denies it, and al-Karkhi offers a middle path. Understanding this debate is crucial for knowing how to weigh a Companion's opinion against analogical reasoning in legal derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
Is taqlid of a Companion obligatory, and in what scope? The passage presents multiple responses.
2
Examine the Hanafi argument
Why does a Companion's statement override qiyas, even if it is his own ijtihad? Because they witnessed revelation and have insight.
3
Analyze al-Karkhi's restriction
Taqlid is only wajib in matters not accessible to qiyas, because otherwise the Companion may have erred in his own reasoning.
4
Consider the Shafi'i objection
Companions disagreed among themselves, so no single opinion is binding; none is more entitled than another.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response and examples
The practice of the school (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn) is on taqlid in matters not comprehended by qiyas, e.g., minimum menstruation from A'ishah.

Source Text

فصل في أفعال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم
بيان تقليد الصحابي

وتقليد الصحابي الله واجب يترك به القياس أي قياس التابعين ومن بعدهم؛ لأن قياس الصحابي الله لا يترك بقول صحابي به آخر لاحتمال السماع من الرسول ، بل نه الظاهر في حقه وإن لم يسند إليه، ولئن سلّم أنه ليس مسموعا منه بل هو رأيه، فرأي الصحابي الله أقوى من رأي غيرهم؛ لأنهم شاهدوا أحوال التنزيل وأسرار الشريعة فلهم مزية على غيرهم. وقال الكرخي له: لا يجب تقليده إلا فيما لا يدرك بالقياس؛ لأنه حينئذ يتعيّن جهة السماع منه ، بخلاف ما إذا كان مدركا بالقياس؛ لأنه يحتمل أن يكون هو رأيه وأخطأ فيه، فلا يكون حجة على غيره.

وقال الشافعي له: لا يقلّد أحد منهم سواء كان مدركًا بالقياس أو لا ؛ لأن الصحابة ريال كان يخالف بعضهم بعضا، وليس أحدهم أولى من الآخر، فتعين البطلان. وقد اتفق عمل أصحابنا بالتقليد فيما لا يعقل بالقياس يعني أن أبا حنيفة لله وصاحبيه كلهم متفقون بتقليد الصحابي الله كما في أقل الحيض، فإن العقل قاصر بدركه، فعملنا جميعًا بما قالت عائشة : أقل الحيض للجارية البكر والثيب ثلاثة أيام ولياليها، وأكثره عشرة. وشراء ما باع بأقل مما باع قبل نقد الثمن الأول؛ فإن القياس يقتضي جوازه، وهذا في الأمور التي لا تُدرك بالقياس مشكل كذا قيل (القمر) أو لا أي لا يكون مدركا بالقياس كالمقادير الشرعية. (القمر) فتعيّن البطلان ولو كان ما قاله الصحابي المسموعا من الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم لرفعه إلى ولما لم يرفعه عُلم أنه من اجتهاده واجتهاده واجتهاد غيره مساويان في احتمال الخطاء ؛ لعدم ,عصمته، فلا يكون حجة، وهذا فيما يُدرك بالقياس، وأما فيما لا يُدرك بالقياس فيجوز أن الصحابي له إنما أفتى به لخبر ظنه دليلا، ولا يكون كذالك، فمع جواز أن لا يكون دليلا كيف يلزم غيره، فلا يكون حجة. (القمر) فيما لا يعقل إلخ اعلم ما لا يدرك بالقياس فله نوعان أحدهما ما لا يُعقل أصلاً، بل العقل قاصر بدركه، وثانيهما: ما لا يكون مدركًا بالقياس، بل كان القياس مخالفًا له بأن يقتضي القياس خلافه. (السنبلي) أقل الحيض: فإن تقديره لا يُعرف بالقياس.(القمر) وشراء ما باع إلخ صورته أن يبيع الرجل عرضًا من رجل بثمن مؤجل، ثم اشترى ذالك البائع ذالك من المشتري بأقل من الثمن الأول قبل نقد الثمن الأول، فهذا الشراء حرام فاسد ولقائل أن يقول: إن هذا المثال لا يصلح؛ فإن فساد هذا البيع مما يُدرك بالرأي والقياس؛ فإن البائع الأول لما اشترى بأقل من الثمن الأول قبل نقده حصل المبيع في ملك البائع الأول، وهذا القدر الأول سقط من ذمة المشترى الأول، والزيادة عليه بقي ذمته مع خروج المبيع عن ملكه، فكان البائع الأول حصل هذا القدر الباقي بلا ,بدل فاشتبه بالربا، والربا وشبهته كلاهما محرمان فلذا حكم بفساد هذا العقد، نعم، إن وعيد بطلان الحج والجهاد لا يحصل بالقياس، فلا بد من سماع عائشة لها هذا الوعيد من النبي . (القمر) يقتضي جوازه فإن الملك في البيع الأول قد تم بقبض المشتري الأول وإن لم ينقد الثمن، وهو المجوّز للتصرّف فينبغي أن يصح العقد الثاني كما يصح العقد إذا اشترى البائع الأولُ من المشترى الأول بمثل الثمن الأول قبل نقد الثمن الأول. (القمر)
أخرجه الدار قطني مع اختلاف لفظ، كذا أفاده بحر العلوم وقد مرّ تخريجه سابقا من قول النبي ، وفيما ذكر والله ، قدس سره محل نظر ؛ لأن التقليد ههنا قد وقع للحديث المرفوع المذكور سابقا، لا لقول عائشة [إشراق الأبصار ٢٧]
Section on the Actions of the Prophet (peace be upon him): Explanation of Taqlid of a Companion. Taqlid of a Companion is obligatory, and qiyas (of the Followers and those after them) is abandoned because of it. For the qiyas of a Companion is not abandoned by the statement of another Companion due to the possibility that he heard from the Messenger, rather it is apparent in his case even if he does not attribute it. And even if it is conceded that it is not heard from him but is his own opinion, the opinion of a Companion is stronger than the opinion of others because they witnessed the circumstances of revelation and the secrets of the Shari'ah, so they have a merit over others. Al-Karkhi said: Taqlid of him is not obligatory except in matters not perceivable by qiyas, because then the channel of hearing from him is determined; unlike if it is perceivable by qiyas, because then it may be his opinion and he erred in it, so it is not a proof over others. Al-Shafi'i said: No one of them is to be followed, whether it is perceivable by qiyas or not, because the Companions differed among themselves, and none is more entitled than another, so invalidity is determined. And the practice of our school is agreed on taqlid in what is not comprehended by qiyas, meaning that Abu Hanifa and his two companions are all agreed on taqlid of a Companion, as in the minimum of menstruation, for reason is incapable of perceiving it, so we all acted upon what A'ishah said: The minimum of menstruation for a virgin and a non-virgin is three days and nights, and its maximum is ten. And the case of buying what one sold for less than what one sold before paying the first price: qiyas requires its permissibility... This is in matters not perceivable by qiyas, problematic... The hadith was narrated by al-Daraqutni with variant wording, as stated by Bahr al-Ulum...
Source pages p. 616

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute regarding the legal authority of the statements and actions of the Companions (taqlid al-sahabi). The author presents the Hanafi position first: Taqlid of a Companion is obligatory, overriding qiyas because the Companion's statement carries a strong presumption of being based on direct hearing from the Prophet, even if not explicitly attributed. Their first-hand experience of revelation gives their opinions greater weight. Then the author introduces al-Karkhi's restriction: Taqlid is only obligatory in matters inaccessible to qiyas (like fixed quantities), because otherwise the Companion might be relying on his own fallible reasoning. Finally, the Shafi'i position: no Companion can be followed absolutely because they disagreed, and none has authority over another. The Hanafis respond by citing cases where they follow Companions (e.g., A'ishah's report on minimum menstruation) and explain that in matters not reachable by qiyas, the presumption of hearing is stronger. The example of buying back a sold item at a lower price is discussed: qiyas permits it, but the Hanafis prohibit it based on a Companion's practice? Actually, the text debates whether this example is appropriate. The marginal notes clarify that the actual basis is a hadith, not just the Companion's saying. The passage ends noting that the ruling in that case rests on a marfu' hadith, not on A'ishah's statement alone.

Key Terms
التقليد (al-taqlid): Following someone's statement or action without examining the evidence, presuming they are correct.
الصحابي (al-sahabi): A person who met the Prophet as a believer and died as a Muslim, specifically a mujtahid Companion.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical deduction from a revealed text to a new case based on a common illah (effective cause).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school presented in this passage, when is taqlid of a Companion considered obligatory?
A) In all matters, even those known by qiyas
B) Only in matters not perceivable by qiyas, according to al-Karkhi
C) Never, because Companions differed
D) Only when the Companion is a mujtahid and his statement is attributed to the Prophet

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a Companion's statement overrides qiyas in matters not reachable by qiyas, but there is ikhtilaf on its binding force in matters open to analogical reasoning.
