Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
12 min
Ruling on Taqlid of a Tabi'i and Its Effect on Ijma
Hanafi usul dispute on Tabi'i authority and ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on taqlid of a Tabi'i and evaluate its impact on the consensus of the Companions.

Core Idea
A Tabi'i's opinion does not bind, but it is counted in consensus; opposition of a Tabi'i prevents completion of ijma of the Companions.

This passage examines the authority of the Tabi'i in Hanafi usul, using two historical examples to demonstrate that a Tabi'i's ijtihad is valid but does not override a Companion's view. It then clarifies Abu Hanifa's ruling that one does not blindly follow a Tabi'i, and concludes with a key dispute with al-Shafi'i regarding the Tabi'i's role in consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main characters
In the first story, Shuraih (a Tabi'i judge) opposed Ali (RA). In the second, Masruq (a Tabi'i) opposed Ibn Abbas (RA). Determine who is the Companion and who is the Tabi'i.
Shuraih is a Tabi'i who was a qadi; Masruq was a prominent Tabi'i scholar.
2
Understand the conflict
Shuraih opposed Ali's ruling that a son's testimony for his father is acceptable. Masruq opposed Ibn Abbas's ruling that a vow to slaughter a son requires one hundred camels, arguing instead for a sheep.
Note that in both cases the Tabi'i gave an independent ijtihad that differed from the Companion.
3
Observe the reaction
Ali did not deny Shuraih's decision; he accepted the judgment and even gifted the Jew a horse. When Masruq gave his opinion, no one among the Companions denied it, and Ibn Abbas later agreed with him.
The Companions tolerated the Tabi'i's ijtihad, showing its validity, but they did not adopt it over their own.
4
Extract the principle
Abu Hanifa states: 'I do not make taqlid of the Tabi'i.' The reason given is that the Tabi'i lacks the direct companionship of the Prophet and the blessing that accompanies it, which makes the Companion's opinion more reliable.
This ruling applies when the Tabi'i's fatwa appears in the time of the Companions and opposes them.
5
Analyze the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Sarakhsi explains that the real dispute is whether the Tabi'i is counted in the ijma of the Companions. According to the Hanafis, he is counted, so his opposition prevents the ijma from being complete. According to al-Shafi'i, he is not counted, so the ijma stands despite his opposition.
The chosen view (mukhtar) of Shams al-A'imma is that the Tabi'i is counted, consistent with Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أفعال النبي بيان تقليد الصحابي فقال شريح: أما شهادة مولاك فقد أجزتها لك؛ لأنه صار مُعتَقًا، وأما شهادة ابنك لك فلا أجيزها لك. وكان من مذهب على الله أنه يجوز شهادة الابن للأب، وخالفه شريح في ذلك، فلم ينكره علي الله فسلم الدرع لليهودي، فقال اليهودي: أمير المؤمنين مشى معي عليه. إلى قاضيه، فقضى عليه، فرضي به صدقت والله إنها لدرعك، وأسلم اليهودي، فسلّم أي يأمير المؤمنين الدرع عليه لليهودي، ووهبه فرساً، وكان معه حتى استشهد في حرب صفين، وهكذا مسروق كان تابعيًا خالف ابن عباس هما في مسألة النذر بذبح الولد فإن ابن عباس يقول: من نذر بذبح الولد يلزمه مائة إبل قياسًا على دية النفس، فقال مسروق: لا، بل يلزمه ذبح شاة استدلالًا بفداء إسماعيل عليها، فلم ينكره أحد، فصار إجماعا، و روي عن أبي حنيفة الله أني لا أقلّد التابعي؛ لأنهم رجال ونحن رجال، لأن قول الصحابي له إنما يقبل لاحتمال السماع وإصابة رأيهم ببركة صحبة النبي عليه وهو مفقود في التابعي، وهو مختار شمس الأئمة، وهذا كله إن ظهرت فتواه في زمن الصحابة ميم [؟]، وإن لم تظهر فتواه و لم يزاحمهم في الرأي كان مثل سائر أئمة الفتوى لا يصح تقليده. صفين بالصاد ثم الفاء على وزن سكين موضع وقع فيه الحرب بينه وبين معاوية لها. (القمر) على دية النفس أي المقتولة خطأ، وفي غرر الأحكام الدية ألف دينار من الذهب، وعشرة آلاف درهم من الفضة، ومائة من الإبل فقط . (القمر) استدلالا بفداء إسماعيل عليا: فإنه لما أمر إبراهيم عليها بذبح الولد، واستعد له، وألقى الولد على الأرض، وأخذ الشفرة بيده وأمَرِّها على رقبته جاء جبرائيل عليه بالكبش فدية، وقصته في القرآن المجيد. (القمر) فلم ينكره أحد حتى أن عباس لما أخبر بهذا القول قال: وأنا أرى مثل ذالك. (القمر) وروي عن أبي حنيفة لله هذه رواية ظاهر الرواية، وما ذكر في المتن رواية النوادر. (القمر) أني لا أقلّد إلخ وفي رواية عنه: إذا اجتمعت الصحابة لله سلّمناهم، وإذا جاء التابعون زاحمناهم. كذا في " التقرير"، قلت: وإن صح هذا فيُرشدك إلى أن اجتماع الصحابة يوجب العمل ولا عبرة بالتابعين عند حضر تهم. (السنبلي) وهو مختار شمس الأئمة وذكر الإمام السرخسي له أنه لا خلاف في أنه لا يترك القياس بقول التابعي، وإنما الخلاف في أنه هل يعتدّ بالتابعي في إجماع الصحابة حتى لا يتم إجماع الصحابة من خلاف التابعي، فعندنا يُعتد به وعند الشافعي له لا يعتد به. (القمر)
Section on the deeds of the Prophet, explanation of taqlid of the Companion. Shuraih said: As for the testimony of your freed slave, I have allowed it for you because he has become a freedman; but as for the testimony of your son for you, I do not allow it for you. It was the position of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that the testimony of a son for his father is permissible, but Shuraih opposed him in that, and Ali did not deny it. So Ali handed over the coat of mail to the Jew, and the Jew said: The Commander of the Faithful walked with me to his judge, and he judged against me, so I agreed: By Allah, it is truly your coat of mail. And the Jew became Muslim, and he gave the coat of mail to the Jew, and gifted him a horse, and he remained with him until he was martyred in the battle of Siffin. Likewise, Masruq, who was a Tabi'i, opposed Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with both) in the matter of the vow to slaughter a son. Ibn Abbas said: Whoever vows to slaughter his son must pay one hundred camels, by analogy to the blood-money of a life. Masruq said: No, rather he must slaughter a sheep, inferring from the ransom of Ismail (peace be upon him). So no one denied it, and it became a consensus. It is narrated from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him): I do not make taqlid of the Tabi'i, because they are men and we are men. For the statement of the Companion is accepted only due to the probability of hearing and the correctness of their opinion by the blessing of companionship of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and this is absent in the Tabi'i. And this is the chosen view of Shams al-A'imma. All of this if his fatwa appeared in the time of the Companions unclear? And if his fatwa did not appear and he did not oppose them in opinion, he is like other imams of fatwa; his taqlid is not valid. Siffin with sad then fa, on the meter of sikkin, is a place where the war occurred between him and Mu'awiyah (may Allah be pleased with them). (al-Qamar) 'on the blood-money of a life' meaning the one killed by mistake, and in Ghurar al-Ahkam the blood-money is one thousand dinars of gold, ten thousand dirhams of silver, and one hundred camels only. (al-Qamar) 'inferring from the ransom of Ismail (peace be upon him)': For when Ibrahim (peace be upon him) was commanded to slaughter his son, and he prepared for it, and threw the son on the ground, and took the knife in his hand and passed it over his neck, Jibril (peace be upon him) came with the ram as ransom, and its story is in the glorious Quran. (al-Qamar) 'so no one denied it' until Abbas when he was informed of this statement said: And I see the same. (al-Qamar) 'And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him)': This is a narration of Zahir al-Riwayah, and what is mentioned in the text is a narration of Nawadir. (al-Qamar) 'I do not make taqlid' etc. And in another narration from him: When the Companions gather, we submit to them; when the Tabi'un come, we vie against them. So it is in al-Taqrir. I say: If this is correct, it indicates that the gathering of the Companions necessitates action and no regard is given to the Tabi'un in their presence. (al-Sunbuli) And this is the chosen view of Shams al-A'imma. Imam al-Sarakhsi mentioned that there is no dispute that qiyas is not abandoned for the statement of a Tabi'i; rather the dispute is whether the Tabi'i is counted in the consensus of the Companions such that the consensus of the Companions is not complete due to the opposition of the Tabi'i. According to us, he is counted; according to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), he is not counted. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 621

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul discussion on the authority of the Tabi'i (successor) in relation to the Companions. It begins with two historical examples showing that when a Tabi'i opposed a Companion, the Companion did not reject the Tabi'i's ijtihad, yet the ruling of the Companion was upheld. The first story involves Shuraih (a judge) and Ali (RA): Ali allowed a son's testimony for his father, but Shuraih did not follow that and Ali accepted it. The second story involves Masruq (a Tabi'i) and Ibn Abbas (RA): Ibn Abbas ruled that a vow to sacrifice a son requires one hundred camels as blood-money, while Masruq ruled a sheep as ransom for Ismail. No Companion rejected Masruq's view, and Ibn Abbas later agreed. The author then presents Abu Hanifa's explicit ruling: 'I do not make taqlid of the Tabi'i' because the Tabi'i lacks the direct companionship of the Prophet and thus the presumption of correct understanding. However, the text clarifies that this applies only when the Tabi'i's fatwa appeared in the time of the Companions and opposed them. If the Tabi'i's fatwa did not appear or did not oppose them, his view is like that of other imams and taqlid of him is not valid either (since taqlid is generally not allowed for non-mujtahids in Hanafi usul). The commentary then notes that the ruling reported in the matn is from Nawadir (rare transmissions), while the Zahir al-Riwayah (core books) says the Tabi'i is counted in consensus such that his opposition prevents the completion of ijma of the Companions. The author sides with Shams al-A'imma (the preferred view) that the Tabi'i is considered in ijma, contrary to al-Shafi'i who does not count him. This dispute has practical implications: if all Companions agree on a ruling but a single Tabi'i opposes, according to the Hanafi view, the ijma is not established; according to al-Shafi'i, it is. The passage emphasizes that the Tabi'i's opinion does not overturn qiyas (analogy) established by the Companions.

Key Terms
تابعي (tabi'i): A Muslim who met the Companions but did not meet the Prophet (peace be upon him) directly.
تقليد (taqlid): Following the opinion of another without evidence; in this context, accepting the fatwa of a Tabi'i as binding.
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the mujtahids of a particular age on a legal ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in this passage, what is the effect of a Tabi'i's opposition on the consensus (ijma) of the Companions?
A) It does not affect the consensus; ijma is still established.
B) It prevents the consensus from being complete; ijma is not established.
C) The Tabi'i's view becomes part of the consensus.
D) The Tabi'i's view is adopted over the Companions' view.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the Tabi'i's ijtihad is valid and counted in consensus, but his opinion does not override a Companion's; taqlid of a Tabi'i is impermissible when it contradicts a Companion.
